# Tesbo Test Manager — Feature Documentation & Testing Roadmap Reference

> Generated by reading the actual backend (`Tesbo-Backend-Nest`) and frontend (`Tesbo-Frontend`)
> source directly — routes, service methods, DB migrations, and UI components — not from
> assumptions. Every feature entry follows the same structure: **what it is**, **use cases**,
> **problem it solves**, an exhaustive **features & actions** list, and **key files** for
> traceability back to the code. This is meant to be the seed document for a detailed QA testing
> roadmap: the "Features & actions" bullets under each module are written at the granularity of
> individual test cases, and every section also calls out concrete **edge cases worth testing**.

## How this document is organized

Nine modules, roughly in the order a user would encounter them:

1. **Authentication, Signup, Onboarding & Workspace Management** — login/OTP, signup, first-run
   onboarding, multi-workspace, team members/roles, invitations, project access, AI provider keys.
2. **Projects, Test Suites & Test Cases** — the core repository: projects, suites (folders),
   test cases, bulk operations, CSV/XLSX import/export.
3. **Test Plans, Cycles/Runs, Executions, Scheduling & Sharing** — release-level plans, the actual
   "Test Run" execution vehicle, per-case executions, recurring scheduling, public share links,
   requirements traceability.
4. **Bugs / Defect Tracking** — bug CRUD, linking to test cases/runs, evidence/attachments,
   external-tracker references, auto-bug-filing on failed executions.
5. **Reports, Analytics, Dashboards, Activity & Notifications** — workspace/project dashboards,
   the six-tab Reports page, cross-source ticket coverage, the project activity feed.
6. **AI-Powered Test Generation & the Zyra Agent** — BYOK AI provider config, AI test-case
   generation, the Zyra chat assistant, and the Zyra autonomous task/review workflow.
7. **Knowledge Base** — hierarchical folders/documents/files, versioning, AI-memory approval,
   search, and the RAG pipeline that powers Zyra's semantic retrieval.
8. **Third-Party Integrations** — the OAuth framework, Personal Access Token auth, Jira, Linear,
   and how test cases/bugs link to external tickets.
9. **Platform Admin, Branding, Tesbo Reports, MCP Server & RAG Infrastructure** — the
   cross-tenant super-admin console, white-label branding, the (currently stubbed) automated
   test-run ingestion feature, and the MCP server that lets AI clients act on a project.

## How to read this for test-roadmap planning

Every module below was researched independently and, in the process, surfaced a large number of
**concrete, code-verified gaps** — not speculative risks, but things directly confirmed by reading
the controller/service/migration/frontend code: authorization checks that are missing, fields that
silently fail to save, buttons wired to endpoints that are empty stubs, and so on. Rather than
scatter a generic disclaimer through every section, each module documents its own gaps inline
(look for **"Edge cases / validation worth testing"**, **"CRITICAL FINDING"**, or **"Cross-Cutting
Notes"** call-outs). A consolidated, prioritized view of the highest-value findings — the ones
most worth turning into actual test cases first — is collected in the **Appendix** at the end of
this document, so the roadmap owner doesn't have to re-mine nine long sections to find them.

---

## Section A — Authentication, Signup, Onboarding & Workspace Management

Scope covered: login/session/OTP/API-token auth, self-serve and invite-based signup, first-workspace onboarding, multi-workspace switching, team members & roles, invitations, project access control, and workspace AI provider keys.

Config defaults referenced below (from `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/config/app-config.service.ts`): `OTP_EXPIRY_MINUTES=10`, `OTP_MAX_ATTEMPTS=5`, `OTP_RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MINUTES=15`, `SESSION_DAYS=30`, session cookie name `tesbo_session`, invite token TTL is hardcoded at 7 days (not env-configurable).

---

### Authentication & Login

**What it is:** Email/password and passwordless one-time-code (OTP) sign-in, backed by an opaque, DB-resolved session cookie (no JWT). A secondary bearer-token path lets machine clients (e.g. an MCP server) authenticate without a browser session.

**Use cases:**
- A returning user with a password signs in quickly from `/login`.
- A user who forgot their password, or an invited user with no password set, signs in with a one-time emailed code instead.
- Automation/integrations (e.g. Tesbo MCP) call the REST API using a per-project API token instead of a cookie.
- Any page/API call needs to resolve "who is the current user" and "are they a platform super-admin."

**Problem it solves:** Provides a low-friction, secure entry point to the product without requiring a JWT/OAuth stack, while still supporting machine-to-machine calls.

**Features & actions:**
- **Password login** — `POST /api/auth/password/login` (`AuthService.loginWithPassword`)
  - Requires both `email` and `password`; 400 if either missing.
  - Verifies via `PasswordService.verifyLogin`: PBKDF2-SHA256, 210,000 iterations, per-user random 16-byte salt, stored as `pbkdf2_sha256$<iterations>$<salt>$<hash>`; constant-time compare (`timingSafeEqual`).
  - 401 `invalid_email_or_password` for unknown email, wrong password, or a user with no `password_hash` set (OTP-only accounts cannot password-login).
  - On success: creates a session row, sets `tesbo_session` cookie (httpOnly, `sameSite=lax`, `secure` when request is HTTPS or `FRONTEND_URL` is https, `maxAge = SESSION_DAYS*86400s`), writes an audit log entry (`action="login"`).
- **OTP request** — `POST /api/auth/otp/request` (204 no body) (`AuthService.requestOtp` → `OtpService.requestOtp`)
  - Requires `email`; 400 if missing.
  - Generates a 6-digit numeric code (`randomInt(0,1_000_000)` zero-padded), hashes with SHA-256/base64url, stores in `otp_codes` with an expiry (`OTP_EXPIRY_MINUTES`).
  - Rate-limited per email AND per source IP independently (`otp_rate_limit` table): after `OTP_MAX_ATTEMPTS` (default 5) request/verify attempts within `OTP_RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW_MINUTES` (default 15), further attempts return 429 `rate_limited_or_invalid` until the lock window passes. A successful verify clears the rate-limit counters for both keys.
  - Email delivery: real send via Postmark when `POSTMARK_API_TOKEN` is configured; otherwise the code is `console.log`'d (dev/test fallback) — delivery failures raise 503 `otp_delivery_failed`.
  - Emits audit log `otp_requested`.
- **OTP verify (login)** — `POST /api/auth/otp/verify` (`AuthService.verifyOtp` → `OtpService.verifyOtp`)
  - Requires `email` + `code`; 401 `invalid_or_expired_otp` for wrong/expired/already-used code.
  - Code lookup matches on `email + code_hash + not expired + not used`, most recent first; marks it used (single-use).
  - `findOrCreateUser`: if no user exists for that email, silently creates a bare account (`name` defaulted to the email's local-part, no password) — i.e., OTP login doubles as implicit account creation for a brand-new email (see Signup section for the *explicit* signup flow that also exists).
  - On success: creates session, sets cookie, audit-logs `login`.
- **Logout** — `POST /api/auth/logout` (204) (`AuthService.logout`)
  - Deletes the session row (`DELETE FROM sessions WHERE token_hash = ...`) and clears the cookie (maxAge 0) — effectively device-scoped logout (does not revoke other sessions/devices for the same user).
  - Audit-logs `logout` when `req.userId` was resolved.
- **Current user** — `GET /api/auth/me` (`AuthService.me`)
  - 401 if no valid session/token. Returns `{ userId, isPlatformAdmin, email, name }`. `isPlatformAdmin` is a platform-wide super-admin flag (distinct from any workspace role), resolved via `SuperAdminService`.
- **Session resolution middleware** (`AuthMiddleware`, applied to every route via `consumer.apply(AuthMiddleware).forRoutes("*")`):
  1. Primary: reads `tesbo_session` cookie, resolves to a `userId` via `sessions.token_hash` lookup (only if `expires_at > now()`); expired/unknown token → `req.userId = null` (not an error — downstream handlers 401/403 as needed).
  2. Secondary (only if no cookie session resolved): parses `Authorization: Bearer <token>`, authenticates against `api_tokens.token_hash` (SHA-256) via `ApiTokenService.authenticate`; on match sets `req.userId` to the token's owning user and `req.apiToken = { tokenId, userId, projectId, scopes }`. Unknown/blank bearer token → falls through as unauthenticated.
  - Practical effect: a request bearing *both* a valid session cookie and a bearer token is treated as the cookie user (cookie wins).
- **API token (project-scoped machine credential)** — backend-only today (`ApiTokenService`, routes `GET/POST /api/projects/:id/apikeys`, `DELETE /api/projects/:id/apikeys/:keyId`); no frontend UI currently calls these (`lib/api.ts` has no wrapper — confirmed by repo-wide search). Documented here for API-level test coverage:
  - Token format: `tsbo_` prefix + 24 random bytes hex; only a SHA-256 hex hash is ever persisted; raw token is returned exactly once, at creation, and is unrecoverable afterward.
  - Scopes: `read`, `write` (comma-stored); invalid/unrecognized scope strings are filtered out; if nothing valid remains, defaults to **both** `read` and `write`.
  - Create requires `name`; 400 if blank. Requires the caller to be a project member (`requireProjectAccess`) of their currently-active workspace's project.
  - List returns a masked summary (`tsbo_…<last 6 hex chars>`), never the raw token, plus `lastUsedAt`/`createdAt`.
  - Revoke scoped to `(id, projectId)` — 404 if the token doesn't belong to that project.
  - Successful bearer-auth updates `last_used_at` best-effort (failure to update doesn't block the request).
- **Initial platform setup (edge case, tangential)** — `GET /api/setup/status`, `POST /api/setup/first-admin`. The login page (`app/login/page.tsx`) checks `getSetupStatus()` on mount and redirects to `/setup` when `required: true` (fresh install with zero platform admins), and `/setup` itself redirects back to `/login` once setup is no longer required. Bootstraps the first admin (email/password), an initial organization, and optional demo data (`app/setup/page.tsx`).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.controller.ts`, `auth.service.ts`, `otp.service.ts`, `password.service.ts`, `email.service.ts`, `api-token.service.ts`, `auth.middleware.ts`, `auth.module.ts`
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/login/page.tsx`, `app/verify-otp/page.tsx`, `components/auth/AuthModeToggle.tsx`, `components/auth/AuthSplitShell.tsx`, `components/auth/OtpBoxInput.tsx`, `lib/api.ts` (`loginWithPassword`, `requestOtp`, `verifyOtp`, `authMe`, `getSetupStatus`, `createFirstAdmin`)

---

### Signup

**What it is:** An explicit self-serve account-creation flow (separate from OTP-login's implicit bare-account creation) with two modes — Password+OTP-verification, and OTP-only — built on a `pending_signups` staging table so nothing is written to `users` until the email is verified.

**Use cases:**
- A brand-new user creates an account with a name, email, and password, then confirms via a 6-digit emailed code before the account actually exists.
- A user who prefers not to set a password signs up with just email + OTP.
- Both modes also apply to invite-based registration (see Invitations section) — an invited user can create their account either way before joining the inviting workspace.

**Problem it solves:** Ensures email ownership is verified before an account/password is durably created, and gives new users a real "Sign Up" entry point instead of overloading OTP-login for account creation.

**Features & actions:**
- **Self-serve start** — `POST /api/auth/signup/start` (204) (`SignupService.startSelfServeSignup`)
  - Validates: email format (regex), non-empty name, password ≥ 8 characters.
  - 400 `An account with this email already exists...` if `users.email` already taken.
  - Hashes password immediately (PBKDF2 via `PasswordService`) and stores name/hash/expiry in `pending_signups` (no `users` row yet).
  - Sends OTP to the email; 503 `otp_delivery_failed` if the mail send throws, 400 `rate_limited_or_invalid` if OTP request itself was rate-limited.
  - Audit-logs `signup_started`.
- **Self-serve verify** — `POST /api/auth/signup/verify` (`SignupService.verifySelfServeSignup`)
  - Requires `email` + `code`; validates email format again.
  - 401 `invalid_or_expired_otp` on bad code (via shared `OtpService.verifyOtpCode`).
  - 400 `No pending signup found...` if no unconsumed, unexpired `pending_signups` row matches (e.g., signup never started, expired, or already consumed).
  - On success: creates the real `users` row (with the pre-hashed password), marks the pending row consumed, calls `AuthService.signInUser` directly (server sets the session cookie — no separate login call needed), audit-logs `signup_completed`.
  - Race-condition guard: a duplicate email insert at this final step surfaces as 409 Conflict rather than a raw DB error.
- **OTP-only self-serve signup** — reuses the plain login OTP endpoints (`/api/auth/otp/request` + `/api/auth/otp/verify`); no dedicated signup-otp backend route exists. `findOrCreateUser` silently creates the account on first verify (name = email prefix, no password). This means the "OTP mode" tab on `/signup` is functionally identical to OTP login for a new email.
- **Frontend signup page (`/signup`)**:
  - Segmented Password/Email-code mode toggle (styled tab pair, no shared Tabs primitive).
  - Password mode: First name + Last name (both required, concatenated into one `name` field), work email, password (client-side min length 8), then a 6-digit code entry step with a "Back" affordance to re-edit the form.
  - Email-code mode: just an email field; submitting requests an OTP and routes to `/verify-otp?email=...&redirect=/onboarding`.
  - Links to Terms/Privacy Policy; link back to `/login` for existing users.
  - Successful verification routes to `/onboarding`.

**Edge cases worth testing:**
- Password < 8 chars → rejected client-side and server-side.
- Signing up twice with the same email before verifying (second `start` call): allowed to create another pending row (no uniqueness constraint visible on `pending_signups.email` besides the query picking most-recent); only the newest unconsumed pending row is matched at verify time.
- Expired pending signup (past `expires_at`, tied to `OTP_EXPIRY_MINUTES`) → verify fails with "No pending signup found... Please start again," even with a correct OTP code — must restart from `start`.
- OTP delivery failure (Postmark misconfigured/rejects) → 503, not silently swallowed.
- Duplicate account race (two concurrent verifies for the same email) → second one gets 409, not a 500.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/signup.controller.ts`, `signup.service.ts` (deliberately in `src/legacy/`, not `src/auth/`, to avoid a circular import with `LegacyService`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/signup/page.tsx`, `app/verify-otp/page.tsx`, `components/auth/OtpBoxInput.tsx`, `lib/api.ts` (`startSignup`, `verifySignup`)

---

### Onboarding

**What it is:** The two-step guided flow a brand-new (workspace-less) user goes through immediately after first authenticating: create their workspace (becoming its Owner), then optionally add teammates before landing on `/projects`.

**Use cases:**
- A first-time signee with zero organization memberships needs somewhere to land instead of a broken/empty `/projects` page.
- An org owner wants to seed initial teammates right at setup time instead of navigating to Settings afterward.

**Problem it solves:** Guarantees every authenticated user resolves to at least one workspace before reaching the main app, and reduces friction for populating a first team.

**Features & actions:**
- **Access guard** (`app/onboarding/page.tsx`): on mount, calls `authMe()` — redirects to `/login` if not authenticated; then calls `getWorkspace()` — if it *succeeds* (user already has a workspace), redirects straight to `/projects` (onboarding is skipped/one-time only, not re-enterable once a workspace exists).
- **Step 1 — Create workspace** — `POST /api/onboarding/workspace` (`LegacyService.createWorkspace`)
  - Requires `orgName` (or `name`); 400 if blank/whitespace-only.
  - Transactionally: inserts `organizations` row (slugified name), inserts caller into `organization_members` with role `owner`, sets `users.active_organization_id` to the new org.
  - No workspace-name uniqueness constraint enforced — duplicate workspace names across the platform are allowed.
- **Step 2 — Invite team (optional)**: a free-text textarea for teammate emails, one per line or comma/semicolon-separated; de-duplicated client-side (`Set`). For each email, calls `addWorkspaceMember({ email, role: "qa_engineer" })` — **not** the invitation flow.
  - **Important distinction / test focus:** this direct-add path (`POST /api/workspace/members`, `LegacyService.addWorkspaceMember`) is fundamentally different from the "Invite member" flow on the Members tab:
    - No email is sent — the person is added silently and immediately (no acceptance step, no token).
    - The target user is created via `upsertUser` if they don't already exist (bare account: email-prefix as name, **no password set** — they can only ever sign in via OTP unless they later set a password some other way).
    - **No role-based permission check at all** in `addWorkspaceMember` (unlike `createInvitation`, which forbids QA Engineers from inviting and restricts Managers to QA-Engineer-only invites). Any authenticated member of a workspace — including a QA Engineer — can call `POST /api/workspace/members` directly.
    - **No role-string validation/normalization** — `body.role` is used almost as-is (`String(body.role || "member")`) and written straight into `organization_members.role` via `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (organization_id, user_id) DO UPDATE SET role = EXCLUDED.role`. Because it's an upsert, calling this with the caller's **own email** and `role: "owner"` updates the caller's *own* membership row — a potential self-privilege-escalation path worth a dedicated security test (a QA Engineer promoting themselves to Owner, or silently adding an arbitrary external email as Owner of the workspace).
  - "Skip for now" button bypasses step 2 entirely.
  - Both paths finish by routing to `/projects?create=1&fromOnboarding=1` (triggers the "create your first project" affordance on the Projects page).
- **`POST /api/onboarding/org-and-project`** (`createOrgAndProject`) — creates an org + a project + owner membership on both, in one transaction, and sets `users.default_project_id`. **Confirmed dead from the frontend**: `lib/api.ts` exposes a wrapper but no page/component calls it — worth flagging as either legacy/unused or a not-yet-wired alternate onboarding path; still reachable and testable via direct API call.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`POST /api/onboarding/workspace`, `POST /api/onboarding/org-and-project`), `legacy.service.ts` (`createWorkspace`, `createOrgAndProject`, `addWorkspaceMember`, `upsertUser`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/onboarding/page.tsx`

---

### Workspace Management

**What it is:** The single-active-organization model each user has: every user always has exactly one "active" workspace (`users.active_organization_id`) that scopes almost every workspace-level and project-level API call.

**Use cases:**
- Any authenticated page needs to know "which org am I currently working in."
- A workspace owner/manager views aggregate stats about their org's testing activity (Dashboard).

**Problem it solves:** Gives a single, server-side choke point (`workspace(userId)`) for resolving/enforcing the current org context, avoiding a client-controlled org-id-in-URL pattern that would need per-endpoint IDOR checks.

**Features & actions:**
- **Get active workspace** — `GET /api/workspace` (`LegacyService.workspace`)
  - Resolves `users.active_organization_id` joined against `organization_members`/`organizations`.
  - **Self-healing fallback:** if `active_organization_id` is unset or stale (e.g., user was removed from that org since it was set), falls back to the user's *earliest* membership (`ORDER BY created_at ASC LIMIT 1`) and persists that as the new active org (best-effort; still returns the resolved workspace even if the persist write fails).
  - 404 `Workspace not found` if the user belongs to zero organizations (this is exactly the condition the Onboarding guard relies on).
  - 400 `Authentication required` if called with no authenticated user.
- **Workspace analytics** — `GET /api/workspace/analytics` (`workspaceAnalytics` → `LegacyService.analytics`)
  - Aggregate counts scoped to the active org: project count, active test-case count, suite count, plan count, cycle count, and a breakdown of execution statuses + total executions. Powers the workspace Dashboard page.
- **Update project (basic)** — `PATCH /api/projects/:id`, **Delete project** — `DELETE /api/projects/:id` (soft-delete via `archived_at`), **Create project** — `POST /api/projects`, **List my projects** — `GET /api/projects`: all scoped through `requireUser` + the active workspace; `listProjects` further requires the caller to be a `project_members` row on that project. (Full CRUD detail for Projects itself is out of this section's scope — noted here only because project creation participates in onboarding/workspace flows.)

**Edge cases worth testing:**
- User removed from their active org by an Owner while they still have a valid session — next `workspace()` call should self-heal to another membership (or 404 if none left), not silently 500 or leak the old org's data.
- Zero-membership user (e.g., after leaving their only org) hitting any workspace-scoped page should be redirected/guarded gracefully, not crash.
- Concurrent workspace-name collisions are allowed (no uniqueness constraint on org name/slug uniqueness wasn't verified beyond `slugify`).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`GET /api/workspace`, `GET /api/workspace/analytics`), `legacy.service.ts` (`workspace`, `analytics`, `requireProjectAccess`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/dashboard/page.tsx` (analytics consumer), `lib/api.ts` (`getWorkspace`, `getWorkspaceAnalytics`)

---

### Multi-Workspace Support

**What it is:** Full many-to-many user↔organization membership with an explicit "active workspace" switcher — a user can belong to multiple workspaces (with a different role in each) and change which one is active without re-authenticating.

**Use cases:**
- A consultant/QA engineer works across multiple client workspaces under one account.
- A user creates a second workspace for a different team/product line without needing a separate account.
- Switching workspace should immediately re-scope Settings, Members, Invitations, AI keys, etc. to the newly active org.

**Problem it solves:** Removes the old one-workspace-per-account-forever limitation (previously `workspace(userId)` always resolved the earliest-created org).

**Features & actions:**
- **List my workspaces** — `GET /api/workspaces` (`LegacyService.listWorkspaces`) — every org the user belongs to, each with their role in it and an `isActive` flag; ordered by org creation date. Empty array for a user with zero orgs (does not throw, unlike `workspace()`).
- **Create an additional workspace** — `POST /api/workspaces` (reuses `createWorkspace`) — same validation as onboarding's create-workspace step (non-blank `orgName`); also switches `active_organization_id` to the new org immediately.
- **Switch active workspace** — `POST /api/workspaces/:id/switch` (`LegacyService.switchWorkspace`)
  - 403 `You are not a member of this workspace` if the caller isn't an `organization_members` row for that org id (prevents switching into a workspace you don't belong to by guessing/enumerating ids).
  - On success, updates `active_organization_id` and returns the freshly resolved workspace.
- **Role varies per workspace:** the same user can be `owner` in one org and `qa_engineer` in another; `workspace()`/`workspaceMembers()` always reflect the role in the *currently active* org, not some global role.
- **WorkspaceSwitcher UI** (`components/WorkspaceSwitcher.tsx`, docked at the top of the sidebar, below the logo):
  - Shows active workspace's first-letter avatar, name, and role label; collapses to just the avatar when the sidebar is collapsed.
  - Dropdown lists every workspace the user belongs to with role label and a checkmark on the currently active one; clicking a non-active entry calls switch and does a **hard navigation** (`window.location.href = "/projects"`) rather than a client-side route change — deliberate, since most pages fetch data client-side on mount and wouldn't otherwise re-fetch for the new org.
  - Clicking the already-active workspace just closes the menu (no-op switch).
  - "Create new workspace" row opens a modal (single "Organization / workspace name" field) that creates + hard-navigates to `/projects`.
  - Silently renders nothing if `listWorkspaces()` fails or returns empty (e.g., not yet onboarded) — no error state shown in that case.
- **Known scoping gap (flagged in prior session, still true as of this read):** `listProjects(userId)` **is** now correctly scoped to `organization_id = activeOrgId` in the current code (`Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` line ~1108–1122 joins `p.organization_id = $2` against the active workspace) — this appears to have been fixed since the prior memory note was written; worth a regression test confirming switching workspace changes the visible project list, since the memory explicitly called this out as previously broken.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`GET/POST /api/workspaces`, `POST /api/workspaces/:id/switch`), `legacy.service.ts` (`listWorkspaces`, `switchWorkspace`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/WorkspaceSwitcher.tsx`, `components/Sidebar.tsx` (mounts the switcher), `lib/api.ts` (`listWorkspaces`, `switchWorkspace`, `createAdditionalWorkspace`)

---

### Team Members & Roles

**What it is:** Workspace-scoped membership list with a fixed 3-role model (Owner / Manager / QA Engineer), role changes, and removal — surfaced through a single "Members" tab in Workspace Settings.

**Use cases:**
- An Owner reviews who's on the team, promotes/demotes a Manager ↔ QA Engineer, or removes someone who left.
- A Manager checks who else is on the team but has restricted invite/manage rights.

**Problem it solves:** Central place to see and govern workspace access with least-privilege role separation.

**Role model (`normalizeRole`, duplicated in backend `legacy.service.ts` and frontend `MembersTab.tsx`/project settings page):**
| Canonical role | Recognized aliases folded into it |
|---|---|
| `owner` | — |
| `manager` | `manager`, `admin`, `test_manager` |
| `qa_engineer` | anything else (fallback) |

**Features & actions:**
- **List members** — `GET /api/workspace/members` (`workspaceMembers`) — id, email, name, role, `joinedAt`, ordered by email; scoped to the active workspace.
- **Direct-add member** — `POST /api/workspace/members` (`addWorkspaceMember`) — see the Onboarding section above for the detailed, security-relevant caveats (no permission check, no role validation, silent account creation, no email sent). Only reachable today from the onboarding "invite your team" step in the UI, but callable directly via API by any authenticated user.
- **Remove member** — `DELETE /api/workspace/members/:userId` (`removeWorkspaceMember`)
  - Only an Owner may remove members (`callerRole !== "owner"` → 403 `Only the owner can remove team members`) — Managers cannot remove anyone, confirmed by `multi-workspace.spec.ts`.
  - Cannot remove yourself (400 `You cannot remove yourself`) — no self-service "leave workspace" exists via this endpoint.
  - 404 if the target isn't a member of the workspace.
  - **Last-owner protection:** removing an `owner` is blocked with 400 `Cannot remove the last owner` when it's the sole owner; allowed when ≥2 owners exist.
- **Change member role** — `POST /api/workspace/members/role` (`changeWorkspaceMemberRole`)
  - Only an Owner may change roles (403 otherwise).
  - Cannot change your own role, even as Owner (400 `You cannot change your own role`).
  - Cannot change another Owner's role (403 `Owner role cannot be changed`) — ownership transfer is out of scope entirely.
  - Cannot promote anyone to Owner through this endpoint (403 `Cannot promote to owner`) — Owner role is only ever set at workspace-creation time.
  - 404 if the target isn't a member.
  - Valid transitions in practice: Manager ↔ QA Engineer only.
- **Members tab UI (`components/settings/MembersTab.tsx`)**:
  - Members table: Name, Email, Role, Joined date, Actions.
  - Role cell renders as an inline `<select>` (Manager/QA Engineer) only when `canChangeRole` (caller is Owner, target isn't self, target isn't Owner) — otherwise a static role badge.
  - Remove button (icon-only, `IconUserMinus`) shown only when `canRemove` (caller is Owner, target isn't self, target isn't Owner).
  - "(you)" suffix next to the caller's own name in the table.
  - "Invite member" button visible only to Owner/Manager (`canManage`).
  - Toast notifications ("Role updated", "Team member removed", "Invitation resent/cancelled", "Invite sent successfully") auto-dismiss after 3.5s.
  - Role-badge color coding: Owner (blue), Manager (orange), QA Engineer (grey); status badges for invites: active/pending/expired/cancelled each with distinct colors.
  - A static "Role guide" card at the bottom explains what each of the 3 roles can do.
  - Access to the whole Members tab (and Settings generally) is gated: only workspace Owner/Manager or a platform admin can view `/settings`; everyone else is redirected to `/projects` (`app/(app)/settings/page.tsx`).
  - Old standalone routes `/settings/members` and `/settings/project-access` are now thin client-side redirects into `/settings?tab=members` (kept for old links/bookmarks).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`GET/POST /api/workspace/members`, `DELETE /api/workspace/members/:userId`, `POST /api/workspace/members/role`), `legacy.service.ts` (`workspaceMembers`, `addWorkspaceMember`, `removeWorkspaceMember`, `changeWorkspaceMemberRole`, `normalizeRole`, `upsertUser`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/settings/MembersTab.tsx`, `app/(app)/settings/page.tsx`, `app/(app)/settings/members/page.tsx` (redirect stub), `lib/api.ts` (`listWorkspaceMembers`, `removeWorkspaceMember`, `changeWorkspaceMemberRole`, `addWorkspaceMember`)
- Tests confirming behavior: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/multi-workspace.spec.ts` (`removeWorkspaceMember`, `changeWorkspaceMemberRole` describe blocks)

---

### Invitations

**What it is:** A hashed-token, email-delivered invite workflow for adding people to a workspace (optionally pre-scoped to specific projects), with a full status lifecycle and role-based sending restrictions — this is the "proper" onboarding path for new teammates, as opposed to the onboarding-page direct-add shortcut.

**Use cases:**
- An Owner invites a new Manager or QA Engineer by email, optionally pre-assigning them to one or more projects.
- A Manager invites additional QA Engineers to projects they run.
- An invited person clicks the emailed link and either signs in (existing account) or creates an account (new user), landing inside the workspace.
- An Owner/Manager needs to resend a lost invite email or cancel one sent by mistake.

**Problem it solves:** Verifiable, auditable, role-gated team growth with an explicit accept step (vs. silently creating memberships).

**Features & actions:**
- **Create invitation** — `POST /api/workspace/invitations` (`createInvitation`)
  - Requires `email` (validated by regex) and optional `role` (defaults `qa_engineer`, normalized) and optional `projectIds[]`.
  - **Permission checks:**
    - QA Engineers cannot invite anyone → 403.
    - Nobody can invite an Owner directly → 403 `Cannot invite owners directly` (ownership transfer isn't supported anywhere).
    - Managers may only invite QA Engineers → 403 if a Manager tries to invite a Manager (or attempts Owner, already covered above).
    - Owners may invite Manager or QA Engineer.
  - 400 if the email already belongs to an existing org member (`This user is already a team member`).
  - 400 if a **pending** invite already exists for that email in this org (`This email already has a pending invite. You can resend the invite.` — response includes the existing `inviteId` so the UI could offer a direct resend, though the current UI doesn't wire this up automatically).
  - `projectIds` are validated to belong to the same organization and not be archived — 400 `One or more project IDs are invalid` if any don't match.
  - Token: `randomBytes(32).toString("hex")` (64-char raw token) shown only in the email link; **SHA-256 hex hash** is what's stored in `invitations.token`. Expiry fixed at **7 days** from creation.
  - Sends the invite email (Postmark, or console-logged fallback) with inviter name, role label, workspace name, and any pre-assigned project names.
- **List invitations** — `GET /api/workspace/invitations` (`listInvitations`)
  - Auto-expires any pending invite whose `expires_at` has passed *before* returning the list (lazy expiry, not a cron).
  - Returns only `pending`/`expired` statuses (accepted/cancelled invites drop off this list entirely — no "history" view exists), each with inviter name/email and resolved project names.
- **Cancel invitation** — `DELETE /api/workspace/invitations/:id` (`cancelInvitation`)
  - 404 if not found in the caller's workspace.
  - 400 if the invite isn't currently `pending` (can't cancel an already-accepted/expired/cancelled invite).
  - Owner can cancel any invite; a Manager can only cancel invites **they personally sent** (403 otherwise) — enforced by comparing `invited_by` to the caller.
- **Resend invitation** — `POST /api/workspace/invitations/:id/resend` (`resendInvitation`)
  - Same not-pending / not-your-invite restrictions as cancel.
  - **Rotates the token** (old link becomes invalid) and **extends expiry** another 7 days from now, then re-sends the email.
- **Get invitation by token (public, unauthenticated)** — `GET /api/invitations/:token` (`getInvitationByToken`)
  - 404 for an unknown token hash.
  - Auto-expires (updates DB) if past expiry and still marked pending, then reflects `expired` in the response.
  - Returns org name, email, role, status, expiry, accepted-at, assigned project names, and a `hasAccount` boolean (whether the invited email already has a password-bearing account) — this flag is what the frontend uses to branch between "Sign in to accept" vs. "Create account."
- **Accept invitation (existing logged-in user)** — `POST /api/invitations/:token/accept` (`acceptInvitation`)
  - Requires an authenticated caller.
  - Rejects `cancelled` (400), `accepted` (400 — already used), and `expired` (400, including a lazy re-check against `expires_at` even if the DB status hasn't been flipped yet) invites.
  - **Email match enforcement:** the logged-in user's account email must case-insensitively match the invited email, else 403 `You must sign in with the invited email address to accept this invite` — prevents accepting someone else's invite while signed in as yourself.
  - On success: upserts `organization_members` (role = invited role; `ON CONFLICT` updates role if somehow already a member), upserts `project_members` for every pre-assigned project, marks the invite `accepted`, and **switches the user's active workspace** to the org they just joined.
- **Register from invitation (legacy, immediate, no OTP)** — `POST /api/invitations/:token/register` (`registerFromInvitation`) — kept for backward compatibility.
  - Requires `name` and `password` (≥8 chars); re-validates the token isn't taken (`existingUser` check) even though `getInvitationRowOrThrow` already gated status/expiry.
  - Creates the user + org/project memberships **immediately**, no email/OTP verification step — this is the older, superseded path; the current UI instead drives the OTP-gated flows below.
- **Register from invitation — Password+OTP** — `POST /api/invitations/:token/register/start` (204) then `POST /api/invitations/:token/register/verify` (`SignupService.startInviteRegistration` / `verifyInviteRegistration`)
  - `start`: validates invite (via `getInvitationRowOrThrow` — 404/400 for bad/consumed/expired token), validates name + password, 400 if the invited email already has an account (tells the user to sign in instead), stores a `pending_signups` row tied to `invitation_id`, sends OTP.
  - `verify`: validates the OTP, looks up the matching pending signup (400 if none/expired — "Please start again"), then transactionally creates the user, org membership (invited role), per-invite project memberships, marks invite accepted and pending-signup consumed, sets `active_organization_id`, and signs the user in directly (session cookie set server-side — no separate login call needed since OTP-only has no password to log in with afterward).
- **Register from invitation — OTP-only** — `POST /api/invitations/:token/register/otp/start` / `.../otp/verify` (`startInviteOtpRegistration` / `verifyInviteOtpRegistration`)
  - Same as above but no password captured/hashed at all (`password_hash = null`); the resulting account can only ever sign in via OTP.
  - Both invite-verify paths funnel through the same shared `completeInviteVerification` helper.
- **Invite acceptance page (`/invite/[token]`)** — branches on invite status:
  - `invalid` (token not found / never existed) — generic "contact the person who invited you" message.
  - `expired` — tells them to ask the sender to resend from the Team management page.
  - `cancelled` — tells them to contact the workspace owner.
  - `accepted` (already used) — "Sign in" CTA only.
  - `valid` + not logged in + `hasAccount=true` → "Sign in to accept" (pre-fills/locks email on the login page via `?inviteEmail=`).
  - `valid` + not logged in + `hasAccount=false` → "Create account" CTA to `/invite/[token]/register`, plus a "Already have an account? Sign in" link.
  - `valid` + logged in with a **different** email → explicit mismatch warning + "Sign in with {invited email}" CTA (does not silently let them proceed).
  - `valid` + logged in with matching email → "Accept and join workspace" button, routes to `/projects` on success.
- **Invite registration page (`/invite/[token]/register`)**:
  - Redirects straight to `/invite/[token]` if the invite already `hasAccount` (avoids duplicate-account attempts).
  - `invalid`/non-pending invite → "Invitation unavailable" card with a link back to sign-in.
  - Password/Email-code segmented mode toggle (mirrors `/signup`).
  - Password mode: Full name, read-only email (pre-filled, disabled, "Set by the invite — cannot be changed"), password, confirm-password (client-side match check), then a numeric 6-digit code step.
  - Email-code mode: Full name + read-only email only, then the same code step.
  - Both modes' code step has a "Back" link to re-edit the form (goes back to `start`, not a resend of the same pending code).
  - "Already have an account? Sign in" link at the bottom (carries the invite token/email through to login).
- **Login-page invite-lock behavior:** when arriving via `?inviteEmail=...`, the login page locks the email field (read-only) and forces OTP mode (password mode isn't offered) — since the point is just to re-authenticate as the invited email before accepting.

**Edge cases worth testing:**
- Expired invite auto-flips to `expired` on read (`getInvitationByToken`) even if a background job never ran.
- Resending an invite invalidates the old link (token rotated) — old link should show "invalid"/404-equivalent behavior after a resend, not silently still work.
- A Manager attempting to cancel/resend an invite sent by a *different* Manager → 403.
- Accepting while logged in under the wrong email → explicit mismatch UI, not a silent failure.
- Registering (password or OTP path) when the invited email gained an account through some other path in between `start` and `verify` — should be caught (email-taken checks happen at `start`, but a duplicate-insert race at `verify`/user-creation time still needs the 409 Conflict guard, confirmed present in `SignupService.insertUser`/`completeInviteRegistration`... note `completeInviteRegistration` used by `registerFromInvitation` does its own existing-user check up front but doesn't wrap the final insert in the same try/catch 409 mapping used by `SignupService.insertUser` — worth a targeted race-condition test here).
- Invite with `projectIds` referencing an archived project → rejected at creation time, not deferred to accept time.
- Duplicate pending invite to the same email → blocked with the existing invite's id surfaced, not a silent second invite.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`GET/POST /api/workspace/invitations`, `DELETE .../:id`, `POST .../:id/resend`, `GET /api/invitations/:token`, `POST /api/invitations/:token/accept`, `POST /api/invitations/:token/register`), `legacy.service.ts` (`createInvitation`, `listInvitations`, `cancelInvitation`, `resendInvitation`, `getInvitationByToken`, `acceptInvitation`, `registerFromInvitation`, `getInvitationRowOrThrow`, `hashToken`), `src/legacy/signup.controller.ts` + `signup.service.ts` (OTP-gated invite registration), `src/auth/email.service.ts` (`sendInvite`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/invite/[token]/page.tsx`, `app/invite/[token]/register/page.tsx`, `components/settings/MembersTab.tsx` (invite creation/list/cancel/resend UI), `lib/api.ts` (`createWorkspaceInvitation`, `listWorkspaceInvitations`, `cancelWorkspaceInvitation`, `resendWorkspaceInvitation`, `getInvitationByToken`, `acceptInvitation`, `startInviteRegistration`, `verifyInviteRegistration`, `startInviteOtpRegistration`, `verifyInviteOtpRegistration`, `registerFromInvitation`)
- Tests confirming behavior: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/team-invite.spec.ts`, `signup-invite.spec.ts`, `src/auth/email-invite.spec.ts`

---

### Project Access Control

**What it is:** Per-project membership (distinct from workspace membership) that determines which projects a user can see/work in and with what role inside that specific project. A workspace-level `/api/workspace/project-access` endpoint also exists but is **not wired into any current frontend UI**.

**Use cases:**
- An Owner/Manager assigns a subset of workspace members to a specific project (rather than giving everyone access to every project).
- A user with multiple projects in a workspace needs their per-project role (which can legitimately differ from their workspace role, though in practice the UI always sends the same 3-role set).

**Problem it solves:** Fine-grained, project-scoped authorization layered on top of workspace membership.

**Features & actions (actively used, via the Project Settings → Team Members tab):**
- **List project members** — `GET /api/projects/:id/members` (`projectMembers`)
- **Add/update project member** — `POST /api/projects/:id/members` (`addProjectMember`) — requires `userId`; defaults role to `"member"` string if omitted (not normalized to the 3-role set server-side); upserts (`ON CONFLICT (project_id, user_id) DO UPDATE SET role`), so this same endpoint is reused by the UI for "change role" (re-POST with the new role).
- **Remove project member** — `DELETE /api/projects/:id/members/:userId` (`removeProjectMember`)
- **Frontend (project settings "Team Members" tab, `app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/page.tsx`):**
  - Dropdown to add any *workspace* member not already on the project, with a role selector.
  - Assignable roles depend on the caller's own project role: Owner can assign Manager or QA Engineer; Manager can only assign QA Engineer; QA Engineer sees no assign controls at all (`assignableRoles()` returns empty).
  - Change-role control per row, gated by `canChangeRole`: caller must be Owner/Manager, not acting on themselves, target isn't a project Owner, and a Manager cannot change another Manager's role (only Owner can touch Manager-level rows).
  - Remove button gated similarly (`canManageMembers && !isSelf && targetRole !== "owner"`).

- **CRITICAL FINDING — missing server-side authorization on all three project-member routes.** Reading `legacy.controller.ts` lines ~201–214 and the corresponding `legacy.service.ts` methods (`projectMembers`, `addProjectMember`, `removeProjectMember`, lines ~1206–1226): **none of these three routes accept or check `req.userId`, project membership, or role at the backend at all** — unlike almost every other project-scoped route in this file, which routes through `requireProjectAccess`/`requireUser`. Concretely:
  - `GET /api/projects/:id/members` returns the member list for **any** project id, to **any** caller (authenticated or not).
  - `POST /api/projects/:id/members` adds **any** `userId` at **any** role (including `"owner"`) to **any** `projectId`, regardless of whether the caller belongs to that project or even to that workspace.
  - `DELETE /api/projects/:id/members/:userId` removes any member from any project, no ownership/role check.
  - All frontend-enforced restrictions above (role dropdowns, "Owner only" gating, etc.) are **client-side only** for this specific resource — they can be bypassed by calling the API directly. This is a genuine broken-access-control / IDOR gap and should be a high-priority security test case (e.g., an authenticated QA Engineer, or even an unauthenticated client with a guessed/enumerated project UUID, adding themselves as Owner of an arbitrary project).
- **Workspace-level `project-access` endpoints (present in backend, unused in frontend — verify as dead code / test as an orphaned API surface):**
  - `GET /api/workspace/project-access` (`projectAccess` handler) — returns `{ projects, members }` where every member's `projectRoles` is hardcoded to `{}` (i.e., this endpoint doesn't actually return a real per-project role matrix despite the name — looks unfinished).
  - `PUT /api/workspace/project-access` (`setProjectAccess`) and `DELETE /api/workspace/project-access` (`removeProjectAccess`) — thin wrappers around the same unguarded `addProjectMember`/`removeProjectMember`, and **these two routes don't even read `req.userId`** (no `@Req()` at all in the controller signature) — meaning they inherit the exact same missing-authorization issue described above, at a URL that isn't even linked from any UI today. `lib/api.ts` does expose `getWorkspaceProjectAccess`/`setWorkspaceProjectAccess`/`removeWorkspaceProjectAccess` wrappers, but grep confirms **zero call sites** in `app/`/`components/` — the standalone `/settings/project-access` page is now just a redirect stub into `/settings?tab=members`, which doesn't use these functions either.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`GET/PUT/DELETE /api/workspace/project-access`, `GET/POST /api/projects/:id/members`, `DELETE /api/projects/:id/members/:userId`), `legacy.service.ts` (`projectMembers`, `addProjectMember`, `removeProjectMember`, `listProjects`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/page.tsx` ("Team Members" tab — the real, actively-used UI), `app/(app)/settings/project-access/page.tsx` (dead redirect stub), `lib/api.ts` (`listProjectMembers`, `addProjectMember`, `removeProjectMember`, `getWorkspaceProjectAccess`*, `setWorkspaceProjectAccess`*, `removeWorkspaceProjectAccess`* — *unused wrappers)

---

### AI Provider Keys

**What it is:** Workspace-level storage of AI provider API keys (OpenAI/Anthropic/custom-compatible), which are then allocated one-per-project so project-scoped AI features (test-case generation, script review, the "Zyra" agent, etc.) know which credential to use.

**Use cases:**
- A workspace Owner adds a company OpenAI or Anthropic key once, instead of every project needing its own.
- Different projects can be pointed at different keys (e.g., separate billing/quota per team or per client).
- A custom/self-hosted OpenAI-compatible provider (e.g., local Ollama, Groq, Together) can be configured with a custom base URL and auth header.

**Problem it solves:** Centralizes credential management and access control for AI features to the Owner role, while still letting per-project allocation vary.

**Features & actions:**
- **List keys + allocations** — `GET /api/workspace/ai-keys` (`aiKeys`)
  - Returns all `workspace_ai_keys` for the active org (id, name, provider, default model, base URL, auth header/scheme, active flag, masked key, timestamps) plus every non-archived project in the org with its currently allocated key id (if any).
  - Keys are always returned **masked** (`maskedKey`); the raw `api_key` column is stripped from the response (`delete item.apiKey`).
  - No role restriction on *viewing* — any workspace member can call this and see which projects have which key allocated (though not the raw key).
- **Create/replace a key** — `POST /api/workspace/ai-keys` (`createAiKey`)
  - **Owner-only** (403 `Only the workspace owner can manage AI keys` for anyone else).
  - Requires `name`, `apiKey`, `provider`; for non-`openai`/`anthropic` ("custom") providers, `baseUrl` is also required (400 otherwise).
  - Known providers (`openai`, `anthropic`) force `auth_header_name`/`auth_scheme` to `null` server-side even if the client sent overrides — only custom providers respect explicit header/scheme overrides (defends against the SDK's built-in auth being silently broken by a stray custom header).
  - Upsert semantics: `ON CONFLICT (organization_id, name) DO UPDATE` — creating a key with a name that already exists **replaces** the existing key's provider/api_key/model/etc. in place (re-activates it too, `is_active = true`) rather than erroring — worth an explicit test ("adding a key with a duplicate name silently overwrites the old one").
- **Delete a key** — `DELETE /api/workspace/ai-keys/:keyId` (`deleteAiKey`) — Owner-only; scoped to the active org (won't delete another org's key even if the id is guessed, since it filters on `organization_id`).
- **Allocate a key to a project** — `POST /api/workspace/ai-keys/allocations` (`allocateAiKey`)
  - Owner-only.
  - Requires `projectId`; 404 if that project isn't in the caller's active org.
  - `workspaceAiKeyId` is optional — omitting/clearing it (`null`) explicitly **un-allocates** the project (no AI key). Passing an id that doesn't belong to the org → 404 `AI key not found`.
  - Upsert on `project_ai_key_allocations (project_id)` — one allocation per project, always overwritten.
- **Downstream effect on AI features:** `zyraAiAllocation()` resolves, for a given project, the allocated key; if the allocated key exists but is `is_active=false`, AI calls are blocked with a specific "key is allocated but inactive" reason; if nothing is allocated at all, the error message differentiates "other active keys exist but none allocated to this project" vs. "no active workspace AI key exists at all" — useful distinct error states to test for.
- **AI Providers tab UI (`components/settings/AiProvidersTab.tsx`)**:
  - "Workspace AI keys" card: add-key form (name, provider select incl. "Custom provider" which reveals provider-name + base-URL fields, API key as a password input, default-model text input with a `<datalist>` of known model suggestions per provider, and for custom providers an auth-header/auth-scheme pair defaulting to `Authorization`/`Bearer`).
  - Existing keys table: Name, Provider (uppercased), Masked key, Default model, and a "Remove" button — non-Owners see "Owner only" text instead of the button; the whole add-form is hidden entirely for non-Owners (with a banner: "Only workspace owner can manage AI keys and project allocations").
  - "Project key allocation" card: one row per project with a `<select>` of "No key allocated" + every workspace key (`name (provider)`); changing it calls the allocation endpoint immediately (no separate Save button); disabled for non-Owners.
  - A "Provider details" link navigates to `/settings/ai-providers/details` (separate page, not covered in depth here — out of the Auth/Workspace core scope).
  - Success/error banners persist until the next action (not auto-dismissed like the Members tab's toasts).

**Edge cases worth testing:**
- Non-Owner (Manager or QA Engineer) attempting any of the three mutating AI-key endpoints directly via API → 403, even though they can still view keys (masked) via GET.
- Creating a key with a name that collides with an existing one → silently overwrites (verify this is really intended, not a bug — no warning is shown to the user in the UI before this happens).
- Allocating a key belonging to a different workspace/org (by id) to a project → 404, not silently accepted.
- Un-allocating a project (selecting "No key allocated") should immediately block that project's AI features with a clear reason string, not a generic failure.
- Custom provider without a base URL → blocked both client-side (submit button disabled) and server-side (400).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`GET/POST /api/workspace/ai-keys`, `DELETE /api/workspace/ai-keys/:keyId`, `POST /api/workspace/ai-keys/allocations`), `legacy.service.ts` (`aiKeys`, `createAiKey`, `deleteAiKey`, `allocateAiKey`, `zyraAiAllocation`, `buildAnthropicAuthHeaders`, `describeProviderError`)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/settings/AiProvidersTab.tsx`, `app/(app)/settings/ai-providers/page.tsx` (redirect stub to `/settings?tab=ai`), `app/(app)/settings/ai-providers/details/page.tsx` (separate "Provider details" page, not deep-dived — out of Auth/Workspace core scope), `lib/api.ts` (`listWorkspaceAiKeys`, `createWorkspaceAiKey`, `deleteWorkspaceAiKey`, `allocateWorkspaceAiKeyToProject`)

---

## Section B — Projects, Test Suites, Test Cases

Scope: `/api/projects*`, `/api/suites/*`, `/api/projects/:projectId/testcases*` (list/CRUD, bulk ops,
import/export), and the corresponding frontend pages under
`Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/**` and `Tesbo-Frontend/components/testcases/*`,
`Tesbo-Frontend/components/ImportTestCasesModal.tsx`.

> **Cross-cutting authorization finding (applies to almost every feature below):** the global
> `AuthMiddleware` (`Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts`) only resolves *who* the caller
> is (`req.userId`) — it does not check project membership. Authorization is left entirely to each
> service method calling a `requireProjectAccess(userId, projectId)` helper
> (`legacy.service.ts:1163`). That helper is **only** called by: `getProjectForUser`,
> `updateProjectForUser`, `deleteProjectForUser`, `listApiKeys`, `createApiKey`, `revokeApiKey`. It is
> **not** called by `listSuites`, `createSuite`, `updateSuite`, `deleteSuite`, `projectMembers`,
> `addProjectMember`, `removeProjectMember`, `listTestCases`, `getTestCase`, `createTestCase`,
> `updateTestCase`, `deleteTestCase`, `bulkUpdateTestCases`, `bulkDeleteTestCases`,
> `linkedJiraKeys`/`linkedLinearKeys`. In practice this means **any authenticated user of the
> workspace (or even a different workspace, since these methods never check `organization_id`
> either) can read/list/create/rename/delete suites and test cases, and list/add/remove members, for
> any project ID they can guess or observe** — the UI simply never exposes the option, but the API
> does not enforce it. `addProjectMember` additionally performs no validation on the `role` value, so
> a caller could add themselves to any project with `role: "owner"`. This is flagged as a priority
> authorization/IDOR test area under each relevant section below rather than repeated in full each
> time.

---

### Projects

**What it is:** A Project is the top-level container for a test-management workspace inside an
organization — it owns suites, test cases, cycles/runs, plans, reports, and integrations. Each user
sees only the projects they are a member of, scoped to their currently active organization/workspace.

**Use cases:**
- A QA lead spins up a new project per product/app/repo being tested.
- A tester switches between multiple active projects from a dashboard-style list.
- A manager reviews project health at a glance (test case count, suite count, pass rate, team, last activity) before drilling in.
- An owner retires a project that's no longer maintained.

**Problem it solves:** Gives every other feature (suites, test cases, runs, reports, integrations) a
tenant boundary, and gives teams a single place to see the health/status of each product area they test.

**Features & actions:**
- **List projects** (`GET /api/projects` → `listProjects`, `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/page.tsx`)
  - Scoped to the caller's active organization AND to projects where the caller has a `project_members` row; excludes soft-deleted (`archived_at IS NULL`) projects.
  - Ordered by `created_at DESC`.
  - Frontend enriches each project with: test case count, suite count, team member avatars, last activity timestamp, latest test-run pass-rate breakdown (passed/failed/blocked), and a derived **status badge**: `setup_required` (0 test cases), `active` (has activity), `configured` (has test cases but no activity yet).
  - **Grid view** (cards: color-coded initial avatar, key, description, 3-stat row, pass-rate bar, team avatars, relative last-updated time) and **List view** (dense table). View choice persisted in `localStorage` (`tesbo_projects_view`).
  - Toolbar has **Sort** ("Last updated") and **Filter** buttons that render but have **no `onClick` handler wired up — they are currently non-functional/cosmetic**; only the grid/list toggle actually works. Worth testing/confirming this is not accidentally clickable-but-broken in some browsers.
  - Empty state ("No projects yet") differs by permission: create-project CTA for owner/admin/manager, or a "ask your manager" message for others.
- **Create project** (`POST /api/projects` → `createProject`)
  - Requires `name` (trimmed, 400 if blank).
  - `key` is optional; if omitted it's derived from `name` via `projectKey()`: uppercased, non-alphanumerics stripped, truncated to 16 chars, falls back to `"TESBO"` if empty. The UI also auto-uppercases/strips as you type in the Key field.
  - **No application-level uniqueness check on the derived/typed key** before insert — the DB has `UNIQUE(organization_id, key)`. Creating a second project with a colliding key (e.g., two projects both named "Test") will hit a raw DB constraint violation, not a friendly validation message. **Worth testing**: create two projects that normalize to the same key.
  - `projectType` defaults to `"tesbox"` (only value currently supported per the frontend type).
  - On create, seeds a root Knowledge Base folder and inserts the creator as `project_members` role `owner` (all inside one DB transaction).
  - Gated client-side to workspace role `owner`/`admin`/`manager` (`canCreateProject`); **not enforced server-side** in `createProject` — any authenticated user with a resolvable workspace can call the endpoint directly.
  - Modal also supports a `?create=1` query param to auto-open the Create Project modal (deep link from elsewhere in the app).
- **Get project** (`GET /api/projects/:id` → `getProjectForUser`) — 404s if not found, archived, or (via `requireProjectAccess`) not in caller's workspace/membership.
- **Update project** (`PATCH /api/projects/:id` → `updateProjectForUser`)
  - Fields: `name`, `description`, `settings` (JSON string blob), each independently `COALESCE`d so partial updates work.
  - `settings` blob (parsed/serialized client-side) currently carries: `jiraAutoComment` (bool), `jiraTicketSelector` (bool), `testcaseIdPrefix` (string, normalized to max 3 upper-alphanumeric chars), `testRunEnvironments` (array of `{name, url}`).
  - Settings page has tabs: **General** (name, description, testcase ID prefix + Save), **Test Environments** (add/remove named env URLs, duplicate name-check case-insensitively), **Team Members**, **Jira** (only shown if Jira is connected workspace-wide), **Integrations** (Jira/Linear connect-in-workspace-settings links + "more integrations coming soon" placeholder).
  - Test-case-ID-prefix change **only affects newly created test cases going forward** — existing external IDs are not renamed/backfilled.
- **Delete project** (`DELETE /api/projects/:id` → `deleteProjectForUser`)
  - Soft delete only: sets `archived_at = now()`; row and all children (test cases, suites, etc.) remain in the DB.
  - UI requires typing the exact project name into a confirmation modal ("Danger zone") before the delete button is enabled/submits; mismatched name aborts client-side with a message, no request sent.
  - Copy warns "permanently removes its test cases, runs, reports, and integrations" — in reality it's a soft-archive of the project row only; child rows (test cases, suites, runs) are **not** cascaded/archived themselves, they simply become unreachable through the normal project-scoped list endpoints. **Worth testing**: whether a test case's `id` from a deleted project is still directly fetchable via `GET /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/:testcaseId` (per the authorization gap noted above, likely yes since that route doesn't check the project's `archived_at`).
- Edge cases to test:
  - Creating a project with an empty/whitespace-only name (client + server both reject).
  - Creating a project with a key that collides with another project in the same org (DB error propagation/UX).
  - Deleting a project you don't manage (role gating only in UI, not enforced server for delete beyond membership check via `requireProjectAccess`).
  - Very long name/description (DB column limits: `name VARCHAR(255)`, `key VARCHAR(32)`).
  - Settings JSON malformed/non-object payload (frontend `parseProjectSettings` swallows parse errors and falls back to `{}`).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:176-199` (routes), `legacy.service.ts:1108-1204` (`listProjects`, `createProject`, `getProject`/`getProjectForUser`, `requireProjectAccess`, `updateProject(ForUser)`, `deleteProject(ForUser)`), `legacy.service.ts:151-157` (`projectKey`).
- Migration: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V1_init_schema.sql` (`projects` table, `UNIQUE(organization_id, key)`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/page.tsx` (list/create/grid/list toggle), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/page.tsx` (redirects to `/dashboard`), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/page.tsx` (general/danger-zone tabs).

---

### Project Members

**What it is:** Per-project membership list mapping workspace users to a project-scoped role
(`owner`, `manager`, `qa_engineer` — with legacy aliases `admin`/`test_manager` normalized to
`manager`). Controls who shows up as "team" on the project and (in principle) what they can do
inside it.

**Use cases:**
- A project owner adds a QA engineer from the workspace to a specific project.
- A manager promotes/demotes another member's project role.
- An owner removes someone who's rolled off the project.

**Problem it solves:** Lets a workspace have many projects with different staffing, without giving
every workspace member access to every project.

**Features & actions:**
- **List members** (`GET /api/projects/:id/members` → `projectMembers`): joins `project_members` + `users`, returns `userId, email, name, role, joinedAt`, ordered by email. **No auth/membership check at all** in the service method (see cross-cutting note above) — callable by any authenticated user for any project id.
- **Add / change role of a member** (`POST /api/projects/:id/members` → `addProjectMember`): upsert on `(project_id, user_id)` — same endpoint is reused for both "add new member" and "change existing member's role" (`ON CONFLICT ... DO UPDATE SET role`). Requires `userId`; `role` defaults to `"member"` if omitted (note: `"member"` isn't one of the three roles the UI normalizes to — an edge case, since `normalizeRole()` on the frontend maps anything unrecognized to `qa_engineer`). **No validation that the caller has permission to add/promote, and no validation that `role` is one of the allowed values** — e.g. a request could set `role: "owner"` for an arbitrary user on an arbitrary project.
- **Remove member** (`DELETE /api/projects/:id/members/:userId` → `removeProjectMember`): unconditional delete, no auth/role check, **no protection against removing the last remaining member or the last/only owner** of a project. Worth testing: remove every member from a project (including yourself) and confirm what happens to a now-memberless project (likely becomes permanently inaccessible through the normal membership-gated project routes, e.g. `getProjectForUser`).
- Frontend (`app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/page.tsx`, tab = `members`; the standalone `/projects/[id]/members` route just redirects here):
  - Read-only role legend card (Owner/Admin/Manager/Member descriptions — note the copy references "Admin" as a role even though the actual role set is owner/manager/qa_engineer, a **UI copy vs. actual role-model mismatch** worth flagging).
  - "Add workspace member" form: dropdown of workspace members **not already** on the project, plus a role dropdown restricted to roles the *current user* is allowed to assign (`assignableRoles()`): owners can assign manager/qa_engineer; managers can only assign qa_engineer; qa_engineers see no assignable roles (form hidden).
  - Per-row role change via inline `<select>`, gated by `canChangeRole()`: not editable for yourself, not editable if target is owner, managers cannot edit other managers.
  - Per-row **Remove** action, gated the same way, hidden for yourself and for owners.
  - "(you)" tag next to your own row.
  - All of this client-side gating is **cosmetic only** given the missing server-side checks noted above — a direct API call bypasses every one of these rules.
- Edge cases to test:
  - Add a user who is not a member of the *workspace* at all (only `userId` is validated as present, not workspace membership) — likely creates an orphaned `project_members` row referencing a foreign-key-valid but workspace-unrelated user.
  - Re-add an existing member with a different role (should update role via the upsert, confirmed by code).
  - Remove yourself as the only owner of a project.
  - Attempt role escalation via direct API call as a `qa_engineer`.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts:201-214`, `legacy.service.ts:1206-1226`.
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/page.tsx` (members tab, lines ~318-386 for logic, ~645-782 for UI), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/members/page.tsx` (redirect stub).

---

### Project API Keys (Tesbo MCP machine tokens)

**What it is:** Project-scoped bearer API tokens ("Tesbo MCP foundation") that let machine
clients (e.g., an MCP server/automation) authenticate as a project without a browser session.

**Use cases:**
- Wiring up an MCP (Model Context Protocol) client or CI job to read/write test cases via API without human login.
- Issuing a scoped (`read` or `read+write`) credential to a third-party integration.

**Problem it solves:** Session-cookie auth doesn't work for headless/automation clients; this gives
them a revocable, project-scoped credential instead of sharing a user's session.

**Features & actions:**
- **List keys** (`GET /api/projects/:id/apikeys` → `listApiKeys`): returns summaries only (`id, name, scopes, tokenPrefix, lastUsedAt, createdAt`) — raw token is never returned again after creation. Properly gated by `requireProjectAccess`.
- **Create key** (`POST /api/projects/:id/apikeys` → `createApiKey`): requires `name` (400 if blank); `scopes` optional, normalized to a set of `read`/`write` values (anything invalid is filtered out; if nothing valid remains, defaults to **both** `read` and `write`). Token format: `tsbo_` + 24 random bytes hex; only the SHA-256 hash is persisted (`token_hash`), raw token returned exactly once in the response body. Gated by `requireProjectAccess`, i.e. **any project member** (not just owner/manager) can mint a key.
- **Revoke key** (`DELETE /api/projects/:id/apikeys/:keyId` → `revokeApiKey`): deletes by `id + project_id`; 404 if not found/already revoked/belongs to a different project. Gated by `requireProjectAccess`.
- **Authentication path**: `AuthMiddleware` checks bearer tokens against `ApiTokenService.authenticate()` (SHA-256 lookup) only when there's no valid session cookie; on success it stamps `last_used_at` (best-effort, doesn't block the request on failure) and attaches `{tokenId, userId, projectId, scopes}` to the request.
- **No frontend UI exists for this feature at all** — grepping the entire `Tesbo-Frontend` tree finds zero references to `apikeys`/`createApiKey`/`listApiKeys`/`revokeApiKey`. This is a **backend-only / API-only feature today**; the only way to test it is directly against the REST API (curl/Postman) or once an MCP client consumes it. Worth flagging to QA as "no UI to verify visually — API-level testing only for now."
- Edge cases to test:
  - Create a key with no `scopes` → should default to `["read","write"]`.
  - Create a key with garbage scopes (e.g. `["admin"]`) → should fall back to default read+write (since nothing valid survives the filter).
  - Revoke a key ID that belongs to a different project than the one in the URL → should 404, not revoke.
  - Use a revoked token on a subsequent request → should be treated as unauthenticated (row no longer matches `token_hash` lookup).
  - Since `createApiKey`/`listApiKeys`/`revokeApiKey` only check *membership*, not *role*, a `qa_engineer` member can mint/revoke project machine credentials — confirm whether that's intended.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts:216-229`, `legacy.service.ts:304-326` (thin wrapper), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/api-token.service.ts` (token issuance/hash/validation), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts` (bearer auth path), migration `V*_api_tokens_webhooks.sql`.
- Frontend: none (feature has no UI as of this writing).

---

### Test Suites / Repository Organization

**What it is:** Suites are folders used to organize test cases within a project's repository, modeled
as an adjacency list (`parent_id` self-reference), so a suite can nest under another suite.

**Use cases:**
- Grouping test cases by feature area/module (e.g., "Authentication" → "Login", "Signup").
- Filtering the repository view down to one suite (or its whole subtree) at a time.
- Deciding what happens to a suite's test cases when the suite itself is deleted.

**Problem it solves:** Flat lists of hundreds/thousands of test cases are unusable without a folder
structure to scope work and reviews to a feature area.

**Features & actions:**
- **List suites** (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/suites` → `listSuites`): returns every suite in the project with a computed `testCaseCount` (`LEFT JOIN` + `COUNT`), ordered by `position` then `name`. **No auth/membership check** (see cross-cutting note).
- **Create suite** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/suites` → `createSuite`): requires `name` (400 if blank); optional `parentId` (no validation that the parent belongs to the same project — a suite could theoretically be parented to a suite in a different project); optional `position` (defaults 0). No auth check.
  - **Suite depth**: the DB/API allow arbitrary nesting depth (any suite can be `parentId` of any other), but the **frontend tree UI only renders two levels** (root suites + their direct children — `rootSuites` / `childrenBySuiteId` in the page component). A suite created as a *grandchild* (child of a child) via direct API call will not display correctly in the sidebar tree — **worth testing** nesting 3+ levels deep via API and observing the UI.
  - The "Add suite" modal's parent dropdown only lists **root** suites, so the UI itself can only ever produce 2 levels of nesting; deeper nesting is only reachable via direct API calls.
- **Update suite** (`PATCH /api/suites/:suiteId` → `updateSuite`): `name` (COALESCE, i.e. omit to keep), `parentId` (**always overwritten**, not COALESCEd — passing no `parentId` sets it to `null`, i.e. **omitting `parentId` on a rename silently moves the suite to root**), `position` (COALESCE). No auth check. Only used by the frontend for **renaming** (only sends `{name}`) — since `parentId` isn't COALESCEd, this rename call as implemented is fine (frontend never sends `parentId` for a plain rename, so it stays under `updateSuite`'s `??` default of `null`... **actually this means every rename via the current UI moves the suite to root-level**, since `updateSuite(suiteId, {name})` is called with no `parentId` field, and the SQL sets `parent_id = $3` unconditionally to `body.parentId ?? null`). **High-value test**: rename a *child* suite via the UI and confirm whether it gets unexpectedly promoted to a root suite.
- **Delete suite** (`DELETE /api/suites/:suiteId?mode=deleteTestcases|moveToDefault` → `deleteSuite`):
  - `mode=deleteTestcases`: hard-deletes (`DELETE FROM testcases WHERE suite_id = ...`) all test cases directly in that suite — **this is a hard delete, bypassing the normal soft-delete (`deleted_at`) used everywhere else** for test cases, so these rows are unrecoverable and won't show up in any "trash/restore" flow if one exists elsewhere.
  - `mode=moveToDefault` (default if omitted): sets `suite_id = NULL` on the suite's test cases. **There is no actual "Default Suite" entity anywhere in the schema/service** — the UI's modal copy ("Move all test cases to the Default Suite") is misleading; the real effect is "unassign the suite" (test cases show as "No suite" elsewhere in the UI). **Worth flagging as a copy/behavior mismatch.**
  - Neither mode touches **child suites** of the deleted suite — the UI warns "This suite has N sub-suites. Deleting it may affect those too" but the DB has `parent_id UUID REFERENCES suites(id) ON DELETE CASCADE`, so deleting a parent **cascades and hard-deletes its child suites** at the DB level (their test cases, per the same FK behavior on `testcases.suite_id` which is `ON DELETE SET NULL`, would just become unassigned, not deleted — unless `mode=deleteTestcases` only cleared the *parent's* direct test cases before the cascade, leaving the child suites' cascade to independently `SET NULL` their own test cases). **High-value test**: delete a suite with sub-suites in both modes and verify exactly what happens to grandchild test cases.
  - No auth check on delete.
- Frontend suite panel (in the Test Case repository page, since the standalone `/suites` route is now just a redirect into `/testcases`):
  - Collapsible left sidebar (persisted open/closed to `localStorage` key `tesbo_tc_suite_panel`).
  - "All test cases" pseudo-node showing total repository count.
  - Root suites expandable/collapsible (client-side only, `expandedSuiteIds` state, not persisted across reloads) to reveal one level of children.
  - Per-suite rollup count = suite's own `testCaseCount` + sum of its direct children's counts.
  - Hover-reveal row actions: **Add sub-suite**, **Rename**, **Delete** (root level); **Add test case**, **Rename**, **Delete** (child level — no "add sub-suite" for children, consistent with the 2-level UI limit).
  - "New suite" dashed-border CTA row at the bottom of the tree.
  - Clicking a suite navigates to `?suiteId=<id>` which filters the main test case table (does **not** automatically include child-suite cases — the suiteId filter is an exact match, `suite_id = $suiteId`, not a subtree match, so viewing a parent suite's filtered list will **not** show test cases that live directly in its child suites). **Worth testing/confirming**: does the "1234" rollup count shown on the parent suite row match what's actually displayed when you click into it (it won't, if the parent has any test cases nested in children).
- Edge cases to test:
  - Create a suite with a `parentId` from a different project.
  - Rename a child suite (see promotion-to-root bug above).
  - Delete a suite that has no test cases (should be a no-op data-wise, both modes behave identically).
  - Delete the suite currently being viewed (`activeSuiteId === deleteSuiteId`) — UI redirects to the unfiltered `/testcases` view.
  - Very deep nesting via API and its effect on the two-level UI tree.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts:231-249`, `legacy.service.ts:1228-1260`.
- Migration: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V2_test_cases_and_suites.sql` (`suites` table, `parent_id ... ON DELETE CASCADE`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/testcases/page.tsx` (suite tree UI, lines ~121-185 state, ~226-270 derived trees, ~545-608 create/rename/delete handlers, ~869-1121 tree rendering, ~1693-1794 add/delete modals), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/suites/page.tsx` (redirect stub).

---

### Test Cases

**What it is:** The core repository record: a single test case with title, description, steps,
metadata (priority/severity/type/status), automation linkage fields, and issue-tracker linkage
(Jira/Linear).

**Use cases:**
- Authoring manual test cases with step-by-step actions and expected results.
- Categorizing by priority/type/status for planning and reporting.
- Linking a test case back to the Jira ticket or Linear issue that prompted it.
- Archiving stale test cases without permanently losing them.

**Problem it solves:** Central, structured source of truth for "what needs to be tested," reused
across test plans, cycles/runs, and reporting.

**Features & actions:**
- **Full field inventory** (DB columns in `testcases`, `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V2_test_cases_and_suites.sql` + `V7_testcase_additional_fields.sql`), and whether each is reachable from the manual create/edit UI, the CSV/XLSX import mapping, or API-only:
  | Field | Manual UI form | CSV/XLSX import mapping | Notes |
  |---|---|---|---|
  | `title` | Yes (required) | Yes (required) | |
  | `description` | Yes | Yes | |
  | `preconditions` | Yes | Yes | |
  | `postconditions` | **No** | Yes | API/import-only field — no manual form field for it |
  | `steps` (jsonb array of `{stepNumber, action, expectedResult}`) | Yes (dedicated Steps tab/section, add/remove rows) | Yes (single text column split into steps on newline or ` \| `, expected result always blank) | |
  | `testData` | Yes | Yes | |
  | `priority` (P0-P3, default P2) | Yes | Yes | No DB CHECK constraint — any string is technically insertable via direct API call, bypassing the fixed P0-P3 dropdown |
  | `severity` | **No** | Yes | API/import-only — no manual form field |
  | `type` (Functional/Regression/Smoke/.../Security, default Functional) | Yes | Yes | No DB CHECK constraint, arbitrary values possible via API |
  | `status` (Draft/In Review/Approved/Deprecated/Archived, default Draft) | Yes | Yes | No DB CHECK constraint |
  | `component` | **No** | Yes | API/import-only |
