  | `estimatedDuration` | Yes (form field exists) | Yes (mappable in import UI) | **Dead field end-to-end**: DB column exists (`estimated_duration VARCHAR(64)`), but `createTestCase`/`updateTestCase` in `legacy.service.ts` never include it in the INSERT/UPDATE column list, so anything typed here is silently discarded and never persisted, and the import flow's own `createTestCase()` call in `ImportTestCasesModal.tsx` also drops it from the payload. **High-value, easy-to-demonstrate bug for QA.** |
  | `attachments` | Yes, labeled **"Notes"** (free text) | **No** (not in `IMPORTABLE_FIELDS`) | Despite the name/DB column (`TEXT`), this is used purely as a free-text notes box in the UI, not file attachments (there is a separate, unrelated `attachments` *table* for entity file metadata that this feature does not use) |
  | `automationStatus`, `automationRepo`, `automationPath`, `automationTestName`, `automationFramework` | **No** | **No** | API/MCP-only fields, no UI anywhere in this scope to set them |
  | `automationTags` | **No** (read-only chip display in the repository table only) | **No** | Comma-split and rendered as small tags under the title in `RepositoryTestCaseTable`; nothing lets a user set/edit it manually |
  | `ownerId` | **No** | **No** | Column + API param exist, no UI |
  | `jiraIssueKey`/`jiraUrl`, `linearIssueKey`/`linearUrl` | Read-only chip in edit panel header (external link) | **No** | Set via Jira/Linear integration sync (out of this scope), not directly editable here |
  | `suiteId` | Yes | Yes (by suite *name*, auto-resolved/auto-created) | |
  | `externalId` (e.g. `TC-TC-1`) | Auto-generated; a "Test case ID prefix" field lets you steer the prefix **at creation time only** | N/A (import rows never set an explicit external ID) | See ID generation below |
- **List test cases** (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/testcases` → `listTestCases`):
  - Server-side pagination (`limit` capped at 500, default 100; `offset`), filters: `suiteId`, `status`, `priority`, `type`, `automationStatus`, `jiraIssueKey`, `linearIssueKey`, and a `search` term matched (case-insensitive `LIKE`) against `title`, `description`, `external_id`, and `type`.
  - Fixed sort: `updated_at DESC` — **there is no user-facing "sort by" control** on the repository page (only filter dropdowns), and no way to sort by title/priority/ID from the UI.
  - Response returns only a lightweight column subset (id, externalId, title, priority, type, automationStatus, automationTags, status, suiteId, ownerId, updatedAt, jira/linear key+url) — not description/steps/preconditions, which is why opening a row does a separate full `GET` fetch.
  - Total count returned via the `X-Total-Count` response header (set by the controller) as well as in the JSON envelope on the frontend's wrapped call.
  - **No auth/membership check** in `listTestCases` itself (cross-cutting finding above).
- **Get single test case** (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/:testcaseId` → `getTestCase`): looks up **by `testcaseId` only** — the `:projectId` path segment is accepted but never validated against the row's actual `project_id`. **Worth testing**: fetch a real test case ID while putting a *different, unrelated* project's ID in the URL — expect it to succeed and return the test case anyway (since the service ignores `projectId` entirely here).
- **Create test case** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/testcases` → `createTestCase`): requires an authenticated user (`requireUser`, 400 if missing) but **not project membership**. Defaults: `title` → "Untitled test case" if blank (not actually required/validated beyond that fallback), `priority` → P2, `type` → Functional, `status` → Draft, `steps` → `[]`. Logs a `testcase_created` project-activity entry (with full after-snapshot).
  - `testcaseIdPrefix` in the request body only affects **ID generation for this one call**, it's not persisted as a project default (that lives in project `settings.testcaseIdPrefix`, set from the Settings page).
- **Update test case** (`PUT /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/:testcaseId` → `updateTestCase`): despite being a `PUT` (which conventionally implies full replacement), the implementation is **fully partial** — every column is `COALESCE`d against the existing value except `suite_id`, which (like suite rename above) is **always overwritten** to `body.suiteId ?? null` — meaning **omitting `suiteId` in an update payload unassigns the test case from its suite**. The frontend always sends the current `suiteId` explicitly on save so this isn't hit through the UI, but any direct/partial API `PUT` that forgets `suiteId` will silently unassign the test case. Logs `testcase_updated` with before/after snapshot. 404s if the row is already soft-deleted.
- **Delete test case** (`DELETE /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/:testcaseId` → `deleteTestCase`): soft delete (`deleted_at`, `deleted_by`); 404 if already deleted; logs `testcase_deleted` with before-snapshot. Frontend confirms via a native `window.confirm()` dialog before calling.
- **Archive / Unarchive** (UI-only convenience, not separate endpoints): both call the normal update endpoint with `{status: "Archived"}` / `{status: "Draft"}` respectively. Confirmed via `window.confirm()` for archive, **no confirmation for unarchive**.
- **ID generation** (`nextExternalId`): format `{PREFIX}-TC-{n}`, where `n` = `MAX(trailing numeric suffix of existing external_ids matching "{PREFIX}-TC-%")` + 1. This is a **read-then-insert pattern with no locking/sequence**, so two test cases created concurrently with the same prefix in the same project can compute the same `n` and race to insert the same `external_id` — the DB's `UNIQUE(project_id, external_id)` index will then reject the second insert with a raw constraint-violation error (not a friendly "ID already taken, retry" message). **High-value concurrency test**: fire two near-simultaneous "Create" submissions for the same project/prefix.
  - Because it's MAX-based rather than count-based, deleting test cases doesn't cause ID reuse/collisions on its own — a genuinely good property — but it does mean IDs are **not** contiguous once anything is deleted.
- **Detail/edit panel UI** (right-side drawer over the repository table):
  - **Create mode**: single scrolling form — Title*, Test case ID prefix (editable only at this stage), Description, Suite/Type/Priority/Status/Estimated Duration grid, Preconditions, Test Data, Test Steps (add/remove rows, each with Action + Expected Result), Notes.
  - **Edit mode**: tabbed — **Overview** (same fields minus ID prefix, which can't be changed after creation) and **Steps** (dedicated step list with its own add/remove).
  - Footer actions: **Create** / **Save changes**, **Create & Add Next** (create-mode only — saves then immediately resets the form pre-seeded with the same suite for rapid sequential entry), **Cancel**, and in edit mode **Archive/Unarchive** + **Delete**.
  - Success/error banners auto-dismiss (success message clears after 4s).
  - Opening a row while an edit is in-flight (`panelLoading`) shows a spinner; the panel closes on backdrop click or the X button.
- Edge cases to test:
  - Save with an empty title in edit mode (HTML `required` attribute is the only client-side gate; server falls back to "Untitled test case" only on **create**, not on update — an update with `title: ""` sent explicitly: since `body.title ?? null` and empty string `""` is not `null`/`undefined`, `COALESCE("", title)` will actually **set the title to empty string**, since COALESCE only substitutes on SQL `NULL`, not empty string. **Worth testing**: submit an edit with title cleared out via direct API call bypassing the `required` HTML attribute).
  - Steps with an empty `action` (removed automatically only via the "Remove" UI button; steps API accepts empty-string actions/expected results with no validation).
  - Very long steps arrays, very long title/description.
  - Cross-project `testcaseId`/`projectId` mismatch in URL (see IDOR note above).
  - Un-archiving a test case restores it to `"Draft"` unconditionally, not to whatever status it had before archiving (status history isn't preserved/restored).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts:251-296` (routes), `legacy.service.ts:1262-1503` (`listTestCases`, `getTestCase`, `createTestCase`, `updateTestCase`, `deleteTestCase`, `linkedJiraKeys`, `linkedLinearKeys`), `legacy.service.ts:7810-7823` (`nextExternalId`).
- Migrations: `V2_test_cases_and_suites.sql`, `V7_testcase_additional_fields.sql`.
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/testcases/page.tsx` (single large file covering list + detail panel; state ~121-190, form handlers ~363-726, detail panel UI ~1361-1691), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/testcases/RepositoryTestCaseTable.tsx` (row rendering), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/testcases/[tcId]/page.tsx` (redirect stub — detail is a drawer, not a route).

---

### Test Case Bulk Operations

**What it is:** Multi-select on the repository table plus a single "Bulk actions" modal offering
move/update/archive/delete across the current selection.

**Use cases:**
- Moving a batch of test cases into a newly created suite.
- Mass-updating priority/status after a planning meeting.
- Archiving or deleting a batch of obsolete test cases at once.

**Problem it solves:** Avoids opening and editing dozens/hundreds of test cases one at a time for
routine reclassification/cleanup.

**Features & actions:**
- **Selection**: per-row checkbox + header "select all" checkbox (`RepositoryTestCaseTable`). "Select all" only affects the **rows currently loaded on the current page** (`selectedSuiteCases` = current page's results) — **it is not a "select all N results across all pages"** operation. Selection state is reconciled automatically whenever the visible case list changes (page turn, filter change, search) — any previously selected IDs that are no longer in view are dropped from the selection silently.
- **Bulk action bar**: appears only when `selectedCaseIds.length > 0`, shows a live count, a "Bulk actions" link (opens the modal) and "Clear selection".
- **Bulk actions modal**, action dropdown with 4 options:
  - **Move to suite**: target suite dropdown includes "Unassigned (no suite)" plus every suite in the project (flat list, not tree-indented) → `bulkUpdateTestCases({testcaseIds, suiteId})`.
  - **Update status / priority**: two dropdowns (defaults Draft / P2 when the modal opens, **not the current values of the selected cases** — so opening this action always shows Draft/P2 regardless of what's actually selected, and applying it without changing the pre-filled defaults will blast every selected case to Draft/P2) → `bulkUpdateTestCases({testcaseIds, status, priority})`.
  - **Archive**: sets `status: "Archived"` for every selected case, warning banner shown, no extra confirmation beyond "Confirm".
  - **Delete**: soft-deletes every selected case (`bulkDeleteTestCases`), red warning "This action cannot be undone", "Confirm" button rendered in destructive styling.
  - Confirm button disabled while no action chosen or while a request is in flight; errors surface inline in the modal.
- **Backend bulk-update** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/bulk-update` → `bulkUpdateTestCases`): single `UPDATE ... WHERE id = ANY($ids) AND deleted_at IS NULL` statement; only supports **`priority`, `suiteId`, `status`, `ownerId`** (all `COALESCE`d against existing values, so any field omitted from the body is left untouched per-row — unlike the single-update endpoint's suite-always-overwritten quirk, here `suiteId` **is** COALESCEd, so bulk "move to suite" with no `suiteId` would be a no-op rather than unassigning, which is inconsistent with `updateTestCase`'s behavior for the same field). No-ops silently (returns nothing) if `testcaseIds` is empty. Logs one `testcase_bulk_updated` activity entry listing all affected IDs + the field values applied.
- **Backend bulk-delete** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/bulk-delete` → `bulkDeleteTestCases`): same soft-delete as the single-delete endpoint, applied via `id = ANY($ids)`; logs one `testcase_bulk_deleted` activity entry with the ID list. No-ops silently on an empty array (controller defaults `body.testcaseIds` to `[]` if missing).
- Both bulk endpoints require an authenticated user (`requireUser`) but, like the single-record endpoints, **do not verify project membership**, and **do not verify the given `testcaseIds` actually belong to the `:projectId` in the URL** — a bulk request could reference IDs from a different project and (based on the plain `id = ANY($ids)` WHERE clause with no `project_id` filter) still update/delete them.
- After a bulk action, if the currently-open detail panel's test case was part of the selection: for bulk-delete the panel is closed; for other bulk actions the panel is refreshed in place to reflect the change.
- Edge cases to test:
  - Bulk "Update status/priority" opened and confirmed **without** changing the pre-filled Draft/P2 defaults — verify all selected cases silently get reset to Draft/P2 even if that wasn't the intent.
  - Bulk actions with a mix of already-deleted IDs mixed into the selection (stale client-side state) — should just no-op for those rows (`deleted_at IS NULL` guard).
  - Selecting on page 1, changing the page size or turning the page (selection for now-hidden rows is dropped — confirm this doesn't silently apply a bulk action against a stale, larger set the user thinks is still selected).
  - Cross-project `testcaseIds` in a bulk request (see authorization note above).
  - Bulk move-to-suite targeting a suite ID that doesn't exist / belongs to another project (no FK-level validation visible beyond the actual foreign key constraint on `testcases.suite_id`).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts:288-296`, `legacy.service.ts:1461-1485`.
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/testcases/page.tsx` (selection state ~164-171, 256-269, 359-361; handlers ~473-543; modal UI ~1796-1883), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/testcases/RepositoryTestCaseTable.tsx` (checkbox column/select-all header).

---

### Test Case Import/Export

**What it is:** CSV/XLSX export of a project's full test case repository, a downloadable import
template, and a client-side-driven import wizard (upload → map columns → review → import row-by-row).

**Use cases:**
- Bulk-authoring test cases in a spreadsheet, then importing them.
- Migrating test cases from another tool via a CSV/XLSX export from that tool.
- Exporting the repository for offline review, backup, or reporting outside the app.

**Problem it solves:** Manual one-by-one entry doesn't scale for seeding a new project's repository
or migrating from a legacy spreadsheet/tool.

**Features & actions:**
- **Export CSV** (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/export/csv` → controller builds CSV directly) and **Export XLSX** (`GET .../export/xlsx`, via `sendWorkbook`/`xlsx` package): both call `exportTestCases(projectId)` which pulls **all non-deleted test cases** for the project (no filter/suite scoping — exporting while viewing a filtered suite still exports the **entire project**, not just what's currently visible). Fixed 12-column schema: `externalId, title, description, preconditions, steps, testData, priority, severity, type, status, suite, component`.
  - `steps` (jsonb) is flattened to a single text cell as `"action1 => expected1 | action2 => expected2"` (falls back to just the action/description text if `expectedResult` missing, joins multiple step fragments with `" | "`).
  - CSV cells are escaped (quoted + doubled internal quotes) if they contain a comma, quote, or newline.
  - Downloads trigger via plain `<a href target=_blank>` links (Export dropdown in the repository page's top bar), not a JS fetch — so auth relies on cookie-based session for the direct navigation to work.
- **Import template download** (`GET .../testcases/import/template?format=csv|xlsx`): returns one example row (Login test) with the same header set as export, minus `externalId` (template has no ID column, so re-imported IDs are always freshly assigned).
- **Import wizard** (`Tesbo-Frontend/components/ImportTestCasesModal.tsx`) — **entirely client-side**, not backend-driven (see stub-endpoint note below):
  1. **Upload step**: drag-and-drop or browse for `.csv/.xlsx/.xls`; parsed **in-browser** via the `xlsx` npm package (dynamically imported). Every sheet in a workbook is parsed; a sheet is kept only if it has at least one detected header. Header row is auto-detected by scanning for a cell that normalizes to `title`/`testcasetitle`/`testcase`/`summary`/`name`; falls back to row 0 if nothing matches. Blank rows are filtered out.
  2. **Mapping step**: shows detected row/sheet counts; if multiple sheets qualify, a sheet picker `<select>` is shown, and re-selecting a sheet re-runs auto-mapping. 13 importable fields (title, description, preconditions, postconditions, steps, testData, priority, severity, type, status, suite, component, estimatedDuration), each with a **"Skip"** option and a per-field alias dictionary used for auto-mapping (e.g. "prio" → priority, "folder"/"module" → suite, "scenario" → title). Only Title is required to proceed. Live preview table of the first 3 rows shown with only the currently-mapped columns.
  3. **Import execution** (`handleImport`):
     - Fetches **every existing test case already in the project** first (paginated 500-at-a-time loop against the normal list endpoint) to build a case-insensitive, whitespace-normalized title index for duplicate detection.
     - For each import row: skip with an error if Title is blank; skip with a "Skipped duplicate title: already exists in this project" error if the normalized title matches an existing case; skip with "Skipped duplicate title: repeated in this import file" if it matches an **earlier row in the same import batch** (so duplicates within the file are caught too, not just against existing data).
     - Steps column (if mapped) is split on newlines or ` | ` into a numbered step list with `expectedResult` always empty (import can't express expected results per step — only export can reconstruct the `=>` shorthand, but import doesn't parse it back out).
     - Suite column (if mapped) resolves to an existing suite by case/whitespace-normalized name, or **auto-creates a brand-new suite** with that exact (trimmed) name if none matches — meaning a typo'd suite name in the spreadsheet silently creates a new, similarly-named suite rather than erroring or prompting.
     - **`estimatedDuration` is mappable in the UI (shows in the field list and the mapping preview) but is never included in the actual `createTestCase()` payload sent** — confirming the same dead-field issue noted under Test Cases; it's dropped both here and in the manual form.
     - Each surviving row triggers **one sequential `POST .../testcases` call** — there is no batch/bulk-create endpoint used, so a 1,000-row import means 1,000 sequential HTTP round-trips (plus the up-front suite-creation calls), which will be slow and is fully sequential (not parallelized), meaning a browser tab closed/network drop mid-import leaves the job **partially complete** with no resume — re-running the import will just skip the already-created rows via the duplicate-title check (a reasonably safe retry story, worth confirming explicitly).
     - Per-row failures (e.g. a transient network error) are caught individually and added to the error list without aborting the rest of the batch.
  4. **Result step**: "N test cases imported successfully / Out of M total rows", plus a scrollable error table (row number + message) for anything skipped/failed. "Done" closes the modal and triggers a data refresh (`onImported` → reloads suites + the current test case page).
- **Backend import endpoints are dead stub code**: `POST /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/import/preview` (`previewImport()`) and `POST /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/import` (`executeImport()`) both **ignore their request body/uploaded file entirely** and hard-return placeholder payloads (`{uploadId: "local-upload", headers: [], previewRows: [], totalRows: 0}` and `{imported: 0, errors: []}` respectively). `lib/api.ts` even has an orphaned `previewImport()` helper that posts a `FormData` file to the preview endpoint, but the current `ImportTestCasesModal` **never calls it** — the whole import flow described above happens client-side against the ordinary create-test-case/list-suites endpoints instead. **Test recommendation**: explicitly verify (e.g., via curl/Postman) that hitting these two routes directly returns the empty stub response regardless of what's posted, so nobody mistakes them for a working server-side import path in the future.
- **Linked issue-key lookups** (`GET .../testcases/linked-jira-keys` / `linked-linear-keys` → `linkedJiraKeys`/`linkedLinearKeys`): return distinct Jira/Linear issue keys referenced by any non-deleted test case in the project, with a per-key count. Used to power the Jira/Linear filter chips (`?jiraIssueKey=`/`?linearIssueKey=` query params) on the repository page — clicking a chip elsewhere in the app (e.g. from a Jira ticket view, out of this scope) deep-links here pre-filtered; the chip in the filter bar shows the active key with an "X" to clear it (clearing navigates back to the unfiltered `/testcases` URL).
- Edge cases to test:
  - Import a file where the header row isn't the first row (e.g., a title/description banner above the real headers) — auto-detection should still find it by scanning for a title-like cell.
  - Import a workbook with multiple sheets, only some of which have valid headers — sheets without headers should be filtered out of the sheet picker entirely.
  - Import rows with a suite name that only differs by case/whitespace from an existing suite — should reuse the existing suite, not create a duplicate.
  - Import the same file twice in a row — second run should report every row as a duplicate (skipped), zero new imports.
  - Import a CSV exported from this same project (round-trip) — note `steps`' `" => "` shorthand is **not** parsed back into structured steps on import; the whole steps cell will land as one single step with the raw arrow text as the "action" and blank expected result, since the import step-splitting logic only splits on newlines/pipes, not on `=>`.
  - Export while a suite/status/priority filter is active in the repository view — confirm (per the code) that the export still contains the **whole project**, not just the filtered subset, and consider whether that matches user expectations.
  - Hitting `import/preview` or `import` directly with a real file — confirm it really is ignored (stub response) rather than partially processed.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts:516-566` (export/template/preview/import routes — note preview/import are stubs), `legacy.service.ts:1301-1340` (`exportTestCases`), `legacy.service.ts:1487-1503` (`linkedJiraKeys`/`linkedLinearKeys`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/ImportTestCasesModal.tsx` (entire client-side import pipeline), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` (`getExportUrl`, `getTemplateUrl`, orphaned `previewImport`, `listLinkedJiraKeys`/`listLinkedLinearKeys`), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/testcases/page.tsx` (Import/Export menu in the top bar, ~754-829).

---

### Test Case Repository Table (columns, sorting UI, selection)

**What it is:** The dense data-grid component (`RepositoryTestCaseTable`) that renders the current
page of test cases inside the repository view, with per-user column customization.

**Use cases:**
- A tester who mostly cares about Title/Status/Priority hides the Suite/Jira/Type columns to reduce clutter.
- Widening the Title column to read full test case names without truncation.
- Reordering columns to match a team's preferred scanning order (e.g., Priority before Title).

**Problem it solves:** Different roles care about different columns; a one-size-fits-all table either
shows too little or forces horizontal scrolling for everyone.

**Features & actions:**
- **8 data columns** available: ID, Test case title, Suite, Jira, Priority, Status, Updated, Type — plus a permanently-first, non-configurable **selection checkbox column**.
- **Show/hide columns**: "Columns" dropdown (portaled inline next to the type/status/priority filter dropdowns) lists all 8 with checkboxes and their raw field id; toggling updates visibility immediately. Default visible set: ID, Title, Priority, Status, Updated, Type (Suite and Jira hidden by default).
- **Reorder columns**: native HTML5 drag-and-drop on column headers (drag handle icon shown on hover); dropping a header onto another reorders the underlying data-column order; the selection column can't be dragged/reordered (always first).
- **Resize columns**: a drag handle on the right edge of each header (`mousedown` → track `mousemove`/`mouseup` globally) resizes between a per-column minimum (e.g. 72px for ID, 180px for Title) and a shared 560px maximum; cursor changes to `col-resize` and text-selection is suppressed while dragging.
- **Persistence**: all three (order, visibility, widths) are saved to `localStorage` under `tesbo-repo-tc-table:v1:<projectId>` — i.e. **preferences are per-project, per-browser**, not synced across devices/users. Loading is deferred one tick (`setTimeout(...,0)`) to avoid a layout flash; corrupted/partial/unknown-column JSON is defensively normalized back to sane defaults rather than throwing.
- **Suite column auto-show**: even if a user has hidden the Suite column, it automatically re-appears whenever the suite side panel is collapsed — so suite context isn't lost when the user reclaims horizontal space by hiding the sidebar. This is computed live (`visibleDataColumns`), not persisted as a preference change.
- **Row interactions**: clicking anywhere on a row (other than the checkbox) opens the detail panel for that test case; ID and Title cells are independently clickable buttons (same action, just for click-target precision/underline-on-hover affordance); the row that matches the currently-open detail panel is highlighted with a brand-tinted background.
- **Cell rendering specifics**: Priority/Status rendered as colored `StatusChip`s (P0→error/red, P1→warning, P2→"confidence-high" tint, P3→neutral; Approved→success, In Review→warning, Deprecated→error, Archived→neutral, anything else→brand tint); Jira column renders a clickable external link with a Jira glyph when both `jiraIssueKey` and `jiraUrl` are present, plain text if only the key is present, an em-dash otherwise; Updated column shows `toLocaleDateString()` (date only, no time); Title cell shows up to 2 lines (CSS line-clamp) plus small automation-tag chips beneath if `automationTags` is set.
- Edge cases to test:
  - Resize a column past its minimum/maximum — should clamp, not overflow or invert.
  - Hide every optional column — table should still render with just ID + Title (Title min-width guards against a fully collapsed table).
  - Corrupt the `localStorage` value by hand and reload — should fall back to defaults without crashing (defensive `try/catch` + per-key type/range validation in `loadPrefs`).
  - Switch between two projects in the same browser — column prefs should be independent (namespaced by `projectId`).
  - Drag a column onto itself (`from === to`) — should no-op (`moveColumn` guards this).

**Key files:**
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/testcases/RepositoryTestCaseTable.tsx` (entire component — column config ~9-117, persistence ~119-180, drag/resize handlers ~222-320, header/body cell rendering ~322-546, Columns menu ~548-588).

---

## Section C — Test Plans, Test Cycles/Runs, Executions, Scheduling, Public Share Links, Requirements Traceability

> Terminology used by the product: a **Test Plan** (`plans` table) is a lightweight release-scoped
> container (name, description, target release, owner) that test runs can optionally be linked to.
> A **Test Cycle** — surfaced everywhere in the UI as a **"Test Run"** — (`cycles` table) is the actual
> execution vehicle: a snapshot list of test cases (`cycle_items`) each with one `executions` row
> tracking status/assignee/result/defect linkage. "Plan" = scope/intent, "Run" = execution instance.

---

### Test Plans

**What it is:** A named, release-scoped folder (`plans` table) that groups test runs together and
optionally records a fixed scope of suites/test cases (`plan_items`) for release-level progress
reporting. Frontend calls it "Test plans".

**Use cases:**
- A release manager creates a "Sprint 12 Regression" plan tied to target release `v2.1.0` to group every regression run for that release.
- A QA lead opens a plan to see aggregate pass/fail/blocked counts across every run ever associated with it, without opening each run individually.
- A tester links an already-existing test run to a plan retroactively (e.g. a hotfix run created before the plan existed).

**Problem it solves:** Gives a release/sprint-level rollup of execution progress across multiple test
runs, instead of tracking each run in isolation.

**Features & actions:**
- List plans for a project (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/plans`) — grid or list view, toggle persisted in `localStorage` (`tesbo_plans_view`).
  - Each card shows: computed status badge (**Active** if `runCount > 0`, else **Draft** — there is no explicit "Completed"/"Archived" plan status), pass-rate bar (passed/failed/blocked only — skipped/untested excluded from the ratio), case count, run count, "last run" relative time, owner avatar.
  - Search (name/description substring), status filter chip (All/Active/Draft), sort (Recent/Name/Status cycles via a single button).
- Create plan (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/plans`) — name (required, defaults to "Untitled plan" server-side if blank is somehow submitted), description, target release. No environment/owner picker in the create form (ownerId only settable via raw API).
- Open plan detail (`GET /api/plans/:planId`) — breadcrumb + plan switcher side panel (collapsible, state persisted in `localStorage` `tesbo_plan_switcher_panel`) listing all plans in the project for quick switching.
- Edit plan inline (`PATCH /api/plans/:planId`) — name/description/target release only; **empty string is written as empty**, not treated as "no change" (the service does `COALESCE($2, name)` but the frontend always sends a string, e.g. `""`, when the description field is cleared, so clearing a field persists as blank, not as "field untouched").
- Delete plan (`DELETE /api/plans/:planId`) — confirm dialog explicitly states "Associated runs will not be deleted but will be unlinked." Backend matches: `cycles.plan_id` has `ON DELETE SET NULL`, so runs survive with `planId = null`.
- **Plan Items tab** (`GET /api/plans/:planId/items`) — lists suites or individual test cases that define the "intended scope" of the plan (`plan_items.suite_id XOR testcase_id`, DB-enforced via `CHECK (suite_id IS NOT NULL OR testcase_id IS NOT NULL)`).
  - Remove an item (`DELETE /api/plans/:planId/items/:itemId`) is implemented in the UI (trash icon per row).
  - **There is no "Add item" control anywhere in the UI.** `POST /api/plans/:planId/items` (`addPlanItem`) exists in `lib/api.ts` but is never called from any component — the only way to populate a plan's item scope is a direct API call. The Items tab can therefore only ever shrink, never grow, through the web app.
  - Each item shows last execution result for that test case *anywhere under this plan* (correlated subquery across all of the plan's cycles) — not scoped to a specific run.
- **Test Runs tab** — the plan's linked runs, each with its own segmented pass/fail/blocked/skipped bar and pass %.
  - **Create test run from this plan** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/cycles/from-plan`) — requires selecting an Environment from the project's configured `testRunEnvironments` (project settings); button disabled if none are configured. **Does not seed the new run with the plan's Plan Items** — backend `createCycle()` only inserts the `cycles` row (name/description/environment/buildVersion/releaseName/ownerId/planId); it never reads `plan_items` or any `testcaseIds`. The new run is created empty and cases must be added manually afterward, completely decoupled from whatever suites/cases were registered as the plan's scope.
  - **Link existing run** (`associateRunWithPlan` → `PATCH /api/cycles/:cycleId {planId}`) — opens a modal listing runs not yet linked to *any* plan shown in-memory (`allRuns` minus currently-linked); does not exclude runs already linked to a *different* plan at the API level, only client-side filtering based on what's currently displayed — a run could theoretically be re-parented from one plan to another this way.
  - **Unlink run** (`dissociateRunFromPlan` → `PATCH /api/cycles/:cycleId {clearPlan: true}`).
  - Only runs with status `In Progress` or `Completed` are shown in the Runs tab (`visibleRuns` filters out `Planning`) — a freshly created/linked run in `Planning` status is invisible in this tab until started, which can look like the create/link action silently failed.
- Overall progress bar + 6-stat tile grid (Total/Passed/Failed/Blocked/Skipped/Untested) is computed from **all cycles ever linked to the plan** (`planProgress`), not from Plan Items — i.e., the plan's headline % is really "average of its linked runs," while the Items tab (if ever populated) is an entirely separate, disconnected list.
- Permission gating: "Active"/create/edit/delete controls only shown when `myRole` is empty or one of owner/admin/manager; `qa_engineer` role sees a read-only plans list (no "New test plan" button, no create form, no edit/delete on cards).

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- Create a plan with an empty name — client blocks submit (`disabled={!newName.trim()}`), but nothing stops `POST` with a blank name via direct API (server falls back to `"Untitled plan"`).
- Delete a plan that has active runs — runs remain, `planId` becomes null; runs' own detail pages should stop showing a plan name/breadcrumb link.
- Two windows: unlink a run from Plan A in tab 1 while tab 2 still shows it in the Runs list — stale-until-refresh.
- Attempt to add a Plan Item via raw `POST /api/plans/:planId/items` with **neither** `suiteId` nor `testcaseId` — DB `CHECK` constraint `plan_item_ref` rejects the insert (500/DB error surfaces, not a clean 400).
- `DELETE /api/plans/:planId/items/:itemId` does not verify `itemId` actually belongs to `:planId` — the service ignores the `planId` route param entirely and matches only `id = itemId`; a mismatched pair still deletes the item (from whatever plan it really belongs to).
- No auth/ownership check on any plan route (see "Cross-Cutting" section below) — any logged-in user on the platform can `GET/PATCH/DELETE` any `planId` by guessing/using a UUID from another project, regardless of project membership.
- No activity-log entries are ever written for plan create/update/delete — the project Activity feed will never show "created/edited/deleted plan X" (only execution status changes and evidence uploads are logged anywhere in this module).
- Plan with `runCount === 0` always renders "Draft" even if it has Plan Items configured — status is purely a function of linked-run count.
- If the referenced test case behind a Plan Item is later archived/soft-deleted, `planItems()` still joins to `testcases` with **no `deleted_at` filter**, so its title/priority continue to display normally — inconsistent with how Cycle executions blank out the same fields for archived cases (see Test Executions).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` L298–346 (`/api/projects/:projectId/plans`, `/api/plans/:planId`, `/items`, `/runs`, `/progress`); `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` L1505–1674 (`listPlans`, `createPlan`, `getPlan`, `updatePlan`, `deletePlan`, `planItems`, `addPlanItem`, `deletePlanItem`, `planRuns`, `planProgress`).
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V3_plans_cycles_executions.sql` (`plans`, `plan_items`), `V28_plan_cycle_external_ids.sql` (adds `external_id`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/plans/page.tsx` (list), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/plans/[planId]/page.tsx` (detail: items/runs tabs, create/link run modals), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/testplans/PlanCard.tsx` (status badge, pass-rate bar, owner avatar).
- API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` L1299–1388 (`PlanItem`, `PlanRunItem`, `PlanProgress`, `PlanListItem`, `listPlanItems`, `addPlanItem`, `removePlanItem`, `listPlanRuns`, `getPlanProgress`, `associateRunWithPlan`, `dissociateRunFromPlan`).

---

### Test Cycles / Runs

**What it is:** A "Test Run" (`cycles` table, still literally named `cycle` in the schema/API) is a
concrete execution instance: a **snapshot** list of test cases (`cycle_items`, capturing the title at
add-time) each paired with one `executions` row that carries the live status/result. Runs have a
lifecycle status of `Planning → In Progress → Completed` (and back to `In Progress` via "Reopen").

**Use cases:**
- QA engineer creates "Sprint 42 Regression" run against the `staging` environment before a release, adds the approved regression suite, and starts executing.
- A tester reopens a "Completed" run after a late-breaking regression is discovered, to re-execute a subset of cases.
- A manager scans the Test Runs list, filters to "In Progress," and checks overall pass rate/open failures across all active runs.

**Problem it solves:** Separates the *definition* of what to test (test case repository) from a
*specific pass* at testing it (a run), so historical results per release/build are preserved even as
the underlying test case library evolves.

**Features & actions:**
- List runs (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/cycles`) — summary stat tiles (Total Runs / In Progress / Pass Rate / Open Failures), status filter chips (All/Planning/In Progress/Completed), sort (Newest/Oldest/Name/Status).
- Create run (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/cycles`) — Name (required), Description, **Environment (required, dropdown sourced from Project Settings' `testRunEnvironments`; create button disabled and a warning shown if none configured)**, Build Version (free text).
  - **`from-plan`** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/cycles/from-plan`) and **`from-cases`** (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/cycles/from-cases`) are distinct routes but both are wired to the *exact same* `createCycle()` service method — there is no server-side behavioral difference between "plain create," "from a plan," and "from selected cases." `from-cases` has **no frontend caller anywhere** in the codebase; it's reachable only via direct API/automation and, if invoked with `testcaseIds` in the body, silently ignores them (no cases get attached) since `createCycle` never reads that field.
- Edit run (`PATCH /api/cycles/:cycleId`) — name/description/environment (required)/build version. Also used internally for plan linking (`planId`/`clearPlan`) and status transitions.
- Delete run (`DELETE /api/cycles/:cycleId`) — confirm dialog warns "This will remove all associated test case executions. This action cannot be undone." Matches schema: `cycle_items` cascades from `cycles` (`ON DELETE CASCADE`), and `executions` cascades from `cycle_items` — a hard, unrecoverable delete of every execution result, attachment reference, and defect link tied to the run.
- **Run status lifecycle** — manual, button-driven, not automatically derived from completion %:
  - `Planning` → **Start Execution** → `In Progress`
  - `In Progress` → **Mark Completed** → `Completed`
  - `Completed` → **Reopen** → `In Progress`
  - The inline per-execution status dropdown only renders while the run is `In Progress`; in `Planning`/`Completed` the row shows a read-only status chip. **This gating is client-side only** — `PATCH /api/cycles/:cycleId/executions/:executionId` has no server-side check on the parent run's status, so a direct API call can still update execution results on a `Planning` or `Completed` run.
  - **Add Test Cases** button is hidden once `Completed`; **Remove case** action is likewise hidden once `Completed` (both client-side only — same caveat as above for the underlying endpoints).
- **Add Test Cases picker** (`POST /api/cycles/:cycleId/testcases`) — modal with search/priority/type/suite/status filters over the full project repository.
  - **Only test cases with status "Approved" are selectable** (checkbox disabled + row dimmed + tooltip "Only Approved test cases can be added to a test run..." for Draft/In Review/other statuses) — enforced client-side only; nothing stops adding a non-Approved case via direct `POST` to the endpoint.
  - Already-included cases (by `testcaseId`) are excluded from the picker list entirely.
  - Adding a case creates both a `cycle_items` row (snapshotting the current title) **and** a paired `executions` row defaulted to `Untested`, in the same request.
- **Remove case from run** (`DELETE /api/cycles/:cycleId/testcases/:testcaseId`) — hard-deletes the `cycle_items` row, which cascades to hard-delete its `executions` row too (bypassing the soft-delete columns `deleted_at`/`deleted_by` added for executions in `V60`) — i.e. removing a case from a run **permanently and irreversibly destroys that case's execution history for this run** (status, actual result, defect key/URL), not a soft-delete/archive.
- **Export CSV** (`GET /api/cycles/:cycleId/export/csv`) — plain link (`target="_blank"`), columns: `externalId, title, status, priority, type, actualResult, executedAt, defectKey, defectUrl`. Reuses the same `executions()` query as the in-app table (no dedicated report query), so it always reflects live data at click-time, and works even on very large runs (no pagination/limit).
- **Run detail meta row**: owner avatar, plan name/link (if any), environment, build version, duration (`startedAt`→`endedAt`/now, formatted `Xh Ym`), created date. Note: `startedAt`/`endedAt` are schema columns but **no code path in this module ever sets them** — they stay `null` forever via this UI (duration always renders `—`) unless populated by another module (e.g. automation).
- Runs switcher side panel — same collapsible/localStorage pattern as Plans, lets you jump between runs in-project without leaving the detail page.
- Run-level "Share" button opens the Public Share Links modal (see below).

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- Try to create a run when the project has zero configured environments — button is disabled; verify there's no way to bypass via Enter-key submit.
- Create a run, immediately delete it while its "Add Test Cases" modal is still open in another tab — verify the add-cases call fails gracefully (FK cascade already removed the cycle).
- Reopen a `Completed` run, verify `endedAt`-driven duration display doesn't misbehave (moot today since `endedAt` is never set by this module).
- Add the same test case to a run twice in rapid succession (double-click) — `cycle_items` has no explicit unique constraint on `(cycle_id, testcase_id)` visible in the base migration (only `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` is used when the *execution* insert races, implying reliance on some uniqueness — verify whether a duplicate `cycle_items` row can be created, producing two execution rows for one case in the same run).
- Call `POST /cycles/from-cases` directly with a `testcaseIds` array (as its name implies) — confirm it creates an **empty** run, silently dropping the cases; this is a real trap for anyone integrating against the documented-sounding route name.
- No auth/ownership check on `getCycle`/`listCycles`/`updateCycle`/`deleteCycle`/`addCycleTestCases`/`removeCycleTestCase` — same platform-wide IDOR gap as Plans (see Cross-Cutting section).
- No activity-log entries for run create/update/delete/case-add/case-remove — only execution status changes and attachment uploads are journaled.
- `GET /api/cycles/:cycleId/report/summary` (`cycleSummary()` in the controller) is a **hard-coded stub** returning `{ total: 0, passed: 0, failed: 0, blocked: 0, skipped: 0, untested: 0 }` regardless of the actual cycle — unused by the frontend (which computes its own stats client-side from `/executions`), but any external integration calling it will get permanently-zero data.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` L348–392 (`/cycles` list/create/from-plan/from-cases, `/cycles/:cycleId` get/update/delete, `/testcases` add/remove), L568–575 (`/export/csv`), L587–590 (`/report/summary` stub); `legacy.service.ts` L1676–1790 (`listCycles`, `createCycle`, `getCycle`, `updateCycle`, `deleteCycle`, `addCycleTestCases`, `removeCycleTestCase`).
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V3_plans_cycles_executions.sql` (`cycles`, `cycle_items`), `V9_cycle_status.sql` (`status` column), `V28_plan_cycle_external_ids.sql` (`external_id`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/page.tsx` (list + create/edit/delete modals), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx` (detail — 1876 lines: status lifecycle buttons, case picker, CSV export link, share modal trigger).
- API client: `lib/api.ts` L1391–1431 (`TestRunListItem`, `TestRunDetail`), L1548–1578 (`listTestRuns`, `getTestRun`, `createTestRun`, `updateTestRun`, `deleteTestRun`, `addTestCasesToRun`, `removeTestCaseFromRun`, `createCycleFromPlan`).

---

### Test Executions

**What it is:** The per-test-case result record within a run (`executions` table) — one row per
`cycle_item`, holding status, assignee, actual result notes, executed-at timestamp, and defect
key/URL. This is what testers actually update while "running" a test.

**Use cases:**
- A tester works through a run's test case list, marking each Passed/Failed/Blocked/Skipped and jotting an actual result.
- Marking a case "Failed" immediately prompts the tester to file (or link) a bug against it, capturing the defect key/URL on the execution.
- A tester opens the dedicated full-page "Execute" view for a single test case to read full steps/preconditions/test data before recording a result.

**Problem it solves:** Gives an auditable, per-case, per-run record of what was actually tested,
by whom, and what happened — the atomic unit all run/plan progress rollups are built from.

**Features & actions:**
- **Statuses**: `Untested` (default), `Passed`, `Failed`, `Skipped`, `Blocked`, `Retest` — six values, defined only as a frontend constant (`EXEC_STATUSES` / `STATUSES`) in two places (run detail page and the standalone execute page). **The DB column (`executions.status VARCHAR(32)`) has no `CHECK` constraint**, so any string is technically persistable via direct API call; the UI would then render it with a generic/neutral style since it isn't in the tone map.
- **Inline quick-toggle**: a `<select>` in the run's execution table (only while run is `In Progress`) lets a tester change status without opening any panel/drawer; disabled per-row while its own save request is in flight.
- **Full detail panel** (right-side `Drawer`, opened by clicking a case's title) — shows description/preconditions/test data/steps (parsed from JSON or plain text, tolerant of several shapes), current assignee (display-only), and lets you edit Status, Actual Result / Notes, Defect Key, Defect URL, then Save (`PATCH /api/cycles/:cycleId/executions/:executionId`).
- **Standalone full-page "Execute" view** (`/projects/:id/cycles/:cycleId/execute/:executionId`) — same status/actual-result/defect fields as the drawer, as a dedicated page (useful for deep-linking / larger screens); big colored status buttons instead of a dropdown.
- **Auto bug-filing on Failed**: changing status to `Failed` (via inline dropdown or the detail panel) automatically opens the "File a bug" dialog, pre-filled with a "Failed: <test case title>" draft title; the tester can create a new bug (optionally routed to Jira/Linear/self-logged/Tesbo-native, with file or BetterBugs evidence) or link the execution to an already-existing bug (`addBugLink`) instead of creating a duplicate. Can be skipped.
- **"Log bug" row action** — available on every row regardless of current status (magnifier/bug icon), not just after a Failed transition.
- **Assignee** — `assigneeId` is part of the execution record and is **displayed** (avatar + name) in both the table row and the detail drawer, but there is **no UI control anywhere to set or change it**. `updateExecution()`'s payload type supports `assigneeId`, yet neither the inline-status handler nor the drawer's Save handler ever sends it. In practice, an execution can only ever be assigned via a direct API call (or some other, out-of-scope, automation path) — there is no manual "assign to teammate" workflow in the product today.
- **Evidence attachments** — `POST /api/cycles/:cycleId/executions/:executionId/attachments` (multipart, up to 10 files, size-limited by `MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE`/50MB default) and `GET .../attachments` are fully implemented backend features (stores to `attachments` table with `entity_type='execution'`, logs a `execution_evidence_uploaded` activity entry) but have **zero frontend callers** — no `lib/api.ts` wrapper function exists for them and no component references them. Execution-level evidence upload/download is effectively a backend-only, UI-inaccessible feature today (bug evidence upload is the analogous feature that *does* have full UI, via the "File a bug" dialog).
- **Test case fallback rendering**: title falls back `snapshot_title → 'Untitled test case'`; if the underlying test case has since been archived/soft-deleted (`testcases.deleted_at`), the executions query's `LEFT JOIN ... AND t.deleted_at IS NULL` means priority/type/description/steps/etc. all render blank (`—`) even though the execution row itself still exists and is fully editable.
- Tabs on the run detail table: All / Passed / Failed / Blocked / Skipped / Pending (Pending buckets both `Untested` and `Retest`), each with a live count badge; free-text search by title/external ID; client-side pagination (10/page).

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- PATCH an execution's status to an arbitrary non-enum string via direct API (e.g. `"WontFix"`) — persists with no server-side validation; confirm how the UI renders an unrecognized status (falls through to the default/neutral tone).
- Update an execution on a run that is `Planning` or `Completed` via direct API — succeeds despite the UI hiding the control, since there is no server-side run-status gate.
- Set `assigneeId` via direct API to a user who has since been removed from the project/workspace — the UI's `memberNames` lookup (built from current project members) would silently show "Unassigned" instead of erroring, since it can't resolve the stale ID.
- Mark Failed → open bug dialog → close/skip without filing — execution stays `Failed` with no bug link; re-opening later and clicking "Log bug" should still work.
- Remove a test case from the run (hard-deletes its execution) after evidence attachments were uploaded to that execution via direct API — the `attachments` row (`entity_type='execution', entity_id=<deleted execution id>`) is **not cleaned up** (no FK/cascade — `attachments.entity_id` is a bare UUID, not a foreign key), leaving an orphaned DB row and orphaned file in storage.
- Upload 11 files in one request to the attachments endpoint — `FilesInterceptor("files", 10, ...)` caps at 10; verify the resulting error is a clean 4xx.
- Upload a file at/over the `MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE` limit — verify graceful rejection vs. a raw multipart error.
- Two testers editing the same execution's detail panel simultaneously — last `PATCH` wins, no optimistic-concurrency check (no version/updated_at comparison).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` L393–417 (`/executions` list, `/executions/:executionId` update, attachments upload/list); `legacy.service.ts` L1792–1836 (`executions`, `updateExecution`), L2040–2079 (`uploadExecutionAttachments`, `listExecutionAttachments`).
- Schema: `V3_plans_cycles_executions.sql` (`executions` table), `V60_executions_soft_delete_and_actors.sql` (`executed_by`, `deleted_at`/`deleted_by`, assignee repointed to `actors`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx` (inline status select L1170–1186, detail drawer L1727+, bug-filing dialog logic L558–697), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/execute/[executionId]/page.tsx` (standalone execute page).
- API client: `lib/api.ts` L1433–1457 (`ExecutionItem`), L1580–1586 (`listCycleExecutions`, `updateExecution`).

---

### Bulk Execution Actions

**What it is:** Two REST routes intended for bulk-assigning executions to a user and bulk-setting
execution status across multiple executions at once.

**Use cases (intended, not delivered):**
- A test lead wants to assign all "Untested" cases in a run to two testers in one action.
- A tester wants to mark 20 already-verified-fixed cases as "Passed" in one batch instead of one at a time.

**Problem it solves:** Nothing today — see below.

**Features & actions:**
- `POST /api/cycles/:cycleId/executions/bulk-assign` — controller handler is a **completely empty method body** (`bulkAssign() {}`), with no parameters bound at all (not even `@Body()`); it returns `undefined` (HTTP 200 with an empty response) no matter what is sent.
- `POST /api/cycles/:cycleId/executions/bulk-status` — identical situation (`bulkStatus() {}`).
- **No frontend caller exists for either route** — no function in `lib/api.ts`, no component references `bulk-assign`/`bulk-status` anywhere in the frontend tree. There is also no bulk-selection UI (checkboxes, "select all," a bulk action bar) anywhere on the run detail execution table — the checkbox/multi-select pattern that exists for bulk test-case operations (status/suite/priority/owner and delete) on the **Test Cases** repository page has no equivalent on the **Test Executions** table.
- Net effect: this is a fully unimplemented feature end-to-end (no UI, no backend logic, no persistence) — currently indistinguishable from a no-op API if called directly.

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- Confirm both routes currently return 200/empty for literally any payload (including malformed JSON, missing `cycleId`, or a `cycleId` that doesn't exist) — there is no validation to trigger a 4xx.
- Regression-test that whenever this is implemented, it gets standard coverage: assigning to a user not on the project, assigning to an empty list, bulk-status to an invalid status string, bulk actions on a `Completed` run, and permission gating consistent with the single-execution update path.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` L419–423 (`bulkAssign`, `bulkStatus` — both empty stub bodies). No corresponding methods exist in `legacy.service.ts`.
- Frontend: none (no caller, no bulk UI on `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx`).

---

### Recurring Run Scheduling

**What it is:** A dedicated "Schedule Test Run" page where a user can define a one-time or
recurring reminder/trigger tied to a specific run, with a fully-designed backing DB table
(`cycle_run_schedules`) — but the controller endpoints backing it are **disconnected stubs that
never touch that table.**

**Use cases (intended by the schema/UI, not actually delivered):**
- Schedule a nightly smoke-test run reminder every 1440 minutes (24h).
- Schedule a one-time run for a specific release date/time in a given timezone.
- Disable a schedule temporarily without deleting it; see when it last ran and whether it errored.

**Problem it solves:** Nothing today in production — the feature is fully modeled in the database
and fully built in the UI, but the API layer connecting them is stubbed out, so **nothing persists**.

**Features & actions (as built in the UI, none of which actually work end-to-end):**
- Schedule form: Name, Test Run (dropdown of the project's runs), Schedule Type (One-time / Recurring), Timezone (free text, default `"UTC"`), and conditionally either "Run At" (datetime-local) or "Interval Minutes" (numeric, default `1440`).
- Schedule list table: Name, Run, Type ("One-time" or "Every {n}m"), Next Run, Last Status, Enable/Disable toggle, Delete — plus a `lastError` message shown under the row if present.
- **Backend reality**:
  - `GET /api/projects/:projectId/cycles/schedules` → `schedules() { return []; }` — **always returns an empty array**, ignoring `projectId` entirely.
  - `POST /api/projects/:projectId/cycles/schedules` → `createSchedule(@Body() body) { return { id: "local-schedule", ...body }; }` — returns a fake object with a **hard-coded, non-unique id `"local-schedule"`** and never writes to the database. The UI's "New Schedule" form will appear to succeed (the promise resolves) and then immediately call `load()`, which re-fetches the (always-empty) list — **so a freshly created schedule vanishes from the table the instant it's created.**
  - `PATCH /api/cycles/schedules/:scheduleId` → `updateSchedule() {}` and `DELETE /api/cycles/schedules/:scheduleId` → `deleteSchedule() {}` — both are literal no-ops (empty method bodies, no params bound), returning 200/empty regardless of input.
  - The real table backing this, `cycle_run_schedules`, has non-trivial, correctly-designed constraints that nothing ever exercises: `schedule_type IN ('one_time','recurring')`, and a `CHECK` requiring `run_at IS NOT NULL` for one-time schedules and `interval_minutes IS NOT NULL AND interval_minutes > 0` for recurring ones. There is also no scheduler/cron worker anywhere in the backend that would actually *execute* a due schedule even if rows existed.
- Net effect: this entire feature (nightly/one-time run scheduling) is **non-functional** in the current codebase — worth explicit regression coverage confirming it stays visibly broken (or is fixed) rather than silently trusted.

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- Create a schedule, confirm it disappears from the list on next load (documenting the current broken state) — this should be the primary regression test until the feature is wired up.
- Submit the create form with `scheduleType="recurring"` and `intervalMinutes=0` or negative — client `<input min={1}>` discourages it, but nothing server-side would reject it today anyway since the endpoint ignores the body.
- Submit `scheduleType="one_time"` with no `runAt` — client has `required` on the datetime input; verify behavior of `new Date("").toISOString()` (produces `Invalid Date` → `"Invalid Date"` string) if a user bypasses the required attribute.
- Toggle Enable/Disable and Delete on a schedule — both currently no-ops; confirm the UI doesn't falsely indicate success (it calls `load()` after, so the empty list will make the row disappear either way, masking the fact the underlying action did nothing).
- Once implemented: verify a schedule's `cycleId` pointing at a deleted run is handled (FK is `ON DELETE CASCADE` at the DB level, so the schedule row would vanish with the run — confirm the "no scheduler" gap doesn't turn into a crash when a worker is eventually added).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` L430–444 (`schedules`, `createSchedule`, `updateSchedule`, `deleteSchedule` — all stubs).
- Schema (unused): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V21_cycle_run_schedules.sql` (`cycle_run_schedules` table, full constraint set).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/schedule/page.tsx` (complete CRUD UI against the stub endpoints).
- API client: `lib/api.ts` L1524–1546 (`TestRunSchedule` type), L1612–1651 (`listTestRunSchedules`, `createTestRunSchedule`, `updateTestRunSchedule`, `deleteTestRunSchedule`).

---

### Public Share Links

**What it is:** A per-run toggle that generates a public, token-based URL (`/share/:token`)
displaying that run's results with no authentication required.

**Use cases:**
- A QA lead shares a live regression run's results with a client/stakeholder who has no Tesbo account.
- A team posts a shareable link in a release-readiness Slack thread.

**Problem it solves:** Lets non-users view run status without provisioning accounts or exposing the
full authenticated app.

**Features & actions:**
- **Enable/disable toggle** (`POST /api/cycles/:cycleId/share { enabled }`) in a "Share Test Run" modal, opened via the Share button on the run detail page's top bar.
  - Enabling for the first time generates a new random token (`randomBytes(24).toString("hex")`, i.e. a 48-hex-char token) and persists `share_enabled=true, share_token=<token>`.
  - **Disabling does not clear or rotate the token** — the service only ever generates a token when the existing one is empty (`existing.rows[0].share_token || randomBytes(...)`); re-enabling later reuses the exact same token/URL. There is **no "regenerate link" action anywhere** — the only way to invalidate a previously-shared URL for good is disabling (which itself doesn't revoke the token, just gates it) and never re-enabling with that same cycle, or intervening directly in the database.
- **Copy link** button (clipboard API with an `execCommand` fallback for browsers without clipboard permission), 2-second "Copied" confirmation state.
- Warning copy in the modal: "This link is publicly accessible. Anyone with it can view the test run results, execution statuses, and test case details."
- **Public viewer page** (`/share/:token`, no auth) — fetches `GET /api/public/shared-runs/:token` (run header: name/description/status/environment/build/created/started/ended) and `GET /api/public/shared-runs/:token/executions` (full execution list) in parallel.
  - Renders: run title + status badge, 5 metric cards (Total/Passed/Failed/Skipped/Pending — note Blocked is *not* one of the metric cards even though it's tracked and shown in the donut chart), an SVG donut chart, and a table of Test Case ID / Title / Priority / Type / Status.
  - Any failure (disabled share, unknown token) shows a generic "Link Not Available" screen — no distinction in the UI between "token never existed" and "sharing was turned off," which matches the backend (`publicCycle`/`publicCycleExecutions` both throw the same `NotFoundException({ error: "Shared run not found" })` for either case, via `WHERE share_token = $1 AND share_enabled = true`).
- **Access control note — the public executions endpoint returns materially more data than the public page renders.** `getPublicSharedExecutions`/`publicCycleExecutions` calls the *exact same* `executions()` query used inside the authenticated app, which includes `assigneeId`, `actualResult`, `executedAt`, `defectKey`, `defectUrl`, `description`, `preconditions`, `postconditions`, `steps`, `testData`, `automationStatus`, `automationTags` — none of that is filtered or redacted before being returned to an anonymous caller. The rendered `/share/:token` page only displays ID/title/priority/type/status, but anyone can call the JSON endpoint directly (e.g. via curl/devtools network tab) and read the full actual-result text, defect key/URL, assignee's raw user ID, and complete test steps/preconditions/test data for every case in the run. This is a meaningful over-exposure risk for any org that considers actual-result notes or defect links sensitive, since the sharing UI's copy ("view...execution statuses and test case details") doesn't disclose that defect/assignee/full-step data is also reachable.
- `publicCycle()` similarly returns the *entire* `cycles` row (`SELECT *`) including `project_id`, `plan_id`, `owner_id` (raw UUIDs) — internal identifiers leaked to an anonymous caller, beyond what the public page renders.

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- Disable sharing, then hit a previously-copied `/share/:token` URL — should show "Link Not Available" (confirmed by the `share_enabled = true` predicate).
- Re-enable sharing after having disabled it — confirm the URL becomes valid again with the **same** token as before (i.e., anyone who saved the "revoked" link regains access the moment it's re-enabled — there's no revocation, only pausing).
- Hit `GET /api/public/shared-runs/:token/executions` directly (bypassing the rendered page) and confirm the full field set (defect key/URL, actual result, assignee id, steps) is present in the JSON — a concrete finding to log/track, not just a theoretical one.
- Guess/brute-force a token — 48 hex chars (192 bits) is not practically guessable, but confirm there's no rate limiting on the public endpoints that would allow enumeration-adjacent abuse (e.g. hammering many token guesses).
- Delete the underlying test run while its share link is enabled — cascading delete removes the `cycles` row entirely, so the public link should cleanly 404 rather than error.
- Share a run with zero test cases — public page should render the empty-state "No test cases in this test run." without errors in the donut chart (already guards `total === 0`).
- No auth/membership check gates *toggling* sharing either — `shareCycle()` never calls `requireProjectAccess`; combined with the cross-cutting IDOR gap (below), any logged-in platform user could enable public sharing on a run belonging to a project they aren't a member of, purely by knowing/guessing its `cycleId`.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` L425–428 (`/cycles/:cycleId/share`), L446–454 (`/public/shared-runs/:token`, `/token/executions`); `legacy.service.ts` L1720–1745 (`shareCycle`, `publicCycle`, `publicCycleExecutions`).
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V10_cycle_share.sql` (`share_token`, `share_enabled` columns + index).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx` (Share modal, L884–887 trigger, L1631–1725 modal body), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/share/[token]/page.tsx` (public viewer).
- API client: `lib/api.ts` L1653–1669 (`ShareState`, `toggleTestRunShare`, `getPublicSharedRun`, `getPublicSharedExecutions`).

---

### Requirements Traceability

**What it is:** Two related but separate surfaces: (1) a **Requirements page** that imports Jira/Linear
tickets as "requirements" and tracks whether each has at least one linked test case ("coverage"),
with an AI ("Zyra") action to auto-generate test cases from a ticket; and (2) a **Traceability Matrix**
report (`components/reports/TraceabilityTab.tsx`, under Reports, not under the Requirements page)
that shows, per test case, every run/execution/linked-bug row.

**Use cases:**
- A QA lead checks which Jira stories in the current sprint have zero linked test cases ("uncovered") before sign-off.
- A tester clicks "Assign to Zyra" on an uncovered Jira ticket to auto-generate a first pass of test cases from its description.
- An auditor opens the Traceability Matrix to see, for a given test case, every run it's ever been executed in and any bug it's linked to, for release sign-off evidence.

**Problem it solves:** Answers "is this requirement tested?" (Requirements page, ticket-level) and
"where/when was this test case run, and what happened?" (Traceability Matrix, case-level) — but note
the two are **not the same "requirement"**: the Traceability Matrix has no concept of Jira/Linear
tickets at all; its "requirement" is really just the test case's own `external_id`.

**Features & actions:**
- **Requirements page** (`/projects/:id/requirements`):
  - Source tabs: All Sources / Jira / Linear, each with a live ticket count badge from `GET /api/projects/:projectId/tickets/summary`.
  - Stat strip: Total / Covered / Uncovered / Coverage % (progress bar) per selected source.
    - **"Covered" means "at least one non-deleted test case in the project has this exact ticket key recorded against it"** (`EXISTS` correlated subquery matching `jira_issue_key`/`linear_issue_key`) — it does **not** consider whether that linked test case has ever been run, or whether it's passing. A ticket with one `Draft`-status, never-executed, linked test case still counts as fully "covered."
  - **Sync** button — pulls fresh tickets from Jira and/or Linear (per active tab) via `syncJiraTickets`/`syncLinearTickets`; disabled while a connection isn't established (shows a "Connect Jira or Linear to Get Started" empty state linking to Project Settings → Integrations otherwise).
  - Search (key/summary), filters: Issue Type, Status (both populated from the distinct values actually present), Coverage (All/Covered/Uncovered).
  - Expandable row (click anywhere on the row) reveals full description, reporter, labels, created/updated dates, and an "Open in Jira/Linear" external link.
  - Per-ticket "coverage" badge shows linked test-case count (`N saved`) and a **"View testcases"** deep link into the Test Cases repository pre-filtered by `jiraIssueKey`/`linearIssueKey`.
  - **"Assign to Zyra" / "Regenerate with Zyra"** — creates an AI agent task (`createZyraTask`) to generate (or regenerate, updating existing + adding new) test cases from the ticket's summary/description/status/priority, tagging generated cases for traceability; navigates to the Agents/Tasks page to track progress. (Zyra task execution itself is out of this section's scope.)
- **Traceability Matrix** (Reports → Traceability tab, lazy-loaded only when that tab is first opened):
  - One row per (test case × run × bug) combination, **grouped/row-spanned by test case** so each case's ID/Title/Priority/Status/Suite is shown once with its runs listed beneath.
  - Per-run-row columns: Run name, Result (execution status chip), Executed date, linked Bug (title, hyperlinked to `bugUrl` if present).
  - Free-text search across external ID, test case title, run name, and bug title.
  - Resizable columns (drag handles, in-memory only — widths reset on reload).
  - A test case with **no runs at all** still needs to appear somewhere for true "uncovered by execution" visibility — but the underlying query is a `LEFT JOIN` from `testcases`, so cases with zero cycle/execution/bug history do appear as a single row with blank Run/Result/Executed/Bug cells (worth confirming visually, since the grouping-by-`testcaseId` logic assumes at least one row per group, which a pure `LEFT JOIN` guarantees even at zero matches).

**Edge cases / validation worth testing:**
- A test case has `jiraIssueKey` set but the Jira ticket that key refers to was never synced (or was deleted upstream) — the "coverage" count still increments (it's a pure string-match against `jira_tickets`/`linear_tickets`, no cross-check that the ticket the count is computed from actually corresponds to a *currently valid* ticket besides its presence in the synced cache).
- A test case is archived/soft-deleted after being linked to a ticket — `requirementsSummary`'s subquery filters `t.deleted_at IS NULL`, so the ticket correctly flips back to "uncovered"; confirm the Requirements page reflects this after the next load (no live push).
- Disconnect Jira/Linear after tickets were already synced — the Requirements page should still show previously-synced tickets (data isn't purged on disconnect) but Sync/Manage actions should reflect disconnected state.
- Traceability Matrix on a project with zero test cases — confirm "No test case data available" empty state, not a blank table.
- Search the Traceability Matrix for a bug title on a case with multiple runs — only the matching run-row survives filtering, but the grouping/rowSpan logic recalculates per filtered set, so verify the case's ID/Title cells still rowSpan correctly across the *filtered* run count (not the original).
- No auth/ownership check on `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/requirement-matrix` or `/tickets/summary` either (`requirementMatrix`/`requirementsSummary` take a bare `projectId` with no `requireProjectAccess` call) — same cross-cutting gap as everything else in this document.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` L597–600 (`/reports/requirement-matrix`), L1119–1127 (`/tickets/summary`, `/tickets`); `legacy.service.ts` L2168–2198 (`requirementMatrix`), L4910–4944 (`requirementsSummary`).
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/requirements/page.tsx` (Jira/Linear requirements list + coverage stats + Zyra actions), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/reports/page.tsx` (hosts the Traceability tab, lazy-loads on first visit), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/TraceabilityTab.tsx` (matrix table, grouping, resizable columns).
- API client: `lib/api.ts` L1860–1880 (`RequirementMatrixRow`, `getRequirementMatrix`), plus `getRequirementsSummary`, `listAllTickets`/`listJiraTickets`/`listLinearTickets`, `listLinkedJiraKeys`/`listLinkedLinearKeys`.

---

### Cross-Cutting Notes (Access Control & Data Integrity)

**What it is:** Structural observations that apply across *every* feature above, because they live in
shared middleware/service patterns rather than any single route.

**Use cases:** N/A — these are platform-level risks that should seed security- and data-integrity-focused test cases across all of the features above, not a user-facing capability of their own.

**Problem it solves:** N/A (this documents gaps, not a delivered capability).

**Features & actions (i.e., what to specifically verify):**
- **Authentication is "resolve if present," not "enforce."** `AuthMiddleware` (`Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts`) sets `req.userId = null` when there's no valid session/bearer token and always calls `next()` — it never blocks a request. Enforcement is left entirely to individual service methods calling a `requireUser()` helper (throws 400 "Authentication required" if `userId` is falsy).
- **Project-membership enforcement is inconsistent within this module.** The codebase does have a correct, reusable pattern for it — `requireProjectAccess(userId, projectId)` (`legacy.service.ts` L1163–1174) checks the caller is a member of the project **and** that the project belongs to their currently-active workspace/organization — but it is used elsewhere in the codebase (e.g. `getProjectForUser`) and is **never called by any of the Plans/Cycles/Executions/Requirements methods reviewed for this section**: `listPlans`, `createPlan`, `getPlan`, `updatePlan`, `deletePlan`, `planItems`, `addPlanItem`, `deletePlanItem`, `planRuns`, `planProgress`, `listCycles`, `createCycle`, `getCycle`, `updateCycle`, `deleteCycle`, `addCycleTestCases`, `removeCycleTestCase`, `executions`, `shareCycle`, `requirementMatrix`, `requirementsSummary` — none of them check that the caller belongs to the project/plan/cycle they're addressing. `updateExecution` and `uploadExecutionAttachments` go one step further than the rest (calling `requireUser`, so at least *some* valid session is required) but still never verify the execution's parent cycle/project is one the caller has access to.
- **Practical consequence to test:** with any two valid logged-in accounts on *different* projects/organizations, confirm whether User A can `GET`/`PATCH`/`DELETE` a `planId`/`cycleId`/`executionId` that belongs to User B's project, purely by supplying the UUID (e.g., obtained from a shared screenshot, a leaked URL, or straightforward enumeration if IDs are ever sequential/discoverable elsewhere). This is the single highest-value security regression test to add for this entire module.
- **No audit trail for structural changes.** `logProjectActivity(...)` is only ever called from `updateExecution` and `uploadExecutionAttachments` in this module — creating/editing/deleting a Plan or a Cycle, adding/removing a test case from a run, and toggling public sharing all leave **no trace** in the project's Activity feed. Only "someone changed an execution's status/result" and "someone uploaded execution evidence" are recorded.
- **Soft-delete inconsistency for archived test cases.** `executions()` (cycle detail) explicitly joins `testcases` with `AND t.deleted_at IS NULL`, blanking priority/type/etc. for archived cases, while `planItems()` joins with no such filter and continues showing full details for the same archived case. Confirm this is intentional (it doesn't appear to be) when writing test cases around test-case archival interacting with plans vs. runs.

**Key files:**
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts` (session/bearer resolution, never blocks).
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` L358–361 (`requireUser`), L1163–1178 (`requireProjectAccess`, `getProjectForUser` — the *correct* pattern, unused by this module's routes).
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` — compare route signatures across the module: routes taking `@Req() req: AuthenticatedRequest` (rare, e.g. `updateExecution`, `uploadExecutionAttachments`, `bulkUpdateTestCases`) vs. the majority that only bind `@Param`/`@Body` and never see the request/user at all.

---

## Section D — Bugs / Defect Tracking

Scope: the standalone bug/defect tracker at `/projects/:id/bugs`, its linkage to test
cases/runs/executions, its attachment/evidence system, and its touch-points with
execution status changes, the dashboard, and reports. Cross-references to Requirements/
Reports/Jira-Linear-sync internals are noted only where the Bugs module's own behavior
depends on them; those modules are otherwise out of scope.

### Bug Reporting & Lifecycle Management

**What it is:** A lightweight, per-project defect tracker — bugs are simple records with a
title, free-text description, severity, status, and optional links back to the test
artifacts that surfaced them. There is no separate "priority" field, no assignee, no
structured "steps to reproduce"/"environment" fields, and no comment/activity thread — the
description textarea is the only place that information can live.

**Use cases:**
- A QA engineer manually files a bug from the "Bugs" page after noticing a problem outside of any specific test run.
- A tester triages the open bug backlog, changes status as fixes land, and reopens bugs that regress.
- A project lead reviews severity distribution to prioritize the next sprint.
- An automation client (via the Tesbo MCP server) files a bug programmatically after a CI run.

**Problem it solves:** Gives a project a single place to record defects discovered during
testing, independent of (but connectable to) the test-case/test-run hierarchy, without
requiring a full external issue tracker.

**Features & actions:**
- Create a bug (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/bugs`): title (required; server defaults to `"Untitled bug"` if blank/omitted — the *frontend* blocks empty titles, the API does not), description, severity, links array (see Bug Linking section), `externalUrl`/`integrationProvider`/`integrationIssueKey` (external-tracker reference), `betterbugsUrl` (evidence link). `reported_by` is set to the authenticated caller automatically (or the API token's owning user for MCP calls); `status` defaults to `"Open"`.
- List bugs for a project (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/bugs`), newest first; supports optional `status` and `cycleId` query filters server-side — **note: no frontend caller ever passes these**, so they are only reachable via direct API/MCP use, not through the UI.
- Get a single bug (`GET /api/bugs/:bugId`) — returns the bug plus its resolved `links` (with joined test case/run titles) and `attachments`.
- Update a bug (`PATCH /api/bugs/:bugId`) — partial update of title/description/status/severity/externalUrl/integrationProvider/integrationIssueKey/betterbugsUrl/links.
- Delete a bug (`DELETE /api/bugs/:bugId`) — hard delete, no confirmation server-side (UI has a confirm modal).
- Severity: `Critical | High | Medium | Low`, DB-enforced via a CHECK constraint (`bugs_severity_check`), default `Medium`.
- Status: free text at the DB layer (**no CHECK constraint**) but the UI only ever writes/reads four values: `Open | In Progress | Reopened | Closed`.
