- Reporter metadata: `reportedBy` (user id), `reporterName`/`reporterEmail` resolved via join to `users`; not editable after creation.

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- Creating a bug with an empty/whitespace-only title via direct API call (bypassing the frontend's disabled-button guard) — the bug is created titled `"Untitled bug"` rather than being rejected.
- Sending an invalid `severity` value (e.g. `"Urgent"`) directly to the API — this is **not validated in the service layer**, so it fails at the DB CHECK constraint and surfaces as an unhandled 500-style DB error rather than a clean validation message.
- Setting `status` to an arbitrary string (e.g. `"Won't Fix"`) via direct API/PATCH — accepted silently (no DB constraint), but then the bug **disappears from every Kanban column** (columns are hard-coded to the 4 known statuses) and cannot be selected via the List-view status filter dropdown (also hard-coded to the 4 values); it only remains visible under "All Statuses" in list view.
- **Clearing a previously-set field never works**: `updateBug` builds its SQL with `COALESCE($n, column)` and the controller/service pass `body.field || null` for `description`, `externalUrl`, `integrationProvider`, `integrationIssueKey`, and `betterbugsUrl`. Sending an empty string (or explicit `null`) for any of these is indistinguishable from "not provided," so `COALESCE` keeps the **old** value. Concretely: editing a bug, blanking out the Description textarea, and saving does **not** clear the description — the previous text persists. Same for unlinking an external ticket URL or switching evidence mode away from BetterBugs (see Evidence section) — these fields can only ever be overwritten with another non-empty value, never cleared.
- Deleting a bug does **not** clean up its attachments: `deleteBug` only issues `DELETE FROM bugs WHERE id = $1`. The generic `attachments` table has no FK to `bugs` (it's a polymorphic `entity_type`/`entity_id` pair), so rows referencing the deleted bug — and the underlying files in storage — are orphaned indefinitely (storage leak). Worth testing explicitly: create a bug, attach a file, delete the bug, confirm the file/row still exist.
- No role/permission gating on any bug endpoint: the controller methods for get/update/delete/link/attachment routes never call the app's `requireUser`-style check and there is no project-membership check either (confirmed no `@UseGuards`/role decorators on these routes, and `AuthMiddleware` only *resolves* `req.userId`, it never blocks the request). Any caller who can reach the API and knows/guesses a `bugId` (or `attachmentId`) — regardless of which project or organization they belong to — can view, edit, delete it, or add/remove its links and attachments. Worth testing as an authorization/IDOR case: user from Project B (or an unauthenticated request, since `userId` can be `null`) hitting `GET/PATCH/DELETE /api/bugs/:bugId` for a bug in Project A.
- Deleting a **test case** that is hard-deleted (e.g. via "delete suite → delete test cases" bulk mode) cascades and removes the corresponding `bug_links` row entirely (`ON DELETE CASCADE` on `testcase_id`). Deleting a **test run (cycle)** instead just nulls out that link's `cycle_id`/`execution_id` (`ON DELETE SET NULL`) — the bug stays linked to the test case but loses which run/execution surfaced it. Both are worth testing explicitly, since the resulting bug-link states differ.
- A bug linked to a soft-deleted/archived test case (not hard-deleted) continues to resolve and display its title/external id correctly in the bug's link list, since the join has no `deleted_at` filter.

**Key files:**
- Backend routes: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:456-479` (`GET/POST /api/projects/:projectId/bugs`, `GET/PATCH/DELETE /api/bugs/:bugId`)
- Backend logic: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `bugSelect` (1838), `listBugs` (1873), `createBug` (1903), `getBug` (1936), `updateBug` (1943), `deleteBug` (1981)
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V11_bugs.sql`, `V67_bug_severity.sql`, `V48_bug_links.sql` (adds `integration_provider`/`integration_issue_key`), `V49_bug_evidence.sql` (adds `betterbugs_url`)
- Auth (no per-route guard confirmed): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts`
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/bugs/page.tsx` (create/edit/view/delete modals, ~lines 348-1257)
- API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1675-1796` (`BugItem`, `BugLink`, `listBugs`/`createBug`/`updateBug`/`deleteBug`)
- MCP automation surface: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.tools.ts:171-193` (`create_bug` tool, write-scope only; no update/delete/list bug tools exist)

---

### Bug Linking (Test Cases, Test Runs & Executions)

**What it is:** A many-to-many join (`bug_links`) between a bug and the test case /
test run (cycle) / execution combinations it affects, so one defect can be traced across
every failing execution it caused. This is **not** a link to other bugs, and not a synced
link to an external ticket — those are separate fields (`externalUrl`,
`integrationProvider`/`integrationIssueKey`, covered below).

**Use cases:**
- Tester links a newly-reported bug to the specific test case + run where it was found, so anyone viewing that test case's history can see the associated defect.
- The same underlying defect breaks multiple test cases (or the same test case across multiple runs) — a tester links all of them to a single bug record instead of filing duplicates.
- A PM reviews a bug's detail and jumps straight to the linked test case/run for context.

**Problem it solves:** Connects defects to the specific evidence (which test, which run,
which execution) that proves the defect exists, enabling backtrace/traceability reporting
and preventing duplicate bug filings for the same underlying failure.

**Features & actions:**
- Each link row stores `testcaseId`, `cycleId`, and (optionally) `executionId`; unique on `(bug_id, testcase_id, cycle_id)`.
- `POST /api/bugs/:bugId/links` (`addBugLink`) — adds a single link to an existing bug. Requires **at least one of** `testcaseId` or `cycleId` (400 `"testcaseId or cycleId is required."` otherwise); `executionId` alone is not accepted as a standalone link.
- `DELETE /api/bugs/:bugId/links/:linkId` (`removeBugLink`) — removes a single link row. **This endpoint exists in the API client (`removeBugLink` in `lib/api.ts`) but has no button/UI wired to it anywhere in the app** — the only way to drop a link from the main Bugs page is to edit the bug, remove the row from the `TestCaseRunPicker` list, and Save (which does a full-array replace via `PATCH .../bugs/:bugId`, not the per-link DELETE route).
- Editing a bug's links via the main Bugs page always replaces the **entire** link set (`replaceBugLinks`: deletes all existing links for the bug, then re-inserts the array sent in the PATCH body) — there is no incremental "add one more link without touching the others" affordance in that UI (only the Failed-execution dialog's "link an existing bug" flow uses the incremental `addBugLink` endpoint).
- The link picker (`TestCaseRunPicker`) requires selecting **both** a test run and a test case/execution within it before "+ Add link" is enabled; it always attaches `executionId` alongside `testcaseId`/`cycleId` when adding via this UI.
- Reporting a bug when the project has **no test runs at all**: the link field is optional and shows a note ("this bug will be reported unlinked"); Report/Save buttons stay enabled.
- Reporting a bug when the project **does** have test runs: at least one link becomes mandatory in the UI (Report/Save button disabled without one) — but this is a **frontend-only** rule; the backend accepts an empty `links` array unconditionally regardless of whether the project has runs.

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- Adding the exact same `(testcaseId, cycleId)` combination twice (`ON CONFLICT ... DO NOTHING`) is a silent no-op — including when the second attempt carries a **different** `executionId`; the originally-stored `execution_id` is not updated to the new one.
- Attempting to add a link with neither `testcaseId` nor `cycleId` set → 400 error.
- Removing a link by an id that doesn't exist (or already removed) → 200 success, no-op (no existence check before the DELETE).
- Removing the only link on a bug leaves it with `links: []` — no back-fill to the legacy `bugs.testcase_id`/`cycle_id`/`execution_id` convenience columns (those were only populated at creation time from the first link and are not kept in sync afterward).
- Requirement/Traceability Matrix and the MCP `get_requirement_matrix` tool join bugs to executions via the **legacy single-column** `bugs.execution_id` field (`requirementMatrix` query: `LEFT JOIN bugs b ON b.execution_id = e.id`), **not** the `bug_links` table that is the actual source of truth for the bug's own detail view. Practical effect: file a bug from Execution A's failure (auto-populates `bugs.execution_id`), then later link that same bug to Execution B's failure via "Link an existing bug" (only inserts a `bug_links` row) — the bug will show correctly on the bug's own page for both executions, but the **Traceability Matrix will only ever show it against Execution A**, never B. Good concrete test: verify a multi-linked bug's visibility gap between the Bugs page and the Traceability report.

**Key files:**
- Backend routes: `legacy.controller.ts:481-489` (`POST /api/bugs/:bugId/links`, `DELETE /api/bugs/:bugId/links/:linkId`)
- Backend logic: `legacy.service.ts` — `replaceBugLinks` (1892), `addBugLink` (1966), `removeBugLink` (1976), `requirementMatrix` (2168, bug join at 2192)
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V48_bug_links.sql`
- Frontend link picker: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/TestCaseRunPicker.tsx`
- Frontend usage: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/bugs/page.tsx` (create/edit modals), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx:682-693` (`handleLinkExistingBug`)

---

### Auto Bug-Filing on Failed Test Execution

**What it is:** When a tester marks a test execution as **Failed** (via the inline status
button on the Test Run detail page, or via the execution side-panel's status picker +
Save), a "Report a Bug" dialog opens automatically, prefilled with a title derived from
the test case. The same dialog can also be opened manually at any time via a "Log bug"
icon/button, regardless of the execution's current status.

**Use cases:**
- A tester fails a test case during a run and is immediately prompted to log the defect without navigating away, reducing missed/forgotten bug reports.
- The defect for this failure was already logged (by this tester or someone else) — instead of creating a duplicate, the tester links the failing execution to the existing bug.
- The team tracks defects in Jira/Linear rather than in Tesbo — the dialog lets the tester note that instead of forcing a Tesbo-native bug.
- A tester wants to log a bug against a test case that hasn't failed yet (e.g. a bug found incidentally while executing) — the "Log bug" row/panel action is available for any status.

**Problem it solves:** Closes the loop between "test failed" and "defect filed" at the
moment of discovery, and offers a way to avoid duplicate bug records for the same
underlying failure across multiple test cases/runs.

**Features & actions:**
- Triggers: (1) changing a row's inline status dropdown to "Failed"; (2) opening the execution detail panel, changing status to "Failed" (only when it **wasn't already** Failed) and clicking Save; (3) clicking the bug icon in a run's row actions (title "Log bug") — available for any execution status, not just Failed; (4) clicking "Log bug" in the execution detail panel footer.
- Dialog banner shows which test case failed (external id + title).
- "Is this defect already logged?" toggle: **No, log a new one** vs **Yes, link existing**.
- **New bug** path: title (prefilled `"Failed: <test case title>"`, editable), description, evidence (files or BetterBugs link — see next section), and — only when Jira/Linear is connected for the project — a "Where should this be tracked?" choice (Tesbo vs "I'll log it in my task management system myself"), mirroring the main Bugs page create flow. Submitting calls `createBug` with `links: [{ testcaseId, cycleId, executionId }]` for the failing execution.
- **Link existing** path, sub-choice of destination:
  - **Existing Tesbo bug** — opens `ExistingBugPickerModal` (search project bugs by title), then "Link Bug" calls `addBugLink(existingBugId, { testcaseId, cycleId, executionId })` for the current failing execution.
  - **Jira ticket / Linear ticket** (only shown if that integration is connected) — opens `IssuePickerModal`, which live-searches Jira/Linear issues (`searchJiraIssuesLive`/`searchLinearIssuesLive`) and lets the tester pick one (`bugIssue` state), then still creates a **new Tesbo bug** via "File Bug" (title/description/evidence fields remain visible).
- "Skip" closes the dialog with no action — the execution stays Failed with no bug filed.
- Manual "Log bug" action reuses the exact same dialog/flow but with title prefixed `"Bug:"` instead of `"Failed:"`.

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- **Selecting a Jira/Linear ticket via the search picker and then clicking "File Bug" does not actually attach that ticket to the created bug.** `handleBugSubmit` (the function backing the "File Bug" button) never reads the `bugIssue` state at all — it only sets `integrationProvider`/`externalUrl` when the *unrelated* "self-logged" destination fields are used, and always sends `integrationIssueKey: null`. Net effect: the picked ticket key/summary is shown in the dialog but silently dropped on submit; the resulting bug has no reference to it. This is a concrete, reproducible defect worth a dedicated test case.
- Marking an execution Failed a second time in a row (already Failed → Failed again) does **not** reopen the bug dialog from the inline-status path in the same way as the panel path — the panel only opens the dialog when transitioning **into** Failed from a non-Failed status (`!wasFailed` check); re-saving while already Failed does not retrigger it. Confirm this asymmetry between the inline dropdown handler (always opens on Failed, regardless of prior status) and the panel handler (only opens on a **transition** to Failed).
- Clicking "Skip" and then re-triggering the same execution's Failed dialog later (e.g. reopening the panel) re-prefills a fresh dialog — no memory that it was previously skipped.
- Filing a new bug from this dialog when the project's only test runs contain no executions is not really reachable from here (this dialog is always invoked with a real `bugExecution` in hand), unlike the main Bugs page's create flow.
- Linking a Failed execution to an existing bug whose status is already "Closed" is allowed with no warning/reopen prompt — the bug stays Closed even though a new failure was just linked to it.

**Key files:**
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx` — dialog state (~lines 412-429), `prepareBugDialog`/`openBugDialogFor` (558-579), `handleStatusChange` (582-597), `handlePanelSave` (612-637), `handleBugSubmit` (658-680), `handleLinkExistingBug` (682-693), `ExistingBugPickerModal` (148-209), modal JSX (1412-1629)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/IssuePickerModal.tsx` (Jira/Linear ticket search — selection not persisted, see above)
- Backend (reused from core CRUD): `createBug`, `addBugLink` in `legacy.service.ts`

---

### Bug Evidence & Attachments

**What it is:** Two mutually-exclusive ways to attach proof of a defect to a bug: uploading
raw files (screenshots, logs, videos) or pointing at an existing BetterBugs session
recording URL.

**Use cases:**
- A tester attaches a screenshot or screen recording showing the failure.
- A tester who already captured the bug via the BetterBugs browser extension/session recorder just pastes the session link instead of re-uploading files.
- Reviewers download an attached file later to inspect it.

**Problem it solves:** Preserves reproducible evidence of a defect alongside its record,
without requiring every team to use the same evidence-capture tool.

**Features & actions:**
- Evidence mode toggle: **Attach Files** vs **BetterBugs Link** — either/or, switching modes doesn't merge them (see gap below).
- File upload: `POST /api/projects/:projectId/bugs/:bugId/attachments`, multipart field name `files`, up to **10 files per request** (`FilesInterceptor("files", 10, ...)`), each file capped at `MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE` env var, default **50 MB** (`KB_MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE`). No file-type/MIME allowlist at all — any extension/content-type is accepted.
- Files are staged client-side (added to a list, individually removable) before the bug is actually created/saved; on Create, the bug is created first, then staged files are uploaded in a second request against the new bug id. On Edit, newly staged files are uploaded alongside the PATCH.
- Each attachment stores `fileName`, `contentType`, `fileSize`, `createdAt`, and a generated storage key (`bugs/<projectId>/<bugId>/<uuid>.<ext>`); storage backend is pluggable (local disk by default, or S3-compatible via `STORAGE_DRIVER=s3`).
- Download: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/bugs/attachments/:attachmentId/download` — for S3 storage, issues a 302 redirect to a short-lived signed URL; for local disk, streams the file directly with `Content-Disposition: attachment` and the original filename (percent-encoded).
- Delete a single attachment: `DELETE /api/bugs/attachments/:attachmentId` — deletes both the storage object and the DB row.
- Removing an already-uploaded attachment while editing a bug happens immediately (its own DELETE call), independent of whether the "Save Changes" button is later clicked — i.e. it is **not** part of the same transaction/undo scope as the rest of the edit form.

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- Uploading 0 files (empty file list / missing multipart part) → 400 `"No files were uploaded"`.
- Uploading more than 10 files in a single request → multer rejects the request (unexpected-file error) before it reaches the service.
- Uploading a file at/above the size cap → rejected by multer's `fileSize` limit; verify the error surfaces usably in the UI rather than a raw network failure.
- Uploading with a `bugId` that belongs to a **different** project than the `:projectId` in the URL → 404 `"Bug not found"` (service explicitly checks `bugId AND project_id` together).
- No MIME/extension restriction — uploading an executable, script, or disguised file type is accepted and later served back with its original client-supplied content-type; worth a security-review pass even though this isn't unique to bugs (attachments table is shared/generic).
- Downloading/deleting an attachment whose underlying storage object was removed out-of-band (e.g. bucket lifecycle rule, manual deletion) → `getBugAttachmentAccess` explicitly checks `storage.exists()` first and returns 404 `"File content is not available"` rather than silently failing or serving a corrupt response.
- Deleting the **only** attachment on a bug, or the only "evidence" of any kind — no warning; the bug just reverts to showing no evidence.
- Switching evidence mode from **BetterBugs Link** back to **Files** and uploading new files does **not** clear the previously-set `betterbugsUrl` on save (same root cause as the "fields can't be cleared" gap in the CRUD section: the edit form sends `betterbugsUrl: undefined` when mode is Files, which is dropped from the JSON body entirely, so `COALESCE` preserves the old value). Net effect: the bug detail view's evidence block checks `betterbugsUrl` truthiness **before** attachments, so it will keep showing the stale BetterBugs link and never show the newly-uploaded files, even though the UI now displays them in the edit modal. This is a concrete, high-value test case.
- Deleting a bug entirely orphans its attachment rows/files (see CRUD section) — no cascade delete exists for the generic `attachments` table.

**Key files:**
- Backend routes: `legacy.controller.ts:491-513` (`POST .../bugs/:bugId/attachments`, `GET .../bugs/attachments/:attachmentId/download`, `DELETE /api/bugs/attachments/:attachmentId`)
- Backend logic: `legacy.service.ts` — `uploadBugAttachments` (1988), `bugAttachment` (2013), `getBugAttachmentAccess` (2019), `deleteBugAttachment` (2029), `KB_MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE` (3410)
- Storage abstraction: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/storage/storage.service.ts`
- Schema (shared generic table): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V2_test_cases_and_suites.sql:133-146` (`attachments` table), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V49_bug_evidence.sql` (`betterbugs_url` column)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/BugEvidenceField.tsx`
- API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1692-1798` (`BugAttachment`, `uploadBugAttachments`, `deleteBugAttachment`, `getBugAttachmentDownloadUrl`)

---

### External Issue Tracker Reference (Jira / Linear / Other)

**What it is:** A lightweight, **one-way, manual reference** from a Tesbo bug to a ticket
that lives in an external system — distinct from the deeper Jira/Linear sync/integration
features (project mapping, live ticket sync, comments) which are a separate module. In the
Bugs UI this shows up as a "Where should this be tracked?" choice at bug-creation/edit
time.

**Use cases:**
- A team already manages defects in Jira/Linear and only wants Tesbo to record *that a bug exists* and a link to it, without duplicating full defect-tracking workflow in Tesbo.
- A tester wants to link a failing test directly to an already-existing Jira/Linear ticket they found via search, without knowing/copying the URL by hand.

**Problem it solves:** Avoids forcing teams with an established issue tracker to fully
switch to Tesbo's own bug tracker, while still keeping a pointer from the test artifact to
where the real defect lives.

**Features & actions:**
- `TrackingDestinationField`: **Log into Tesbo** vs **I'll log it in my task management system myself** — only shown at all when the project has Jira and/or Linear connected (`getJiraStatus`/`getLinearStatus`).
- When "myself" is chosen, `SelfLoggedTrackerField` lets the user pick **Jira** / **Linear** (whichever are connected) / **Other**, plus a free-text URL input (no format validation beyond `type="url"`) — this is a manual paste, "no search here on purpose" per the component's own comment, since the ticket is assumed to already exist.
- Separately, the Failed-execution bug dialog's "Yes, link existing" + Jira/Linear path uses `IssuePickerModal` to **search** live Jira/Linear issues via `searchJiraIssuesLive`/`searchLinearIssuesLive` and pick one by key/summary (see prior section for the bug where this selection is dropped on submit).
- Stored fields on the bug: `externalUrl` (the pasted/derived URL), `integrationProvider` (`"JIRA" | "LINEAR" | null`), `integrationIssueKey` (ticket key, e.g. `PROJ-123`).
- Bug detail view renders this as "Jira Ticket" / "Linear Ticket" / generic "Bug Link" heading depending on `integrationProvider`, linking out to `externalUrl` with `integrationIssueKey` as the link text when present.

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- Pasting a non-URL string into the self-logged URL field — only browser-native `type="url"` validation applies; no server-side URL validation exists (`externalUrl` is stored as-is).
- Switching from "myself"/Jira back to "Log into Tesbo" on an existing bug does not clear `externalUrl`/`integrationProvider` server-side (same `COALESCE`-preservation gap noted earlier) — the ticket reference silently persists and keeps showing in the bug detail view even though the UI implies it was removed.
- Choosing "Other" as the self-logged system with a Jira/Linear-style URL — `integrationProvider` is stored as `null` in this case (only `"JIRA"`/`"LINEAR"` are ever sent), so the detail view falls back to the generic "Bug Link" label even if the URL is actually a Jira/Linear link.
- No indication anywhere that this reference is a point-in-time snapshot — if the external ticket's status/title changes later, Tesbo has no way of knowing (this is a manual link only, not a synced one, unlike the separate Jira/Linear integration module).

**Key files:**
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/TrackingDestinationField.tsx`, `Tesbo-Frontend/components/SelfLoggedTrackerField.tsx`, `Tesbo-Frontend/components/IssuePickerModal.tsx`
- Frontend usage: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/bugs/page.tsx` (create/edit modals), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx` (Failed dialog)
- Backend fields: `bugs.external_url` (`V11_bugs.sql`), `bugs.integration_provider`/`integration_issue_key` (`V48_bug_links.sql`)
- Status check endpoints referenced: `getJiraStatus`/`getLinearStatus` in `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:2107-2231` (full Jira/Linear sync feature is out of scope here)

---

### Bugs List, Board View & Filtering

**What it is:** The main `/projects/:id/bugs` page — a toggle between a Kanban board
(grouped by status) and a flat, paginated table, with client-side search and filtering.

**Use cases:**
- A tester scans the board to see how many bugs are in each stage of resolution.
- A PM filters the list down to just "Open" bugs to plan the next fix cycle.
- Anyone searches for a bug by title or by the test case it's linked to.

**Problem it solves:** Gives a project-wide, at-a-glance view of defect volume and status
distribution, in whichever layout (board vs table) suits the task.

**Features & actions:**
- View toggle: **Board** (Kanban, 4 fixed columns: Open / In Progress / Reopened / Closed) vs **List** (paginated table, 15 rows/page).
- Kanban card: title, description snippet (2-line clamp), severity badge, up to 2 linked test-case chips (+"N more"), external-ticket "Link" (if present), reporter name/email, created date. Per-card hover actions: **Edit**, **Delete**. Clicking the card body opens the detail modal.
- Kanban column header: colored dot matching status, bug count badge, internally scrollable (not paginated) — a very large column just scrolls.
- List view columns: Title (+ external URL underneath if set), Status badge, Severity badge, Test Case(s) (up to 2 + "N more"), Test Run (all linked cycle names, comma-joined), Reporter, Reported date, row actions (Edit/Delete icons).
- List-view-only status filter dropdown: All Statuses / Open / In Progress / Closed / Reopened.
- Search box (both views): matches against bug title OR any linked test case's title/external id — **not** description, reporter, or status text.
- Pagination (list view only): numbered pages with ellipsis for long ranges, "start–end of total" label; resets to page 1 whenever the search/filter/view-mode changes.
- Header stats: `<open> open · <closed> closed · <total> total` (open here = `status === "Open" || "Reopened"`, matching the dashboard's definition — "In Progress" bugs count toward neither "open" nor "closed" in this summary line).
- Detail modal ("Bug Details"): full description, severity + status badges, external ticket link (labeled by provider) or BetterBugs session link or attachments list (mutually exclusive display — BetterBugs takes priority if both are somehow set), full linked test cases/runs list, reporter, reported-on / last-updated timestamps, Delete/Close/Edit actions.
- "Report Bug" primary button (top-right) opens the create modal from anywhere on this page.

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- No bulk actions of any kind exist — no multi-select, no bulk status change, no bulk delete, on either Kanban or List view (confirmed by absence in the component — each card/row only has individual Edit/Delete).
- No comment thread / activity log on an individual bug — `createBug`/`updateBug`/`deleteBug` never call the app's `logProjectActivity` audit-log helper (unlike executions, which do), so bug edits/deletes leave no trace in the project's Activity stream and there's no per-bug discussion thread.
- A bug with a non-standard `status` (set via direct API — see CRUD section) vanishes from the Kanban board entirely (no "Unknown"/catch-all column) while still appearing in List view under "All Statuses".
- List endpoint (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/bugs`) has no pagination/limit — it always returns every bug for the project in one response; pagination is purely a client-side slice of the already-fully-loaded array. Worth a scale test (hundreds of bugs) for both load time and the Kanban board's un-paginated per-column scroll.
- Search and status-filter are both computed client-side over the already-fetched list (the backend's `status`/`cycleId` query params are never invoked from this page) — confirm filtering/searching still works correctly after the full list has loaded, and that there's no server-round-trip per keystroke (there isn't).
- Deleting a bug from within the Detail modal closes the modal and reopens the (separate) delete-confirm modal — verify Cancel from that confirm step doesn't also lose the just-closed detail view's context oddly.

**Key files:**
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/bugs/page.tsx` (entire page: `KanbanCard`/`KanbanColumn` ~118-265, `Pagination` ~268-345, main component ~348-1257)
- Nav entry: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/Sidebar.tsx` (`{ href: "bugs", label: "Bugs", icon: "bug" }`, under "Execution" section)

---

### Bug Metrics & Reporting Integration

**What it is:** Read-only surfacing of bug data in the project Dashboard and the Reports
module — not part of the Bugs page itself, but directly fed by the same `bugs` table and
worth testing whenever bug data changes.

**Use cases:**
- A PM checks the Dashboard's "Open bugs" count and severity breakdown at a glance without opening the Bugs page.
- A stakeholder reviews the Trends tab's "Bug discovery rate" chart to see if defect discovery is accelerating or slowing.
- A stakeholder reviews the Traceability Matrix to see which requirements/test cases have known defects.

**Problem it solves:** Surfaces defect trends and current backlog health without requiring
a trip to the full Bugs page.

**Features & actions:**
- Dashboard "Open bugs" stat card (links through to `/projects/:id/bugs`) and a "Bug severity breakdown" panel (proportional bars per severity), both driven by `projectDashboardSummary`.
- Trends tab "Bug discovery rate" bar chart — count of bugs **created** per calendar week (by `created_at`), last 7 weeks, regardless of status/severity.
- Traceability Matrix — a "Bug" column per requirement/test-case/run row, populated via `bugs.execution_id` (see the gap noted in the Linking section — only reflects a bug's original single link, not all `bug_links`).

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- "Open bugs" total/severity breakdown counts **only** `status IN ('Open', 'Reopened')` — a bug marked "In Progress" is excluded from this figure even though it is still unresolved. Verify this matches (or intentionally diverges from) user expectations of "open."
- Bug discovery rate counts bugs by creation week only — reopening an old bug does not add to a later week's count, and deleting a bug removes it from its original week's historical count retroactively (no historical snapshot).
- A bug linked to a second execution via `addBugLink` after creation is invisible to the Traceability Matrix for that second test case (see Linking section) — worth a dedicated cross-check test between the Bugs page and this report for any multi-linked bug.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.service.ts` — `projectDashboardSummary` (2522, bug severity query 2526-2556), `reportsTrends` (2497, bug discovery query 2500-2510), `requirementMatrix` (2168)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/dashboard/page.tsx` (~lines 200-320, 446-475), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/TrendsTab.tsx`, `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/TraceabilityTab.tsx`, `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/charts.tsx`

---

### Programmatic Bug Filing (MCP Tool)

**What it is:** A single MCP ("Model Context Protocol") tool, `create_bug`, that lets an
API-token-authenticated automation client (e.g. a CI pipeline or an agent) file a bug into
a specific project without going through the UI.

**Use cases:**
- A CI pipeline automatically files a Tesbo bug when an automated test suite reports a failure.
- An AI agent connected via MCP reports a defect it discovered while exploring the app.

**Problem it solves:** Extends bug creation to non-interactive/automated clients using the
same project-scoped API token system used elsewhere in the platform.

**Features & actions:**
- Tool name `create_bug`, requires `write` scope on the API token.
- Required: `title`. Optional: `description`, `status`, `externalUrl`, `links` (array of `{testcaseId, cycleId, executionId}`); `additionalProperties: true` means other bug fields (e.g. `severity`, `betterbugsUrl`) can also be passed through even though undocumented in the tool schema, since the handler forwards `args` straight to the same `createBug` service method used by the REST API.
- `reported_by` is set to the **token's owning human user**, not a synthetic "agent" actor (explicit design choice, per code comment, since `bugs.reported_by` is a FK into `users`).

**Edge cases / validation gaps worth testing:**
- No `update_bug`, `delete_bug`, `list_bugs`, or attachment tools exist in the MCP surface — only creation is possible via this channel; verify that's the intended (documented) scope for automation clients.
- Passing an invalid `severity` through `create_bug`'s `additionalProperties` passthrough hits the same unvalidated DB-CHECK-constraint failure path noted in the core CRUD section.
- A token scoped to Project A cannot file into Project B — confirm `ctx.projectId` (bound to the token) is always used, never a caller-supplied project id.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.tools.ts:171-193` (`create_bug` tool definition and handler)

---

## Section E — Reports, Analytics, Dashboards, Activity Feed, and Notifications

Scope covered: workspace-wide dashboard, project-level dashboard, the six-tab Reports & Insights
page (Overview, Execution Report, Traceability, Repository, AI Insights, Trends), the cross-source
Ticket/Requirements summary, the project Activity feed, and the (unimplemented) Notifications
feature. All backend logic lives in the "legacy" module — there is no separate reports/analytics
service or controller.

---

### Workspace Dashboard

**What it is:** The top-level `/dashboard` page shown after login — an aggregate rollup of every
project in the user's currently-active workspace/organization (not scoped to a single project).

**Use cases:**
- A workspace owner or manager wants a single-glance health check across all projects without
  opening each one individually.
- A new user landing after login sees whether the workspace has any content yet (projects, test
  cases, executions) before drilling into a specific project.
- Quick navigation jump-off point — clicking the "Projects" stat or "View projects" link routes to
  the full projects list.

**Problem it solves:** Gives an org-wide summary of test activity (counts + execution status split)
without requiring the user to pick a project first.

**Features & actions:**
- Stat tiles (5): Projects, Test cases, Suites, Plans, Cycles — each a raw `COUNT(*)` scoped to the
  active organization via `project_id IN (SELECT id FROM projects WHERE organization_id = $1)`.
  - "Projects" tile is a clickable link to `/projects`; the other four tiles are static (not links).
- Execution status breakdown: a horizontal grid of chips (Passed / Failed / Blocked / Untested /
  any other status value present), each showing count + percentage of total executions and a
  fill-bar sized to that percentage.
  - Percentages are computed client-side from `count / executionTotal`, rounded to nearest integer
    — rounding across many statuses will not always sum to exactly 100%.
  - Status chip colors are hardcoded for `Passed/Failed/Blocked/Untested` only; any other status
    string (e.g. `Retest`, `Skipped`) falls back to a generic neutral style but still renders.
- "Total executions across all projects: N" footer line + "View projects →" link.
- Empty state: when `executionTotal === 0`, shows "No executions yet. Run a test cycle in any
  project to see status breakdown." instead of the chip grid.
- Auth gate: redirects to `/login` if `authMe()` returns no user.
- Loading and error states are distinct screens (not inline skeletons).

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Workspace with zero projects → all five stat tiles show 0; execution section shows empty state.
- Workspace with projects but zero test cycles/executions anywhere → empty-state message appears.
- Large execution counts (rounding behavior of percentages, e.g. 3-way split not summing to 100%).
- User belongs to multiple workspaces — confirm this dashboard reflects only the **active**
  organization (`switchWorkspace` changes what `/api/workspace/analytics` returns).
- API failure (e.g. network error) → error screen renders instead of dashboard content.
- Only counts *active* (non-deleted) test cases/executions — confirm archived/soft-deleted test
  cases and executions do not inflate the numbers (backend queries `testcases_active` /
  `executions_active` views, which filter `deleted_at IS NULL`).

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/workspace/analytics` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:78-82` (resolves the caller's workspace, then calls `analytics(undefined, workspace.id)`)
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.analytics()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2200-2237`
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/dashboard/page.tsx`
- API client: `getWorkspaceAnalytics()`, `WorkspaceAnalytics` type — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1799-1811`

---

### Project Dashboard

**What it is:** The project-scoped home page (`/projects/:id/dashboard`, aka "Project home" in the
sidebar) — a KPI overview plus recent runs and recent activity for a single project. This is what
the project root URL (`/projects/:id`) redirects to.

**Use cases:**
- A QA lead opens a project and immediately sees pass rate, open bugs by severity, coverage, and
  active runs without navigating to the full Reports page.
- A team member checks "what changed this week" (deltas) and "what's happening right now" (active
  runs, recent activity) in one screen.
- Quick-launch actions: "New run" and "New test plan" buttons in the header.

**Problem it solves:** Surfaces the handful of numbers a project stakeholder checks daily (pass
rate trend, bug severity mix, requirement coverage, active runs) in one place, backed by
week-over-week deltas so trends are visible without opening the full Reports page.

**Features & actions:**
- Primary stat cards (4), each linking to its detail page:
  - **Test cases** (→ `/testcases`): total count + "+N this week" success badge if any created in
    the last 7 days (created_at >= now() - 7 days).
  - **Pass rate** (→ `/reports`): percentage of executed (non-Untested) executions that are
    `Passed`; shows `—` when there have been zero executions. Badge shows `+N%`/`-N%` "this week"
    by comparing pass rate of executions in the trailing 7 days vs. the 7 days before that (both
    windows require at least one executed test to produce a rate, otherwise the delta is `null`
    and no badge renders).
  - **Open bugs** (→ `/bugs`): count of bugs with status `Open` or `Reopened`, broken down by
    severity (Critical/High/Medium/Low) with a proportional stacked mini-bar; "N critical" error
    badge shown only if `Critical > 0`.
  - **Test coverage** (→ `/requirements`): percentage of Jira+Linear tickets that have at least one
    linked, non-deleted test case (`coveredRequirements / totalRequirements`); shows `—` and the
    label "Test coverage — no requirements linked" when there are zero synced tickets.
- Secondary stat cards (3, no badges): Plans (→ `/plans`), Suites (→ `/testcases`), Active runs
  (→ `/cycles`, cycles with `status = 'In Progress'`; "running" warning badge if > 0).
- Header actions: "New run" (→ `/cycles?create=1`), "New test plan" (→ `/plans?create=1`).
- **Recent test runs panel** (left column): up to 4 most-recent cycles (fetched via `listCycles`,
  sliced client-side), each showing name, status chip, relative timestamp, a 3-segment
  passed/failed/blocked progress bar, and an "X/Y executed" counter. Empty state: "No test runs
  yet."
- **Bug severity breakdown panel** (left column, below runs): horizontal bars per severity level
  with count and percentage-of-total-open-bugs width. Empty state: "No open bugs right now."
- **Recent activity panel** (right column, sticky, max-height scrollable): last 10 activity-log
  entries (via `listActivity(projectId, { limit: 10 })`), each with a colored dot (green=create/
  approve, red=delete/reject, blue=update/move, purple=AI/agent actor), a human-readable
  description sentence, actor avatar, and relative time. Empty state: "No activity yet."
- Client-side guard against a known data quirk: a cycle with zero cycle_items still returns one
  all-NULL aggregate row from the backend's LEFT JOIN, so `executed = totalCases - untested` is
  clamped to `Math.max(0, ...)` to avoid showing a negative "executed" count.

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Brand-new project: all stat cards should show 0 / `—` / empty states, not errors.
- Project with test cases but zero executions ever → Pass rate shows `—`, no delta badge.
- Project with executions only in the prior 7-day window (none in the last 7 days) →
  `passRateDeltaThisWeek` should be `null` (not a misleading 0% or negative infinity).
- Bug with a severity value outside `Critical/High/Medium/Low` (e.g. null, empty string, custom
  value) — confirm whether it's silently dropped from the "Open bugs" total. (Backend initializes
  `bySeverity` with exactly those four keys and only assigns `if (row.severity in bySeverity)`, so
  an unrecognized severity is excluded from `openBugsTotal` entirely — worth a dedicated test.)
- Zero Jira/Linear tickets synced → coverage card shows `—` and "no requirements linked" label
  rather than 0%.
- Cycle with zero cycle_items (empty test run) → recent-runs card must not show a negative
  "executed" count.
- Deep-linking directly to `/projects/:id` (not `/dashboard`) → should redirect via
  `ProjectRootRedirect`.
- Invalid/nonexistent `projectId` → `getProject` rejects → redirects to `/projects`.

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/dashboard` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:582-585`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.projectDashboardSummary()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2522-2582` (also calls `analytics()` and `requirementsSummary()` internally)
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/dashboard/page.tsx`
- Redirect stub: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/page.tsx`
- API client: `getProjectDashboardSummary()`, `ProjectDashboardSummary` type — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1976-1988`
- Note: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/analytics` (`projectAnalytics` controller method →
  `LegacyService.analytics(projectId)`, same function as the workspace dashboard uses) is defined
  in the API client (`getProjectAnalytics`) but is **not called from any current frontend page** —
  it exists as a lighter project-scoped analytics endpoint with no UI consumer yet.

---

### Reports Overview (KPI Summary tab)

**What it is:** The default landing tab of the project's Reports & Insights page (`/projects/:id/reports`)
— a condensed KPI dashboard combining a pass-rate trend chart, per-suite health bars, and a
rule-generated text summary.

**Use cases:**
- A test lead opens Reports and wants the single highest-level view before drilling into
  execution/traceability/repository detail tabs.
- Spot-checking which suites are healthy (high pass rate) vs. struggling, at a glance.

**Problem it solves:** Answers "is quality trending up or down, and which suites need attention"
without requiring the reader to interpret raw execution tables.

**Features & actions:**
- **Pass rate trend** line/area chart: pass rate (%) of the last 10 test cycles (cycles with zero
  executed items are plotted as gaps/nulls, not zero). Header badge shows `+N%`/`-N%` delta between
  the first and last cycle with a valid rate, only shown when ≥2 cycles have a valid rate.
- **Suite health** bars: per-suite pass percentage of executed cases; suites with zero executions
  show "Not run" instead of a percentage; color threshold at 70% pass (green vs. amber).
- **"AI summary"** panel (labeled with an "AI" badge in the UI): a **rule-based, template-generated**
  sentence — *not* an LLM call. It is assembled by string-concatenating up to three canned
  sentences depending on computed conditions, in this order:
  1. If any flaky test exists: `"<Suite> suite has a flaky test (<ID>) with inconsistent results across runs."`
  2. If any suite has <70% coverage: `"<Suite> suite shows low coverage — only X of Y cases executed."`
  3. If ≥2 cycles have a valid pass rate: `"Overall pass rate improved/declined N% over the last M runs."`
  4. If none of the above apply: `"Not enough execution history yet to generate insights."`
  - Below the summary, up to 3 pill badges show live counts: flaky test count, coverage gap count,
    untested P1 count (each only rendered if > 0).
- Header stat chips (shared across all report tabs, computed client-side from `overview` +
  `insights` responses): Pass rate %, Runs count, Open bugs count, Coverage %.
- Left nav sidebar (`ReportsNav`) persists across tabs: Overview / Execution Report / Traceability
  / Repository under "Analytics"; AI Insights (with a live flaky-count badge) / Trends under
  "Intelligence"; Export PDF / Export CSV under "Export" — **both export buttons are disabled
  ("Coming soon" tooltip, `cursor-not-allowed`) and not wired to any backend endpoint.**
- Top bar also has a page-level "Export" button, also disabled/"Coming soon" — no PDF/image/CSV
  export is actually implemented anywhere on the Reports page as of this writing.

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Project with zero test cycles → pass rate trend shows "Not enough run history yet"; suite health
  shows "No suites yet"; AI summary falls back to the "not enough history" sentence.
- Project with exactly 1 cycle with a valid pass rate → no trend delta badge shown (requires ≥2).
- Confirm the "AI" badge/label does not imply non-deterministic or LLM output — re-running the
  report for identical data must produce byte-identical summary text (useful regression check to
  distinguish this from a true generative-AI feature).
- Suite with 0 executed cases shows "Not run", not "0% pass".
- Click every disabled Export control and confirm no network request fires and no crash occurs.
- Flaky test count badge in the left nav must match `insights.flakyTests.length` exactly (shared
  data source between Overview and AI Insights tabs).

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/overview` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:607-610`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.reportsOverview()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2432-2467`
  (depends on private helpers `cyclePassRateSeries`, `suiteHealth`, `coverageBySuite`,
  `untestedP1Count`, `detectFlakyTests` — `legacy.service.ts:2280-2430`)
- Frontend page shell: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/reports/page.tsx`
- Frontend tab: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/OverviewTab.tsx`
- Nav sidebar: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/ReportsNav.tsx`
- Chart primitives: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/charts.tsx` (`TrendLineChart`)
- API client: `getReportsOverview()`, `ReportsOverview` type — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1909-1930`
