### Execution Report

**What it is:** A groupable breakdown of every test execution in a project, viewable as either a
stacked bar chart + donut chart or a sortable data table, grouped by one of seven dimensions.

**Use cases:**
- "Show me pass/fail counts broken down by test run" (the default "Overall" view).
- A manager filters to a specific person to see their execution workload and pass rate.
- QA wants to see which test plan, suite, priority level, or tag has the worst fail rate.

**Problem it solves:** Lets any status axis (run/person/plan/suite/priority/tag) be sliced without
needing a separate report per dimension — one query serves all seven groupings.

**Features & actions:**
- **Group-by selector** ("Group by" dropdown) with 7 modes: Overall (by Test Run) [default],
  By Person, By Test Plan, By Test Run, By Test Suite, By Tags, By Priority.
- **Secondary filter-value dropdown**, contextual to the group-by mode:
  - Plan mode → dropdown of the project's plans ("All Plans" + each plan).
  - Run mode → dropdown of the project's cycles ("All Runs" + each run).
  - Suite mode → dropdown of the project's suites ("All Suites" + each suite).
  - Person mode → dropdown of project members ("All Members" + each member by name/email).
  - Priority mode → fixed P0–P3 dropdown.
  - Tags mode → free-text input (matches against comma-split `automation_tags` on the test case;
    untagged cases are bucketed under a synthetic "Untagged" group when grouping by tags).
  - Switching group-by resets the filter value.
- **Chart / Table view toggle.**
  - Chart view: stacked horizontal bar (one bar per group, segmented by status) + a status
    distribution donut chart with legend.
  - Table view: one row per group with per-status counts, total, and computed pass rate % (colored
    green ≥80%, amber ≥50%, red <50%), plus a totals footer row.
- **Metric cards** row: Total + one card per status (Passed/Failed/Blocked/Skipped/Untested/Retest).
- Status set is fixed to exactly these 6 keys; any execution status not in this set is coerced to
  "Untested" server-side.
- Empty state: "No data available" in the table when `rows` is empty (e.g. zero cycles/executions).

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Project with zero cycles → empty rows, all metric cards show 0, charts show "No data".
- Filter by a person who has never been assigned an execution → 0 rows for that filter, no error.
- Filter by tags with a tag value that matches nothing → empty result, not an error.
- A test case with multiple comma-separated tags is counted once per tag when grouping by tag
  (i.e. total execution count across tag groups can exceed total unique executions — worth
  verifying this "fan-out" behavior is intentional/documented for QA).
- A test case with no `automation_tags` set is only counted under "Untagged" when grouping by tags.
- Switching "Group by" clears the previously-selected filter value (verify UI resets the
  dependent dropdown, not just the state).
- An execution whose `status` is null/unrecognized should display and count as "Untested".
- Cycle-level filter should include cycles regardless of status (Planning/In Progress/Completed).
- Table "Total" footer row math must always equal the sum of all group rows exactly.

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/execution` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:592-595`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.executionReport()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2084-2166`
- Frontend tab: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/ExecutionReportTab.tsx`
- Chart primitives: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/charts.tsx` (`StackedBarChart`, `DonutChart`, `Legend`)
- API client: `getExecutionReport()`, `ExecutionReportRow`/`ExecutionReportResponse` types — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1827-1857`

---

### Requirement Traceability Matrix

**What it is:** A "Traceability" tab showing, per test case, every test run it was executed in and
any linked bug — i.e. a Requirement → Test Case → Run → Bug chain in one table.

**Use cases:**
- Auditors/compliance reviewers verify every test case has traceable execution history and, if
  failed, a linked defect.
- QA leads check which test cases have never been run (no `run`/`execution` columns populated).
- Searching for a specific bug or run to see which test case surfaced it.

**Problem it solves:** Gives a single denormalized view connecting test case identity, its
priority/status, every run it participated in, the outcome of each run, and the resulting bug (if
any) — without manually cross-referencing the Test Cases, Cycles, and Bugs pages.

**Features & actions:**
- One row is returned **per (test case × run × execution × bug)** combination server-side; the
  frontend groups consecutive rows sharing the same `testcaseId` into a single visual block using
  `rowSpan`, so a test case that ran in 3 cycles shows as 1 merged block with 3 sub-rows.
- A test case that has **never** been added to any cycle still appears (via `LEFT JOIN`), with
  run/execution/bug columns all blank (`—`).
- Columns: Test Case ID (external ID), Title, Priority (color-coded P0–P3), Status (chip), Suite,
  Run name, Result (execution status chip), Executed date, Bug (title, hyperlinked to
  `bugUrl` if present, otherwise plain text).
- **Resizable columns**: every column header has a drag handle (mouse-down + mouse-move) to resize
  width live, with a per-column minimum width floor.
- **Client-side search** box: filters by external ID, test case title, run name, or bug title
  (case-insensitive substring match) — filtering happens in the browser, not via a server request.
- Footer summary: "N test cases across M rows" (M ≥ N when a test case has multiple runs).
- Only non-deleted test cases are included (`t.deleted_at IS NULL`); soft-deleted executions
  (`e.deleted_at IS NULL`) are excluded too, but a test case's *other* still-valid executions still
  show.
- Ordered by external ID, then by run creation date descending (nulls last).

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Test case never added to any cycle → appears once with all run/result/bug columns blank.
- Test case executed in the same cycle multiple times (e.g. retested) — confirm each execution
  shows as its own sub-row, not deduplicated.
- Test case with an execution but no linked bug vs. one with a linked bug that has no `external_url`
  (should render bug title as plain text, not a broken link).
- Searching for text that matches only a bug title (not the test case ID/title/run name) should
  still surface that test case's row.
- Column resize drag should not let a column shrink below its declared `minWidth`.
- Archived/soft-deleted test case must not appear at all.
- A cycle that itself is soft-deleted or a test case removed from a cycle — verify it doesn't
  leave orphaned rows.
- Very large projects (thousands of test cases × multiple runs) — verify pagination/perf isn't a
  problem, since this endpoint returns **all** rows in one response with no `limit`/`offset`.

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/requirement-matrix` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:597-600`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.requirementMatrix()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2168-2198`
- Frontend tab: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/TraceabilityTab.tsx`
- API client: `getRequirementMatrix()`, `RequirementMatrixRow` type — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1859-1881`

---

### Repository Summary Report

**What it is:** An inventory report of the project's test case repository — totals, breakdowns by
suite/status/priority, and a 30-day creation trend.

**Use cases:**
- A test manager checks overall test case inventory size and how it's distributed across suites.
- Verifying recent authoring activity (how many cases were added/updated today/this week/this
  month) — useful for sprint retros or contributor productivity checks.
- Spotting suites that are disproportionately large/small, or priority distribution skew (e.g. too
  few P0/P1 cases).

**Problem it solves:** Gives a repository-health snapshot independent of execution/run data —
answers "what do we have," not "what happened when we ran it."

**Features & actions:**
- 4 summary tiles: Total test cases, Updated today (rolling 24h), Updated this week (since Monday,
  `date_trunc('week', now())`), Updated this month (since the 1st).
- **Test cases by suite**: horizontal bar chart, one bar per suite (cases with no suite grouped
  under "Unassigned"), each bar colored from a fixed 6-color palette cycling by index.
- **By status**: donut chart + legend. Status color mapping is hardcoded for
  Draft/Approved/"In Review"/Deprecated/Archived; any other status value falls back to a generic
  "AI primary" color rather than failing.
- **Test cases added (last 30 days)**: daily trend line chart. Backend always returns exactly 30
  data points (one per calendar day) via `generate_series`, with `0` (not a gap) for days with no
  creations — this differs from the pass-rate trend charts elsewhere, which use `null` for
  no-data points.
- **Test cases by priority**: 4 stat tiles (P0–P3), each showing count + a human label
  ("P0 - Critical" etc.); a priority value outside P0–P3 (e.g. "Unspecified") still renders via
  `groupTestcases`, just without a friendly label mapping (shows the raw value).
- Only counts test cases where `deleted_at IS NULL` (uses the `testcases_active` view) — archived/
  soft-deleted test cases are excluded from every metric on this tab.

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Project with zero test cases → all 4 tiles show 0, suite/status/priority charts show empty
  states, 30-day trend shows a flat zero line (not "no data").
- Test case updated the same second it was created should not spuriously count as "updated" (the
  broader activity-feed logic elsewhere uses a `+1 second` guard for this; verify whether this
  specific report has the same protection or double counts near-simultaneous create+update).
- Test case with `suite_id = NULL` → grouped under "Unassigned" bucket, not omitted.
- Test case with a non-standard/custom status string → still appears in the donut with fallback
  color, not silently dropped.
- Archived (soft-deleted) test case must not appear in totals, by-suite, by-status, by-priority, or
  the 30-day trend.
- Boundary check: a test case created exactly at midnight local vs. UTC — verify "Updated today"
  bucket boundary matches user expectation (query uses Postgres `now()`/server timezone, not
  client timezone).

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/repository-summary` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:602-605`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.repositorySummary()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2239-2278` (uses private `groupTestcases()` helper — `legacy.service.ts:7825-7831`)
- Frontend tab: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/RepositoryTab.tsx`
- Chart primitives: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/charts.tsx` (`HorizontalBarChart`, `DonutChart`, `TrendLineChart`)
- API client: `getRepositorySummary()`, `RepositorySummary` type — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1883-1897`

---

### AI Insights (Health Score, Flaky Test Detector, Coverage Gaps)

**What it is:** The "AI Insights" tab — a composite project health score plus two derived-risk
widgets: a flaky-test detector and a per-suite coverage heatmap. **Important:** despite the "AI"
branding badge in the UI, none of this is generated by a language model — it is entirely
deterministic SQL aggregation plus a hand-tuned weighted formula computed on every request.

**Use cases:**
- A test lead wants one number ("health score") to report up to stakeholders about overall test
  suite quality/risk.
- Identifying specific flaky tests (inconsistent pass/fail across runs) that erode trust in the
  test suite and should be triaged/fixed or quarantined.
- Identifying which suites have the weakest execution coverage (cases that have never been run)
  to prioritize test execution effort.

**Problem it solves:** Converts several raw signals (pass rate, coverage, untested-critical-cases,
flakiness) into one actionable score and a prioritized list of specific tests/suites to investigate,
rather than requiring a human to manually correlate multiple reports.

**Features & actions:**
- **Health score gauge** (semicircular 0–100 gauge) + label: "Healthy" (≥70), "Needs attention"
  (≥40), "At risk" (<40). Formula, verbatim from the code comment:
  - `rawScore = avgPassRate * 0.6 + avgCoverage * 0.3 + untestedPenalty - flakyCount * 5`
  - `avgPassRate` = mean of per-cycle pass rates over the last 10 cycles (cycles with no executions
    excluded, not counted as 0).
  - `avgCoverage` = mean of per-suite coverage % (cases with ≥1 non-Untested execution / total
    cases in that suite).
  - `untestedPenalty` = `10` if there are zero untested P1 cases, else `max(0, 10 - untestedP1Count)`.
  - Final score is clamped to `[0, 100]` and rounded.
  - Explicitly documented in code as a "v1 heuristic... no historical baseline exists yet to
    calibrate weights against" — i.e. an unvalidated/arbitrary scoring model, worth flagging to QA
    as something to sanity-check against real project data rather than trust blindly.
- **Flaky test detector**: a test case counts as flaky if it has ≥2 executions across different
  cycles with at least 2 distinct status values seen. "Flip count" = number of status changes
  between consecutive (chronologically ordered) executions. Flip rate = flips / (executions - 1).
  Label: "High" (≥50% flip rate), "Medium" (≥25%), "Low" (below). List is capped to the top 20 by
  flip count, sorted descending.
  - Table shows: test case ID, title, suite, a chip-per-run showing that run's status in
    chronological order, and a flakiness bar + label.
- **Coverage gaps**: any suite with <70% of its test cases having ≥1 non-Untested execution is
  flagged as a "gap." Displayed both as a count (stat tile) and as a full heatmap (all suites, not
  just gapped ones) with color bands: green ("Good") ≥70%, amber ("Low") ≥30%, red ("Critical") <30%.
- **Untested P1s** stat tile: count of P1-priority test cases with zero non-Untested executions
  ever recorded.
- 3 top-row stat tiles mirror the flaky/coverage-gap/untested-P1 counts with a one-line contextual
  description (e.g. names the top offending suite/test).

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Project with zero execution history → health score should reflect `avgPassRate = 0`,
  `avgCoverage = 0`, `untestedPenalty` still computed — verify the score doesn't misleadingly show
  as "Healthy" or crash when there is no history (edge case: `avgPassRate` mean-of-empty-array
  should be 0, not `NaN`).
- Health score exactly at a boundary (69 vs 70, 39 vs 40) — verify label transitions correctly.
- A test case executed exactly twice with the same status both times → should NOT be flagged
  flaky (needs ≥2 *distinct* statuses).
- A test case executed exactly twice with different statuses → minimal flaky case, flip rate = 100%
  → "High" label.
- More than 20 flaky tests detected → list truncates to top 20 by flip count; verify sort order
  (most-flipping test first).
- Suite with 0 test cases → coverage % should not divide by zero (code returns 0% for `total = 0`).
- Negative-score inputs (e.g. many flaky tests) — verify score clamps to 0, not negative.
- Score >100 in theory (e.g. very high pass rate + full coverage + no flaky/untested) — verify
  clamped to 100.
- Re-verify the "AI" badge doesn't set an expectation of non-determinism — same underlying data
  must always produce the exact same health score/labels (good regression-test candidate).

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/insights` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:612-615`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.reportsInsights()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2469-2495`
  (shares helpers `coverageBySuite`, `untestedP1Count`, `detectFlakyTests`, `cyclePassRateSeries` with the Overview tab — `legacy.service.ts:2280-2430`)
- Frontend tab: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/AIInsightsTab.tsx`
- Chart primitive: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/charts.tsx` (`HealthGauge`)
- API client: `getReportsInsights()`, `ReportsInsights`/`FlakyTestRow`/`CoverageRow` types — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1932-1961`

---

### Trends

**What it is:** A time-series tab showing pass rate history, execution velocity, and bug discovery
rate over recent weeks/cycles.

**Use cases:**
- Leadership wants to see if quality is trending up or down over the last several test cycles.
- Identifying weeks with unusually high bug discovery (could indicate a risky release or a testing
  push) vs. quiet weeks.
- Correlating execution volume (how many tests were run per cycle) against pass rate trend.

**Problem it solves:** Provides longitudinal context that single-point-in-time reports (Overview,
Execution Report) can't — is quality/velocity improving or regressing release over release.

**Features & actions:**
- **Pass rate over time**: line/area chart over the last 12 cycles (vs. 10 for Overview/Insights).
  Subtitle states "Based on the last N test runs." Header badge shows `+N%`/`-N%` "vs first run"
  when ≥2 cycles have a valid rate.
- **Execution velocity**: vertical bar chart, one bar per cycle, height = number of executed
  (non-Untested) test items in that cycle. Cycle names truncated to 8 characters + ellipsis if
  longer.
- **Bug discovery rate**: vertical bar chart, one bar per calendar week (last 7 weeks, via
  `generate_series` on `date_trunc('week', ...)`), height = count of bugs created that week
  (all bugs, not filtered by status/severity). Weeks with zero bugs created show a 0-height bar,
  not a gap — every week in the 7-week window always appears.

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Project with 1 cycle only → no trend delta badge (requires ≥2 valid-rate cycles); bar charts
  still render with a single bar.
- Project with 0 cycles → pass rate chart shows "Not enough run history yet"; velocity/bug charts
  show "No data available."
- Week with 0 bugs created should show a zero-height bar (present in the axis), not be omitted
  from the chart entirely — verify the 7-week window is always fully populated.
- Bug discovery counts **all** bugs regardless of current status (even if later closed/resolved) —
  confirm this is the intended semantic (discovery ≠ still-open).
- Cycle name longer than 8 characters is truncated with `…` in the velocity chart x-axis label —
  verify no layout overflow with very long cycle names.
- 13th+ cycle should be excluded (only last 12 considered) — verify ordering (oldest→newest) so
  "vs first run" delta compares the correct endpoints.

**Key files:**
- Backend route: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/reports/trends` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:617-620`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.reportsTrends()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2497-2520`
- Frontend tab: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/TrendsTab.tsx`
- Chart primitives: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/reports/charts.tsx` (`TrendLineChart`, `VerticalBarChart`)
- API client: `getReportsTrends()`, `ReportsTrends` type — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:1963-1973`

---

### Ticket Summary / Requirements Coverage (cross-source Jira + Linear)

**What it is:** The project's "Requirements" page — a cross-source aggregate + browsable list of
Jira and Linear tickets, showing which ones have linked (covered) test cases. This is what backs
the "Coverage" metric shown on the Project Dashboard.

**Use cases:**
- A BA/PM checks how many requirements (tickets) have test coverage before a release, per source
  or combined.
- A tester filters to "Uncovered" tickets to find what still needs test cases written.
- Using "Assign to Zyra" to auto-generate test case coverage directly from an uncovered ticket.

**Problem it solves:** Bridges external issue trackers (Jira/Linear) with Tesbo's test case
repository so coverage can be measured and gaps immediately actioned (via AI test generation)
without leaving the page.

**Features & actions:**
- **Source tabs**: All Sources (Σ) / Jira / Linear, each showing a live ticket count badge.
- **Stat strip** (scoped to the active source tab): Total, Covered, Uncovered, and a Coverage %
  progress bar. "Covered" = ticket has ≥1 linked, non-deleted test case
  (`jira_issue_key`/`linear_issue_key` match).
- **Filters**: free-text search (key or summary, submit-on-enter), Type dropdown (options derived
  dynamically from *actual* distinct `issue_type` values present — no fixed enum since Jira/Linear
  types are free text), Status dropdown (same, dynamic), Coverage dropdown (All/Covered/Uncovered).
  "Clear filters" link appears whenever any filter is active.
- **Sync button**: triggers a live pull from Jira and/or Linear (`syncJiraTickets`/
  `syncLinearTickets`) depending on active tab and which integrations are connected; refreshes both
  the ticket list and the summary stats afterward. Shows a dismissible error banner on failure.
- **Ticket table**: Key (source badge + hyperlink to the external ticket), Summary, Type (colored
  chip: Bug/Story/Epic/Task get distinct colors), Status (chip, tone derived from common
  Done/In Progress/To Do vocabulary), Priority (colored by Highest/High/Medium/Low/Lowest), Assignee,
  Coverage (shows linked test-case count or `—`), Action.
  - Row click expands an inline detail panel: description, reporter, labels, created/updated dates,
    "Open in Jira/Linear →" link.
  - Action column: "Assign to Zyra" (generate) if uncovered, or "View testcases" + "Regenerate with
    Zyra" if already linked — both create a Zyra AI task (`createZyraTask`) and redirect to
    `/projects/:id/agents/tasks`.
- **Pagination**: 25 tickets/page, Previous/Next controls, "Page X of Y" indicator.
- **Not-connected empty state**: if neither Jira nor Linear is connected, shows a "Connect Jira or
  Linear to Get Started" prompt linking to integration settings instead of the table.
- **Connected-but-never-synced empty state**: distinct "No Requirements Synced Yet" prompt with an
  inline "Sync Tickets" button.

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Neither integration connected → connect-prompt shown, table/filters hidden.
- Integration connected but zero tickets ever synced → "sync tickets" prompt (distinct from the
  "no results for these filters" case — verify the page doesn't confuse the two).
- Search/filter combination that matches zero tickets → table area should show *some* empty
  indication rather than blank (verify against actual runtime behavior — the "no synced tickets"
  block only shows when there's no active search/filter).
- "All Sources" totals must equal `jira.total + linear.total` (and same for covered/uncovered) —
  verify aggregate math when both sources have tickets referencing the *same* linked test case
  differently (they're keyed independently by `jira_issue_key` vs `linear_issue_key`, so no
  double-counting risk, but worth confirming).
- A ticket whose issue_type/status is blank/empty string is excluded from the Type/Status filter
  dropdowns (backend filters `issue_type <> ''`/`status <> ''`) — confirm such tickets are still
  visible in the table itself, just not filterable by that dimension.
- Coverage filter edge case: a ticket linked only to a soft-deleted test case should count as
  "uncovered" (backend join requires `t.deleted_at IS NULL`).
- "Assign to Zyra" / "Regenerate with Zyra" while a request is already in flight — button should
  show "Assigning..." and be disabled to prevent double submission.
- Switching source tabs resets all filters, search, and pagination back to page 0.
- Sync failure (e.g. integration token revoked) → dismissible red error banner, ticket list
  unchanged (not cleared).

**Key files:**
- Backend routes: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/tickets/summary` (→ `requirementsSummary`),
  `GET /api/projects/:projectId/tickets` (→ `allTickets`) — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:1119-1127`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.requirementsSummary()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:4910-4944`; `LegacyService.allTickets()` — `legacy.service.ts:4860-4905`
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/requirements/page.tsx`
- API client: `getRequirementsSummary()`, `listAllTickets()`, `RequirementsSummary`/`TicketSourceStats`/`AllSourcesTicket` types — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:2271-2315`
- Related (per-source) endpoints, same page: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/jira/tickets`, `GET /api/projects/:projectId/linear/tickets` (`legacy.controller.ts:1065`, `1102`)

---

### Activity Feed

**What it is:** A project-scoped, paginated audit log (`/projects/:id/activity`) showing every
create/update/delete action across suites, plans, cycles, bugs, and finer-grained actions (test
case edits, Zyra AI actions) captured in a dedicated `audit_logs` table. A condensed version of the
same feed appears on the Project Dashboard.

**Use cases:**
- A manager reviews "what happened this week" and "who did it" for accountability/audit purposes.
- Investigating a specific change (e.g. "who changed this test case's priority and when").
- Distinguishing human-driven changes from AI/Zyra-driven changes (agent actions are visually
  distinct — purple "AI" tone, sparkle avatar).

**Problem it solves:** Gives a single chronological, filterable audit trail spanning multiple
entity types, without needing to check each entity's own edit history separately.

**Features & actions:**
- **Feed construction**: a `UNION ALL` of synthetic "created"/"updated" events derived from
  suites/plans/cycles/bugs timestamp columns, plus real granular rows from the `audit_logs` table
  (which captures things like `testcase_updated`, `testcase_bulk_deleted`, `zyra_created`,
  `zyra_moved_to_suite`, `execution_evidence_uploaded`, etc., each with actor attribution and an
  optional JSON `diff`).
  - **Deduplication rule**: when a `testcase_created`/`testcase_updated` audit row and a sibling
    `zyra_created`/`zyra_updated`/`zyra_archived` row exist for the same entity within 5 seconds of
    each other, the plain `testcase_*` row is dropped — the Zyra-labeled row is kept since it
    carries AI-specific context. (Zyra chat flow logs both; this avoids showing the same mutation
    twice.)
  - A `suite`/`plan`/`cycle` is only shown as "updated" if `updated_at > created_at + 1 second`
    (guards against every row appearing as both created *and* updated immediately after insert).
- **Filters**: Entity type (All / Test cases / Suites / Test plans / Test runs / Bugs / Knowledge
  base — the last is actually 3 entity types combined: `knowledge_folder,knowledge_document,
  knowledge_file`), Actor (Anyone / specific project member), Date range (All time / Today /
  Last 7 days / Last 30 days), and a debounced (300ms) free-text search across entity name, actor
  name, and action.
- **Infinite "Load more" pagination** (30 items/page) rather than numbered pages.
- **Grouped-by-date rendering**: "Today" / "Yesterday" / full weekday+date headers, sticky within
  the scroll container.
- Each row shows: actor avatar (special gradient "Zyra" sparkle mark for agent actions, initials
  avatar for users, "SY" fallback for system/no-actor events), a colored action badge
  (Created=success/green, Updated=info/blue, Deleted=error/red, Zyra actions=ai/purple,
  Approved/Rejected/Restored/Moved/Renamed/Duplicated/Uploaded have their own tones), entity type +
  icon, entity name, an optional derived one-line description (e.g. "Status changed to Passed.",
  "Moved 3 test cases to this suite.", "2 files attached as evidence.") parsed from the stored
  JSON `diff` — description generation explicitly never invents narrative for actions lacking real
  diff data (returns `null`, hides the description line, rather than fabricating text).
  - Relative time (e.g. "2h ago") + absolute timestamp shown together (absolute also as a tooltip).
- **Right-hand summary sidebar** (`/activity` page only, not shown on dashboard):
  - "This week" panel: Created / Updated / AI Actions / Deleted counts + Total, all scoped to the
    trailing 7 days.
  - "Active members" leaderboard: top 6 actors (users or the Zyra agent) by action count in the
    last 7 days, each with a proportional bar relative to the top actor.
  - "By entity type" breakdown: count per entity type, trailing 7 days.
  - Entire summary sidebar is hidden if `weekly.total === 0` (no activity at all this week).
- Empty state (no activity ever): "No activity yet" / "Actions like creating test cases, updating
  suites, and Zyra AI actions will appear here."

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- New project with zero activity → empty state shown, summary sidebar hidden entirely (not shown
  as all-zero).
- A `testcase_updated` + `zyra_updated` pair logged within 5 seconds for the same entity → only
  the `zyra_updated` row should appear in the feed (verify the dedup window boundary, e.g. events
  4.9s apart vs. 5.1s apart).
- A suite/plan/cycle whose `updated_at` is within 1 second of `created_at` (e.g. auto-touched by a
  trigger right after insert) → should NOT show a spurious "updated" event.
- Filtering by a specific actor who has performed zero actions in the selected date range → empty
  feed, no crash.
- Search term matching only inside a JSON `diff` field (not name/actor/action) → should NOT match
  (search is only against entity_name/actor_name/action).
- "Load more" at the exact boundary of `total` results → button should disappear once
  `activities.length >= total`, not show an extra empty click.
- Actor who has since been deleted/removed from the project — verify the activity row still
  renders (via stored actor_name/actor_email at time of action) rather than erroring.
- Combined "Knowledge base" filter (3 entity types in one filter option) — verify it correctly
  matches all three underlying `entity_type` values.
- Diff-derived descriptions for malformed/non-JSON `diff` strings must fail gracefully (parsed via
  a `safeParseDiff` that catches JSON errors and returns `null`) rather than crashing the row.

**Key files:**
- Backend routes: `GET /api/projects/:projectId/activity` (→ `listActivity`), `GET /api/projects/:projectId/activity/summary` (→ `activitySummary`) — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:1129-1137`
- Backend logic: `LegacyService.listActivity()` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts:2584-2623`; shared SQL builder `activityEventsSql()` — `legacy.service.ts:2630-2735`; `LegacyService.activitySummary()` — `legacy.service.ts:2740-2791`
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/activity/page.tsx`
- Also embedded (condensed, last-10) on: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/dashboard/page.tsx`
- API client: `listActivity()`, `getActivitySummary()`, `ActivityLogItem`/`ActivitySummary` types — `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts:2619-2664`

---

### Notifications

**What it is:** A notification bell icon in the global top bar — currently **entirely
unimplemented** on both backend and frontend. This is a stub/placeholder feature, not a working
one, and should be treated as such in test planning.

**Use cases (intended, not yet functional):** presumably alerting a user to activity relevant to
them (mentions, assigned bugs, completed AI tasks, etc.) without needing to check the Activity
feed manually.

**Problem it solves:** Not currently solved — no notification is ever generated, stored, delivered,
or marked read anywhere in the system today.

**Features & actions (current actual behavior):**
- `GET /api/notifications` always returns a hardcoded empty array `[]`, regardless of user or
  workspace — no query parameters, no auth-scoping logic, no database table backing it.
- `POST /api/notifications/:id/read` is a literal no-op — the handler body is empty (`{}`),
  returns nothing, does not validate that `:id` exists, and does not persist any state.
- The bell icon (`IconBell`) in `TopBar.tsx` renders unconditionally on every authenticated page,
  but has **no `onClick` handler, no unread-count badge, no dropdown/panel, and makes no API call**
  — it is purely decorative.
- No frontend API client function exists for notifications at all (`lib/api.ts` has zero
  `notification`-related exports) — confirmed the frontend does not even attempt to call
  `/api/notifications`.

**Validation / edge cases worth testing:**
- Confirm clicking the bell icon does nothing observable (no dropdown opens, no console error,
  no network request) — this is *expected* current behavior, not a bug, but worth a regression
  test to catch the day someone wires up the endpoint without updating this doc/tests.
- Confirm `GET /api/notifications` returns `[]` for any authenticated user (should not 401/500).
- Confirm `POST /api/notifications/:id/read` with any `:id` (including a nonexistent/malformed one)
  returns success/empty rather than erroring — since there's no validation, this is a low-value but
  cheap smoke test.
- **Recommendation for the QA roadmap**: flag this as "not implemented" rather than writing deep
  functional test cases against it; revisit once real notification generation/storage/delivery
  exists.

**Key files:**
- Backend routes: `GET /api/notifications`, `POST /api/notifications/:id/read` — `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts:1139-1145` (both stub bodies, no service method call)
- Frontend: bell icon markup only, `Tesbo-Frontend/components/TopBar.tsx:54-60` — no state, no handler, no API integration

---

### Appendix: Adjacent stub/legacy endpoints (not user-facing features today)

Two additional routes live in the same controller region and are worth flagging to QA as
non-functional placeholders rather than real features, so they aren't mistakenly tested as if they
compute real data:

- **`GET /api/cycles/:cycleId/report/summary`** (`legacy.controller.ts:587-590`) — hardcoded to
  always return `{ total: 0, passed: 0, failed: 0, blocked: 0, skipped: 0, untested: 0 }` for
  *any* `cycleId`, including invalid/nonexistent ones. No corresponding frontend API client call
  was found anywhere in `lib/api.ts` — appears to be dead code / superseded by the Execution
  Report and per-cycle detail views.
- **`GET /api/projects/:projectId/tesbo-reports/{runs,specs,tests,analytics,alerts,settings}`**
  (`legacy.controller.ts:1182-1210`) — an entire family of endpoints (likely for a future
  "automated test run ingestion" integration) that all return static empty/placeholder payloads
  (empty arrays, or fixed objects like `{ totalRuns: 0, totalTests: 0, passRate: 0, byStatus: {},
  runsByDay: [] }` and default settings `{ keepTrace: true, traceRetentionDays: 14,
  ingestionApiKey: "", alertsEnabled: false, shareByDefault: false }`). No frontend page consumes
  these as of this writing — treat as out-of-scope for functional test planning until real logic
  lands.

## Section F — AI-Powered Test Generation & the Zyra Agent

Scope: `/api/projects/:projectId/ai/*`, `/api/projects/:projectId/agents/zyra*`, workspace-level `/api/workspace/ai-keys*`, and all related frontend screens under `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/agents/*` and `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/settings/ai-providers*`.

All AI features in Tesbo are **bring-your-own-key (BYOK)**: there is no Tesbo-hosted LLM. A workspace owner registers an OpenAI/Anthropic/custom-provider API key at the workspace level, then allocates exactly one key to each project. Every AI feature (test generation, Zyra chat, Zyra tasks) is a no-op/blocked state until a key is allocated to the current project.

---

### AI Test Case Generation

**What it is:** A backend capability (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/ai/generate-testcases`, service method `aiGenerate` → async worker `processZyraTask`) that takes a free-text user story/context and produces AI-drafted test case candidates, grounded in the project's knowledge base, Jira/Linear tickets, existing test case repository, and Zyra's running memory. In the current product this endpoint is not called from its own dedicated screen — it is the same method invoked by "Create task" on the **Zyra → Task board** (`POST /agents/zyra/tasks` routes to the identical `aiGenerate` handler), so end users experience it as "creating a Zyra task," not as a standalone generator.

**Use cases:**
- A QA engineer pastes a user story ("As a user, I want to reset my password...") and lets Zyra draft a first pass of test cases instead of writing them from scratch.
- A tester attaches specific Jira/Linear tickets and/or knowledge-base documents so generation is grounded in real requirements rather than the story text alone.
- A team wants generation to avoid duplicating existing coverage — Zyra is given a snapshot of nearby existing test cases and instructed not to re-cover them.

**Problem it solves:** Removes the blank-page problem of manually authoring test cases from a requirement, and shortens the loop from "ticket written" to "test cases exist" by drafting candidates a human only needs to review, edit, and accept.

**Features & actions:**
- Submit a generation request with: `userStory`/`story` (required, free text — 400 if empty), `context`/`prompt` (optional extra context), `acceptanceCriteria` (optional), `jiraIssueKeys[]`, `linearIssueKeys[]` (tickets to pull summary/description from local sync cache), `knowledgeItemIds[]` (specific KB documents to ground on; if omitted, the most-recently-updated KB documents + files are used automatically), `feedback` (optional, seeds a first round of "apply this feedback" instructions), `provider`/`model` override (falls back to the project's allocated key's provider/default model).
- Request is persisted immediately as an `ai_generation_requests` row with `task_status = 'todo'` and returned synchronously (`generationRequestId`, empty `drafts: []`) — generation itself runs **asynchronously** in `processZyraTask`, fire-and-forget (`void this.processZyraTask(...).catch(() => undefined)`), moving the task through `todo → in_progress → in_review` (or back to `todo` on failure) as it works.
- Test-case count is governed by the project's configured **testcase range** (Zyra → Settings → "Test cases per task"): `minimum` (1–3, hard cap 5), `1-10` (default), `10-30` (aim ≥10), `all` (up to 50, "be exhaustive").
- Generation is blocked with `400 zyra_capability_disabled` if the project's Zyra "generation" capability toggle is off.
- Generation is blocked with `400` "Zyra is inactive. Allocate an OpenAI or Claude key to this project first." if no active workspace AI key is allocated to the project.
- Sources considered and recorded per request (`source_summary`): the story/context text, each selected knowledge-base document/file, each Jira/Linear ticket, and each "existing testcase" nearby match (keyword-scored against the story/context, top 25).
- A running per-project "Zyra AI Memory" knowledge document is read as extra context and updated (via a separate LLM summarization call) after every generation — see Zyra Memory under Zyra Agent Chat.
- Draft schema per generated test case: `title`, `preconditions`, `stepsJson` (JSON string of step objects with `step`/`action`/`expected`), `expectedSummary`, `priority` (`P1`/`P2`/`P3`), `tags[]`.
- Full activity log is recorded per task (`activity_log`): "Task created" → "Waiting for Zyra" → "Picked up task" → "Read available sources" → "Generation plan" (a short natural-language coverage-reasoning blurb) → "Generated testcase drafts" (with token counts) — or "Generation failed" with the raw error message if the AI call throws, leaving the task back in `todo` for retry.
- Token usage (`input`/`output`/`total`, estimated via `estimateTokens` if the provider doesn't report usage) is tracked per task and rolled up project-wide.
- AI provider call: OpenAI (`response_format: json_object`, `prompt_cache_key`, optional `prompt_cache_retention: 24h` for gpt-5/4.1 models) or Anthropic (tries multiple model-name candidates via `anthropicModelCandidates` until one is accepted, since Claude model IDs/aliases shift over time); malformed / non-JSON AI output raises `"AI testcase generation returned invalid JSON"` or `"...returned no testcase drafts"`.
- Downstream lifecycle (reviewing drafts, feedback loop, deleting individual drafts, closing, saving into a suite) is the same as **Zyra Autonomous Tasks** below — this endpoint is the entry point into that lifecycle.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/ai/generate-testcases`, ~line 622; `POST /api/projects/:projectId/agents/zyra/tasks`, ~line 700 — same handler)
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `aiGenerate` (~5954), `processZyraTask` (~6028), `generateZyraWithProvider`/`generateZyraWithOpenAi`/`generateZyraWithAnthropic` (~6745+), `zyraSystemPrompt`/`zyraDynamicTaskPrompt`/`testcaseRangeConfig` (~6760–6824), `normalizeAiDrafts` (~6826)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/agents/tasks/page.tsx` ("Create task" modal calls `createZyraTask`)
- Frontend API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` — `generateAiTestCases()` (wraps the raw `/ai/generate-testcases` route; defined but **not called from any current screen** — dead/legacy client code, only `createZyraTask()` which hits `/agents/zyra/tasks` is actually wired into the UI), `createZyraTask()`
- Migrations: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V8_ai_generation_history.sql`, `V35_zyra_agent_tasks.sql`, `V36_zyra_activity_sources.sql`

**Notable test angles / edge cases:**
- Generating with `story` empty/whitespace-only → expect 400 "story is required".
- Generating with the project's Zyra "generation" capability disabled → expect 400 `zyra_capability_disabled` with guidance text.
- Generating with no AI key allocated to the project → expect 400 "Zyra is inactive...".
- Generating with an allocated but `is_active = false` key → same inactive error, different reason string.
- Provider/model returns malformed JSON or prose instead of JSON → task should fail gracefully back to `todo` with a readable `activity_log` entry, not crash the request.
- Very large `testcaseRange = all` request that would exceed the provider's output-token ceiling (this exact failure mode is why the chat path added scenario-batching — verify whether the *task* path has the same truncation risk).
- Selecting Jira/Linear keys that don't exist in the local sync cache (should just contribute nothing, not error).
- Re-submitting the same story twice — verify duplicate testcase suggestions are suppressed via the "existing testcase" snapshot.

---

### AI Script Review

**What it is:** `POST /api/projects/:projectId/ai/review-script` — a route that exists in the controller but is **entirely stubbed**: it takes no meaningful input and unconditionally returns a fixed, empty response.

```ts
reviewScript() {
  return { status: "passed", summary: "", categories: [], validatedSteps: [] };
}
```

**Use cases:** None currently — presumably intended for reviewing an automation test script (e.g. Playwright/Selenium code) for quality/risk before it's checked in, based on the response shape (`status`, `summary`, `categories`, `validatedSteps`).

**Problem it solves:** Not solved yet — this is a placeholder/未-implemented feature.

**Features & actions:**
- Calling the endpoint with any body/no body always returns `{ status: "passed", summary: "", categories: [], validatedSteps: [] }` regardless of input — no AI call is made, no project/auth validation of the payload occurs beyond whatever global auth guard applies to the controller.
- No frontend page or component calls this route anywhere in the current codebase (`review-script`/`reviewScript` do not appear in `Tesbo-Frontend`).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/ai/review-script` (~line 627, method `reviewScript`), no corresponding service method exists.

**Notable test angles / edge cases:**
- Confirm this is genuinely a no-op in the current build (not accidentally reachable with real behavior via some other path) so QA doesn't waste cycles writing functional test cases against it.
- If/when this is implemented, the response shape (`status: passed|failed`, `summary`, `categories[]`, `validatedSteps[]`) is already the contract to test against.
- Flag to the roadmap owner that this is a documented gap, not a working feature — worth a product decision on whether to build it or remove the dead route.

---

### AI Generation History

**What it is:** A read/audit view over every AI generation request ever created for a project (`GET /api/projects/:projectId/ai/generation-history`) and a way to record which of its drafts were actually saved into the repository (`POST /ai/generation-history/:requestId/save`). Functionally this is the same `ai_generation_requests` table that backs Zyra Tasks — "history" is the append-only record, `aiSave` is the write path used both by the standalone flow and by `zyraSave`.

**Use cases:**
- Auditing how many test cases an AI-driven request generated vs. how many a reviewer actually kept, for measuring Zyra's "approval rate."
- Tracing which suite/testcases came from which historical AI request (`save_events` records `{suiteId, testcaseIds, savedAt}` per save action).

**Problem it solves:** Gives traceability/accountability for AI-authored content — nothing gets silently generated and saved without a recorded trail of what was requested, what was produced, and what was kept.

**Features & actions:**
- `GET .../ai/generation-history?limit=&offset=` — paginated list (`limit` capped at 100, default 50) of all `ai_generation_requests` rows for the project, newest first, camelCased in full (includes `userStory`, `generatedPayload`, `taskStatus`, `activityLog`, `tokenInput/Output/Total`, etc.) — no filtering by status/agent in the query itself (all rows returned regardless of `agent_name`, unlike the Zyra-specific `zyraAgent()`/`zyraTask()` reads which filter `agent_name = ANY(ZYRA_AGENT_NAMES)`).
- `POST .../ai/generation-history/:requestId/save` — records a save event: appends `{suiteId, testcaseIds, savedAt}` to `save_events`, increments `saved_count` by `testcaseIds.length`, appends an "Accepted and saved testcases" activity entry, and force-sets `task_status = 'done'`. Does **not** itself create test cases — it only records that a save happened (`zyraSave` calls this after actually creating/updating test cases).
- Because `aiSave` unconditionally sets `task_status = 'done'` and blindly trusts `body.testcaseIds`/`body.suiteId` without verifying they belong to the given `requestId`/project, this endpoint could be called directly with a mismatched/arbitrary request id or fabricated counts — worth testing as a data-integrity boundary.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/ai/generation-history` (~632), `POST .../generation-history/:requestId/save` (~637)
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `aiHistory` (~6135), `aiSave` (~6145)
- Frontend API client only: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` — `listAiGenerationHistory()`, `trackAiGenerationSaved()` — **neither is called from any page/component** in the current frontend (no history browsing UI exists today; the only "history" a user sees is the Zyra Task board, which reads via `zyraAgent()`/`zyraTask()`, not this endpoint).

**Notable test angles / edge cases:**
- Requesting history with `limit` > 100 → confirm it's clamped to 100, not rejected or unbounded.
- Calling the `/save` endpoint with a `requestId` that doesn't exist — currently has **no existence check** (no `NotFoundException`), the `UPDATE ... WHERE id = $1 AND project_id = $2` simply matches zero rows silently and returns success; worth flagging as a gap (silent no-op instead of a 404).
- Calling `/save` with `testcaseIds` referencing test cases that don't exist / belong to a different project — same silent-trust concern, since this call only records counts, it doesn't validate.
- Since there is no dedicated UI, this is effectively an internal/API-only surface today — testing should treat it as a backend contract check rather than an end-to-end UI flow.

---

### AI Provider Configuration

**What it is:** Workspace-level bring-your-own-key management for AI providers (`/api/workspace/ai-keys*`), plus a one-key-per-project allocation model. This is the gate that every AI feature (generation, Zyra chat, Zyra tasks) checks before doing anything.

**Use cases:**
- A workspace owner adds an OpenAI and/or Anthropic key once, then decides which project(s) may use which key.
- A workspace running multiple client engagements keeps separate keys per client/project for cost isolation and key rotation.
- A team wants to point Zyra at a self-hosted or third-party OpenAI-compatible endpoint (Groq, Together, Ollama, etc.) rather than OpenAI/Anthropic directly.

**Problem it solves:** Keeps API keys out of application config/environment and under workspace-owner control, with per-project opt-in rather than a single global key silently used everywhere; also keeps Tesbo provider-agnostic instead of hard-coding one vendor.

**Features & actions:**
- **List keys & allocations** — `GET /api/workspace/ai-keys` returns all `workspace_ai_keys` for the org (with `maskedKey`, never the raw key) plus every project in the org with its current `workspace_ai_key_id` allocation (or null).
- **Create/update a key** — `POST /api/workspace/ai-keys`: `name` (required, unique per org — upsert on conflict), `apiKey` (required), `provider` (`openai` | `anthropic` | arbitrary custom string), `defaultModel`, `baseUrl` (required for any non-openai/anthropic provider), `authHeaderName`/`authScheme` (only meaningful for custom providers — known providers use built-in auth conventions: Anthropic → `x-api-key` header, OpenAI → `Authorization: Bearer`). Owner-only (`403` for non-owners).
- **Delete a key** — `DELETE /api/workspace/ai-keys/:keyId`, owner-only. (No check that it isn't currently allocated to a project — deleting an allocated key leaves the allocation dangling, which then surfaces as "key not found"/inactive at generation time.)
- **Allocate a key to a project** — `POST /api/workspace/ai-keys/allocations` with `{projectId, workspaceAiKeyId}` (or `workspaceAiKeyId: null`/omitted to unallocate). Owner-only; validates the project and key both belong to the caller's org (`404` otherwise). One allocation per project (upsert via `ON CONFLICT (project_id)`).
- **Test connection** (project-scoped) — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/agents/zyra/test`: sends a minimal 5-token completion request to the allocated key's provider and reports `{ok, provider, model, latencyMs, error?}`. Surfaces human-readable, actionable errors for common failure classes (invalid/revoked key → 401, permission/model-access → 403, rate limit, etc.) via `describeProviderError`.
- **Provider details (read-only view)** — `/settings/ai-providers/details` shows each key's provider, default model, resolved API base URL (provider default shown if not overridden), and auth header/scheme + masked key, for any workspace member (management actions are owner-only, shown as "Owner only").
- Model auto-normalization: `normalizeProviderModel` / `anthropicModelCandidates` reconcile a stored/typed model name against what's actually callable at request time (Claude model aliases shift; multiple candidate IDs are tried in order until one succeeds).
- Every AI feature checks allocation freshly per call via `zyraAiAllocation(projectId)`, which distinguishes three "not usable" reasons surfaced to the user: (a) no key allocated at all, listing what active workspace keys *do* exist ("Active workspace AI key(s) exist (openai (2)), but none is allocated to this project."), (b) a key is allocated but inactive/deactivated, (c) no active workspace key exists in the org at all.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` — `GET/POST /api/workspace/ai-keys` (~116–124), `DELETE /api/workspace/ai-keys/:keyId` (~126), `POST /api/workspace/ai-keys/allocations` (~131), `GET /api/projects/:projectId/agents/zyra/test` (~647)
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `aiKeys` (~1017), `createAiKey` (~1044), `deleteAiKey` (~1079), `allocateAiKey` (~1086), `zyraAiAllocation` (~398), `testZyraAiConnection` (~5056), `describeProviderError` (~453)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/settings/AiProvidersTab.tsx` (main management UI, embedded in `/settings?tab=ai`), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/settings/ai-providers/page.tsx` (redirects to `/settings?tab=ai`), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/settings/ai-providers/details/page.tsx` (read-only provider detail cards)
- Frontend (per-project connection test UI): `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/agents/zyra/settings/page.tsx` ("Test connection" button + result banner)
- Migrations: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V29_workspace_ai_keys.sql`, `V37_workspace_ai_custom_providers.sql`, `V42_fix_known_provider_auth_fields.sql`

**Notable test angles / edge cases:**
- Non-owner attempting to create/delete/allocate a key → expect 403 for all three write endpoints; read (`GET ai-keys`) should still work for any workspace member (used to populate the allocation dropdown, though the UI hides the "manage" affordances for non-owners).
- Creating a custom-provider key without a `baseUrl` → expect 400.
- Creating a key with a `name` that already exists in the org → upsert behavior (overwrites provider/apiKey/model/etc. of the existing row) rather than erroring — verify this is the intended UX (silently replacing a key by reusing its name) vs. a duplicate-name error.
- Deleting a key that is currently allocated to one or more projects → verify the resulting user-facing state in Zyra (should read as "allocated but key not found"/inactive, not crash).
- Testing connection with a genuinely invalid key → expect the friendly `describeProviderError` message, not a raw provider error dump.
- Testing connection with a valid key but a model name the account can't access → expect the permission-error branch.
- Allocating a key belonging to a different organization's workspace by guessing/forging IDs → expect 404 (cross-org isolation check).
- Switching a project's allocated key mid-conversation/mid-task — verify in-flight Zyra chat/task generation doesn't silently mix providers oddly (a new call always re-reads allocation fresh, so this should just take effect on the next call).

---

### Zyra Agent Chat

**What it is:** A conversational AI assistant ("Zyra") scoped to one project, exposed as a full chat UI (`/projects/[id]/agents/zyra`) backed by `agents/zyra/chat/sessions*` routes. Zyra can *converse* (answer QA/product questions), *generate* new test case drafts, *update*/*archive* existing test cases, *create/organize suites*, and *report on Jira coverage* — all as first-class chat actions, not just text replies — grounded in the project's knowledge base (via hybrid ANN+FTS RAG retrieval), Jira/Linear tickets, existing test case repository, and its own running memory.

**Use cases:**
- "Generate smoke tests for checkout" → Zyra drafts and (if storage capability is on) saves new test cases directly from chat.
- "Find coverage gaps" → Zyra analyzes existing coverage and answers analytically without mutating anything.
- "Move the last 12 tests you generated into a new suite called Regression" → Zyra creates the suite and reassigns exactly those test cases using `fromLastPlan` tracking (durable server-side memory of the last generated batch, not reliant on the model re-reading chat history).
- "Archive TC-42, it's obsolete" → Zyra proposes the archive, asks for explicit confirmation, and only archives on a clear "yes."
- "Generate every possible test case for the login flow" (exhaustive/"all possible" requests) → Zyra plans a scenario todo-list, generates the first batch inline, and streams the rest in the background across several chat messages, pausable/resumable by the user.
- "How many Jira tickets don't have test coverage yet?" → Zyra runs a dedicated Jira-coverage tool query and reports real counts rather than guessing.

**Problem it solves:** Turns test-case authoring, triage, and repository organization into a natural-language workflow instead of a form-driven one, while still routing every actual repository mutation through the same governed capability/permission checks as the rest of the product (nothing is created/updated/archived/moved unless the relevant Zyra capability toggle is on).

**Features & actions:**

*Sessions*
- List sessions: `GET .../chat/sessions` — up to 50 most-recently-updated sessions per project, with title/timestamps/`activePlan`.
- Create a session: `POST .../chat/sessions` (optional `title`, defaults to "Zyra chat", auto-truncated to 240 chars). The chat page auto-creates a session on first load if none exist, and auto-opens the most recent one otherwise.
- Open a session: `GET .../chat/sessions/:sessionId` — full message history (`role`, `content`, `reasoningSummary`, `actionType`, `status`, `testcases[]`, `activity[]`) plus `activePlan` state.
- Sidebar UI: switch between sessions, see relative-updated-time, create a "New" session at any time.
- Session auto-titling: the first user message is compacted (whitespace-collapsed, 72 chars) into the session title once (only replaces the default "Zyra chat" title, never overwrites a later custom title).

*Sending a message / intent routing*
- `POST .../chat/sessions/:sessionId/messages` with `{message}` (400 if blank). The backend first runs cheap local regex-based intent detection (`detectZyraChatIntent`: create / update / archive / list / suite / jira_pending_testcases / example / answer) as a hint, then asks the model to choose one of: `answer`, `list`, `jira_pending_testcases`, `create`, `update`, `archive`, `create_suite`, `move_to_suite`.
- **Answer** — conversational/analytical response only (product/feature/strategy questions, coverage-gap analysis, examples/how-to). No mutation, no operations emitted.
- **List** — shows existing test case/coverage rows in a rendered table (no mutation).
- **Create** — generates new test case drafts via `generateZyraChatCreateDecision`; if capability `testcaseStorage` is on, drafts are actually persisted as real test cases (via `createTestCase`) and shown with `action: "created"`; if storage is off, capability gate `applyStorageGateToGenerated` downgrades the reply to "these are suggestions only — I did not save them."
- **Update** — finds an existing test case (by `testcaseId` or `externalId`) and patches allow-listed fields (`title`, `description`, `preconditions`, `postconditions`, `stepsJson`, `testData`, `priority`, `severity`, `type`, `automationStatus`, `automationTags`, `component`, `status`, `jiraIssueKey`, `jiraUrl`).
- **Archive** — the model is explicitly instructed to *never* archive without first describing the target(s) and getting an explicit "yes/confirm/go ahead" reply in the immediately following user turn; archiving sets `status = "Archived"` rather than hard-deleting.
- **Suite ops** — `create_suite` (create/reuse-by-case-insensitive-name a suite) and `move_to_suite` (reassign existing test cases' `suite_id`): targets can be named explicitly (`externalIds`/`testcaseIds`), `allExisting: true` (every non-archived test case not already in that suite), or `fromLastPlan: true` (every test case from the most recently *completed* generation batch in this session — tracked server-side in `last_completed_plan`, durable across a multi-batch plan even though chat history context is capped at the last 12 messages). Suite ops never create test cases.
- **Jira pending-coverage tool** — `jira_pending_testcases` intent runs a dedicated SQL analysis (`analyzeZyraJiraTestcaseCoverage`): total Jira tickets, tickets with ≥1 active linked test case, pending tickets, coverage %, and a table of the pending tickets — then the raw tool result is handed back to the model to phrase as a final natural-language answer (model is instructed not to invent numbers beyond the tool result).
- Every capability the model *could* invoke is hard-gated twice: once informationally in the system prompt (model told to decline and explain if a capability is off) and again as a server-side enforcement pass in `applyZyraChatOperations` that silently drops any operation whose capability is disabled — so a jailbroken/malformed model response can never bypass project settings.
- Reply text is markdown (headings, bold, bullets, tables) rendered client-side by a small custom Markdown-to-HTML renderer (`renderMarkdown`/`mdTable`/`mdInline`) — not a full CommonMark implementation, so unsupported syntax (nested lists, links, images, blockquotes) will render as plain escaped text.
- A `reasoningSummary` is returned separately from the reply and shown in a collapsible "Zyra reasoning" `<details>` disclosure per assistant message.

*Exhaustive / "all possible cases" batched generation (the plan/task lifecycle for chat)*
- Detected via message phrasing ("all possible", "as many as possible", "exhaustive", "every scenario", "full coverage", "all types") or by the project's configured testcase range being `all`.
- Zyra first calls a cheap planning pass (`planZyraChatScenarios`) to produce a todo-list of up to 40 distinct scenario labels (never < 2, else falls back to one bounded normal-sized batch to avoid truncation).
- Generates the first batch (5 scenarios) inline and replies immediately ("I identified N distinct scenarios... here are the first 5...").
- Remaining scenarios are handed to a **fire-and-forget background loop** (`continueZyraChatPlan`) that generates and posts each subsequent 5-scenario batch as its own new assistant chat message, polled by the frontend every 3 seconds while `activePlan.status === "running"`.
- **Stop** (`POST .../stop-plan`): pauses the plan (status → `paused`), preserving `remainingScenarios`/`doneCount`/`totalCount` — an in-flight batch already running server-side is *not* aborted mid-request, it finishes and posts its own message, but the loop checks the plan id before starting the *next* batch and stops if the plan was cleared/paused.
- **Resume** (`POST .../resume-plan`): reactivates a paused plan under a **fresh plan id** (so a stale in-flight batch from before the pause can never collide with the resumed loop) and restarts the background loop; no-ops quietly if there's nothing paused to resume.
- Typing "continue"/"resume"/"keep going"/"carry on"/"go ahead"/"proceed"/"pick up where..." as a plain chat message on a paused plan is equivalent to clicking Resume (`isZyraResumeIntent`).
- Sending **any other** new message while a plan is active/paused supersedes it — the plan is cleared (`active_plan = NULL`) so the new message is treated as a fresh request, not folded into the batch.
- If a mid-plan batch fails (provider error), the plan is paused automatically (not discarded) with a message telling the user how many scenarios are done and inviting "continue."
- If AI key or the "generation" capability becomes unavailable/disabled mid-plan, the loop posts an explanatory message and clears the plan rather than retrying forever.
- Frontend shows a pulsing "Generating remaining scenarios — X/Y covered (Z%)" progress bubble, a paused banner with a "Resume" button, and a "Stop" button next to Send while a plan is running.

*Zyra Memory*
- After every successful chat generation turn (and every task generation turn — shared logic), `rememberZyraTurn` asks the LLM to summarize the turn into 1–3 short durable bullet points (what the user wants, constraints/preferences, what was produced) and appends them to a per-project **"Zyra AI Memory"** knowledge document (auto-created/updated, capped context read at 1500 chars, only `status = 'approved'` memory docs are trusted as context input elsewhere). This lets Zyra "recall" prior sessions' decisions without replaying full chat transcripts. Memory-writing never blocks or fails the user-facing response (falls back silently if the summarization call errors).

*No-key / capability-off states*
- No AI key allocated to the project → chat input is disabled, quick-actions are replaced by an amber "AI provider not connected" banner linking to workspace AI settings and Zyra settings.
- A capability (generation/knowledgeBase/testcaseStorage/suiteOperations) toggled off → Zyra still chats/answers, but declines the specific disabled action with an explanation and a pointer to Zyra → Settings → Capabilities, rather than silently doing nothing or substituting a different mutation.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` — `GET/POST /agents/zyra/chat/sessions` (~657/662), `GET .../sessions/:sessionId` (~667), `POST .../sessions/:sessionId/messages` (~672), `POST .../stop-plan` (~682), `POST .../resume-plan` (~691)
- Backend service (chat core): `legacy.service.ts` — `zyraChatSessions`/`zyraChatSession`/`createZyraChatSession` (~5137–5183), `sendZyraChatMessage` (~5185), `buildZyraChatDecision` (~5319, the intent-routing + system-prompt construction), `applyZyraChatOperations` (~5508, server-side capability enforcement + mutation execution), `stopZyraChatPlan`/`resumeZyraChatPlan`/`continueZyraChatPlan`/`startZyraChatPlan` (~5260–5907), `detectZyraChatIntent` (~7338), `normalizeZyraCapabilities`/`zyraCapabilityDisabled` (~7371–7406), `rememberZyraTurn`/`zyraMemoryText`/`summarizeForZyraMemory` (~6426–6544)
- Backend RAG retrieval: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-retrieval.service.ts` (`retrieveKnowledgeContext` — hybrid ANN vector search + Postgres FTS fusion, used only for chat's free-text knowledge grounding, never throws)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/agents/zyra/page.tsx` (full chat UI: sessions sidebar, message bubbles, markdown renderer, testcase table, thinking/plan-progress bubbles, stop/resume controls, quick-action prompt chips)
- Frontend API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` — `listZyraChatSessions`, `createZyraChatSession`, `getZyraChatSession`, `sendZyraChatMessage`, `stopZyraChatPlan`, `resumeZyraChatPlan`
- Migrations: `V40_rename_zyra_agent.sql`, `V41_zyra_chat_sessions.sql`, `V52_zyra_chat_active_plan.sql`, `V53_zyra_chat_last_completed_plan.sql`

**Notable test angles / edge cases:**
- Sending a message with an empty session (auto-created, no history) — should behave like a first-ever message.
- Ambiguous intent phrasing ("update my coverage" — could read as "update a testcase" or "improve overall coverage answer") — verify the local-intent hint + model resolution lands sensibly.
- Archive flow: asking to archive without following up with an explicit "yes" should NOT archive; a vague follow-up like "ok" — check whether that's treated as confirmation (potential false-positive risk).
- "Move all the tests you just generated into a suite" immediately after a multi-batch exhaustive plan finishes — verify `fromLastPlan` picks up test cases from *all* batches, not just the last one (they're merged/deduped via `recordZyraLastCompletedPlanIds`).
- Stopping a plan, then sending an unrelated new message (not "continue") — plan should be silently superseded/cleared, not resumed later by accident.
- Resuming a plan twice in a row, or resuming a plan that was never paused — should no-op cleanly.
- Disabling `testcaseStorage` mid-conversation right after Zyra proposes drafts but before the user confirms — the next create request should downgrade to "suggestions only."
- Disabling `suiteOperations` and asking to move test cases into a suite — should decline with the capability message, not silently do a partial suite create + skip the move.
- Asking Zyra to reference a Jira ticket key that's well-formed but doesn't exist in the local sync cache.
- Long-running exhaustive plan interrupted by the AI key being deleted/deactivated mid-batch.
- Provider returns prose instead of JSON for a chat turn — verify the fallback wraps it as a plain `answer` reply instead of surfacing a raw parse error to the user.
- Rendering a reply containing literal `{`/`[` at the start of otherwise-prose text (the JSON-unwrap heuristic in `sanitizeZyraReply`/`resolveContent` could misfire).

---

### Zyra Autonomous Tasks

**What it is:** A Kanban-style, human-in-the-loop review workflow around every AI generation request (`agents/zyra/tasks*`), letting a reviewer inspect Zyra's generated drafts, give feedback for regeneration, delete individual drafts, and selectively save drafts into the real test case repository (creating new test cases or updating already-linked ones for the same Jira/Linear ticket).

**Use cases:**
- A QA lead creates a task from a user story/Jira ticket, waits for Zyra to move it from Todo → In Progress → In Review, then reviews the drafts like a PR before merging them into the suite.
- A reviewer isn't happy with the first pass, writes free-text feedback ("add more negative-path cases, this doesn't cover expired sessions") plus optional extra doc/ticket references, and Zyra regenerates the *same task* in place rather than starting over.
- A reviewer wants only 3 of the 8 generated drafts — selects those 3 and saves them into an existing or brand-new suite; the other 5 stay as drafts (or get individually deleted).
- Closing out a task once done, whether or not everything was saved, to remove it from the active queue.

**Problem it solves:** Gives AI-authored test cases a review/approval gate instead of writing straight into the repository, with a full audit trail (activity log, sources, token usage) per task and a regenerate-with-feedback loop that doesn't lose the original story/context/tickets.

**Features & actions:**
- **Task board views** — "Task window" (flat list: story, status chip, Jira badges, generated count, token total) and "Kanban board" (columns: Pending/todo, In Progress, In Review, Done) with per-card Jira badges and counts; clicking a row/card opens a slide-over **Task Quick View** panel (tabs: Test cases, Feedback/Activity, Sources, Activity) with stats (test cases, tokens used, approval rate = saved/generated %) and a "Close task" / "View full task" action.
- **Full task detail page** (`/agents/tasks/[taskId]`) — tabs for Generated Testcases (table with per-row Save/Delete, bulk select-all/clear/save-selected/delete-selected), Activities (full timeline), Sources (every input Zyra considered: story, context, KB items, Jira/Linear tickets, existing-testcase matches, feedback references).
- **Create task** (`POST /agents/zyra/tasks`, same `aiGenerate` handler as AI Test Case Generation above) — modal form: Story (required), Context, Jira ticket picker (auto-appends ticket summary/description into story/context, only shown if Jira is connected), Knowledge Base doc picker (multi-select); disabled entirely if Zyra is inactive (no key).
- **Get task** (`GET .../tasks/:taskId`) — 404 if the task doesn't belong to this project or isn't a Zyra-agent-authored row (`agent_name` filter covers both the current `"Zyra the Test Generator"` and legacy `"Zyra the Edge Hunter"` names, so old tasks keep working after the rename).
- **Send feedback** (`POST .../tasks/:taskId/feedback`) — free-text `feedback` (required, else 400) + optional `referenceNote` (docs/tickets to fold into knowledge context) + optional additional `jiraIssueKeys`/`linearIssueKeys` to merge with the task's originals; this **reopens** the task (`task_status` → `todo` → `in_progress` internally as it reruns → `in_review` again), regenerates drafts against the *combined* original + new context, and accumulates token usage (not reset). Blocked with the same "Zyra is inactive" error if no key is allocated (even though the task already exists).
- **Delete a single draft** (`DELETE .../tasks/:taskId/drafts/:draftIndex`) — index-bounds-checked (400 "Invalid testcase draft index" if out of range/non-integer), splices it out of `generated_payload`, decrements `generated_count`, logs an activity entry with the removed draft's title. The frontend also supports "delete selected" (multiple drafts at once, applied index-descending client-side to avoid index-shift bugs).
- **Close task** (`POST .../tasks/:taskId/close`) — force-sets `task_status = 'done'` regardless of how many drafts were saved; logs "Closed task... without saving additional testcase drafts." Available from both the quick-view panel and the full detail page; disabled once already done.
- **Save task drafts** (`POST .../tasks/:taskId/save`) — `selectedDraftIndexes[]` (defaults to *all* drafts if omitted) + either an existing `suiteId` or a `suiteName` (auto-creates the suite). For each selected draft: if the task is linked to a Jira/Linear ticket that *already* has a linked test case (oldest-first match), the draft **updates that existing test case in place** (tag `zyra-regenerated`) instead of creating a duplicate; otherwise it creates a new test case (tag `zyra-generated`), always tagging with `zyra` + `jira:<key>`/`linear:<key>` as applicable. Internally also calls `aiSave` to record the save event/mark the task done. Returns `{savedCount, suiteId, testcases[]}`.
- Task detail statuses shown to the user only ever include `todo`/`in_progress`/`in_review`/`done` in practice — the frontend's `ZyraTask` type also carries legacy `accepted`/`rejected` values (mapped: `accepted`→done styling, `rejected`→todo styling) but **no current backend code path ever sets those two statuses**, so any UI/tests branching on them are effectively unreachable with the present implementation (worth confirming as intentional dead code vs. a removed feature).
- Every task shows an "Approval rate" stat (`savedCount / generatedCount`) — because task_status never reaches `accepted`/`rejected`, the Agents-page-level aggregate approval rate (computed across *all* tasks by counting `accepted`/`rejected` statuses) will always render as "—" (no data) today; the per-task quick-view approval rate (saved/generated ratio) is the one that actually populates.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` — `POST /agents/zyra/tasks` (~700), `GET .../tasks/:taskId` (~705), `POST .../tasks/:taskId/feedback` (~710), `DELETE .../tasks/:taskId/drafts/:draftIndex` (~720), `POST .../tasks/:taskId/close` (~725), `POST .../tasks/:taskId/save` (~730)
- Backend service: `legacy.service.ts` — `zyraTask` (~5104), `zyraFeedback` (~6164), `zyraDeleteDraft` (~6290), `zyraCloseTask` (~6317), `zyraSave` (~6338), `formatAiTask` (~7772, shared row-shaping for all task reads)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/agents/tasks/page.tsx` (board + create-task modal), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/agents/tasks/[taskId]/page.tsx` (full detail page: drafts table, feedback form, activities, sources, save-to-suite modal), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/agents/TaskQuickViewPanel.tsx` (slide-over quick view)
- Frontend API client: `lib/api.ts` — `createZyraTask`, `getZyraTask`, `sendZyraFeedback`, `deleteZyraTaskDraft`, `closeZyraTask`, `saveZyraTask`
- Migrations: `V35_zyra_agent_tasks.sql`, `V36_zyra_activity_sources.sql`

**Notable test angles / edge cases:**
- Deleting a draft at an out-of-range or negative index → expect 400, not a silent no-op or crash.
- Deleting multiple drafts via "Delete selected" and confirming indexes don't shift incorrectly (frontend sorts descending before calling the API sequentially — verify no off-by-one after each delete).
- Saving with `selectedDraftIndexes` omitted → confirm *all* current drafts save, including ones added by a later feedback regeneration.
- Saving into a brand-new suite name that happens to case-insensitively match an existing suite → should reuse rather than duplicate (mirrors `resolveOrCreateSuiteByName` chat behavior — confirm `zyraSave`'s own `createSuite` call for `suiteName` doesn't bypass that dedupe).
- Sending feedback on a task whose original Jira/Linear tickets are re-referenced plus new ones added — verify the merged (deduped) ticket-key set is what's actually used for regeneration context, and both old and new sources appear in the Sources tab.
- Sending feedback when the project's AI key was removed after the task was originally created — expect the same "Zyra is inactive" block.
- Closing a task that still has unsaved drafts — confirm those drafts are simply abandoned (not saved, not deleted) and the task can't be reopened via feedback afterward (`done` tasks: verify whether feedback/save/delete are actually blocked server-side, since the frontend disables the buttons but the API endpoints themselves don't appear to check `task_status === 'done'` before acting — worth confirming whether a done task can still be mutated by a direct API call).
- Saving drafts for a task linked to a Jira ticket that already has a linked test case from a *prior* (different) task — confirm the "update in place" match is scoped correctly and doesn't cross-link the wrong test case when multiple tasks reference the same ticket.
- Concurrent access: two reviewers opening the same task and saving different draft subsets around the same time.
- Task board's "Approval rate" (Agents page modal stat, aggregate across accepted/rejected) always showing "—" given no code path sets those statuses — confirm this is expected/known rather than a bug to fix.

---

## Section G: Knowledge Base Module

Scope: project-scoped Knowledge Base v2 (folders, documents, files, search, versioning, AI-memory
approval) plus its RAG/embedding pipeline. The old flat `knowledge_base_items` v1 endpoints are also
covered briefly since they remain routable (superseded, not removed).

---

### Knowledge Base Folders

**What it is:** A per-project hierarchical folder tree ("Knowledge base" root + nested subfolders)
that organizes documents and files, similar to a file-system explorer.

**Use cases:**
- QA engineers organizing requirements, test data, screenshots, API notes, and release notes into a predictable structure.
- Managers restructuring the tree as a project grows (creating subfolders, renaming, moving folders around).
- Anyone browsing the knowledge base via the folder tree in the left panel of the Knowledge Base page.
- Exporting a folder (and everything under it) as a zip for sharing outside Tesbo.

**Problem it solves:** Gives every project a durable, structured place to store human- and AI-authored
knowledge instead of scattering it across chat threads or external docs, and keeps that knowledge
organized enough to be both human-browsable and machine-retrievable (RAG).

**Features & actions:**
- Create folder (`POST /folders`)
  - Requires `name` (trimmed, non-empty) — 400 if blank.
  - Optional `description`.
  - Optional `parentFolderId`; if omitted, defaults to the project's root folder.
  - Folder names must be unique among siblings (DB unique index on `project_id, parent_folder_id, name` where not deleted) — creating a duplicate name under the same parent returns 400 "A folder with this name already exists here".
  - Every project has exactly one root folder (`is_root=true`, unique per project, DB-enforced), auto-created at project creation (`seedKnowledgeBaseDefaults`) — **note: only the root folder is created for new projects**; the six default subfolders (Requirements, Test Data, Screenshots & Evidence, API Notes, Release Notes, AI Memory) described in the original migration were only backfilled once for pre-existing projects and are NOT created for projects created after that migration.
