Test: verify a freshly created project's KB tree — it should have only a root folder unless this was fixed.
- Get folder tree (`GET /folders/tree`) — returns the full nested tree (id, parentFolderId, name, description, isRoot, children[]) sorted by name at each level; used to render the sidebar and the "Move to folder" picker.
- Get single folder (`GET /folders/:folderId`) — returns folder + breadcrumb (ancestor chain root→folder).
- List folder items (`GET /folders/:folderId/items`) — returns immediate child folders + documents + files (not deeper descendants), each tagged with `type`, plus `updatedByName/Email`; supports client-side `search` substring filter (matches item name/title, case-insensitive) applied only within that folder's contents.
- Update/rename folder (`PATCH /folders/:folderId`) — updates `name` and/or `description`; same uniqueness constraint as create; requires mutate access (see permissions below).
- Move folder (`PATCH /folders/:folderId/move`)
  - Body: `parentFolderId` (required).
  - Root folder cannot be moved (400).
  - Target parent must exist and not be soft-deleted.
  - **Cycle guard**: a folder cannot be moved into itself or any of its own descendants — checked via a recursive CTE; returns 400 "A folder cannot be moved into itself or one of its subfolders". Test: try moving a folder into its own child/grandchild.
  - Moving into a destination that already has a same-named sibling returns 400.
- Delete folder (`DELETE /folders/:folderId`, soft delete)
  - Root folder cannot be deleted (400).
  - **Cascades**: recursively soft-deletes the folder AND all descendant subfolders, documents, and files in one transaction (all in a single DB transaction so it's atomic).
  - **Important asymmetry**: while the DB rows are only soft-deleted (`is_deleted=true`), the underlying **storage objects for every file under the folder tree are actually deleted from disk/S3 immediately** (best-effort, after the transaction commits) — so restoring a deleted folder later restores file *rows* but their bytes are already gone (download/preview/export of a "restored" file will 404 / fail). Test: delete a folder containing files, restore the folder (or its files), then attempt download/preview — expect failure since storage was already purged.
  - Frontend confirms via `window.confirm` before calling delete ("will also move all contents to trash").
- Restore folder (`PATCH /folders/:folderId/restore`)
  - Owner/manager only (403 for qa_engineer, even the folder's own creator).
  - Only flips `is_deleted=false` on the folder itself — **does not cascade to restore child folders/documents/files** that were soft-deleted along with it. Test: delete a folder with nested content, restore the parent folder, verify children remain deleted/invisible until individually restored.
  - **No UI entry point exists** — `restoreKnowledgeFolder` is implemented in the backend and wired into the frontend API client (`lib/api.ts`) but is never called from any page/component; there is no "Trash"/deleted-items view. Currently reachable only via direct API call. Worth flagging as a gap to confirm intentional.
- Export folder as zip (`GET /folders/:folderId/export`)
  - Bundles the folder + all non-deleted descendant subfolders/documents/files into a `.zip`, preserving folder structure as directories.
  - Documents are exported as self-contained `.html` files (from `content_html`, with basic HTML escaping of the title).
  - Files are re-read from storage under their original file name; a file whose storage object is missing/unreadable is silently skipped (export doesn't fail) — logged as a warning only.
  - Zip filename is `Knowledge base.zip` for the root folder, or `<folder name>.zip` otherwise; names are sanitized for use as zip entry/path segments.
  - Test: export a folder containing a file whose storage object was deleted out-of-band — export should still succeed, minus that file.
- Knowledge base summary (`GET /summary`) — project-wide counts (folders excluding root, documents, files, and `total` = documents+files) shown as stat tiles on the KB page header; independent of which folder is currently selected.
- Permission model for all folder mutations (create/update/move/delete): owners and managers can always mutate; a `qa_engineer` can only mutate a folder **they created** (`kbRequireMutateAccess`) — attempting to edit/move/delete someone else's folder as qa_engineer returns 403 "You can only modify items you created". Restore is always owner/manager-only regardless of who created the item.
- All folder endpoints require the caller to be a member of the project (and the project must belong to the caller's active organization/workspace) — 404 "Project not found" otherwise (not 403, to avoid leaking existence).

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` lines 740–811 (create/tree/summary/export/get/items/move/restore/update/delete), route paths under `/api/projects/:projectId/knowledge-base/folders...`
- Backend service: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `createKnowledgeFolder` (2883), `getKnowledgeFolderTree` (2915), `getKnowledgeFolder` (2934), `knowledgeBaseSummary` (2944), `updateKnowledgeFolder` (2966), `moveKnowledgeFolder` (2988), `deleteKnowledgeFolder` (3026), `restoreKnowledgeFolder` (3077), `exportKnowledgeFolder` (3094), `listKnowledgeFolderItems` (3166), plus helpers `kbFolder`, `kbBreadcrumb`, `kbProjectRole`, `kbRequireOwnerOrManager`, `kbRequireMutateAccess` (2841–2867), `seedKnowledgeBaseDefaults` (1146)
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V45_knowledge_base_v2.sql` (`knowledge_folders` table, uniqueness indexes, default-subfolder backfill)
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/knowledge-base/page.tsx` (folder tree panel, CreateFolderModal, RenameFolderModal, MoveModal, folder actions menu)
- Frontend tree component: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/knowledge-base/FolderTree.tsx` (`FolderTreeNodeRow`, `flattenFolders`, `findAncestorIds`)
- Frontend API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` lines 2409–2474

---

### Knowledge Base Documents

**What it is:** Rich-text documents (TipTap JSON + rendered HTML/plain text) stored inside a folder,
used for requirements, test plans, API notes, release notes, test-data notes, and AI-generated memory.

**Use cases:**
- Writing a test plan, feature requirements, API notes, or release notes directly in Tesbo instead of an external wiki.
- Mirroring external Jira tickets into the KB automatically (as read-only-ish `source_provider='jira'` documents) so they're searchable/usable as AI context alongside manual docs.
- Duplicating an existing document as a starting template for a new one.
- Zyra (the AI assistant) writing/updating a rolling "Zyra AI Memory" scratchpad document automatically.

**Problem it solves:** Gives teams a structured, versioned, searchable place for prose knowledge that
both humans and the AI assistant can read, without needing an external documentation tool.

**Features & actions:**
- List documents (`GET /documents`) — project-wide (not folder-scoped) list of non-deleted documents, optional `documentType` filter, capped at 200 rows, sorted by `updated_at DESC`.
- Create document (`POST /documents`)
  - Requires `title` (trimmed, non-empty → 400) and `folderId` (must reference an existing, non-deleted folder in the project → 400/404).
  - Optional `documentType` (defaults `'general'`; DB check constraint restricts to `general | requirement_note | test_data_note | api_note | release_note | ai_memory`).
  - Optional `contentJson` (TipTap JSON), `contentHtml`, `contentText`.
  - New documents always start at `status='draft'`.
  - Frontend offers 6 starter templates when creating (Blank, Test Plan, Feature Requirements, API Notes, Release Notes, Test Data) that pre-populate heading/bullet skeletons and set the matching `documentType`.
  - Triggers an embedding-pipeline enqueue (`enqueueEmbedding`, reason `"created"`) for RAG indexing.
- Get document (`GET /documents/:documentId`) — returns document + breadcrumb of its folder.
- Update document (`PATCH /documents/:documentId`)
  - Frontend auto-saves 1.2s after the user stops typing (debounced), plus a manual "Save" button; title and editor content are saved together.
  - **Versioning trigger**: if title/HTML/text actually changed vs the stored row, and the most recent version snapshot for this document is older than 15 minutes (or none exists), the *pre-update* state is snapshotted into `knowledge_document_versions` before applying the update — i.e. edits are throttled to at most one version snapshot per 15-minute window, not one per keystroke/save. Test: make several edits within 15 minutes — expect only one prior-state version to be captured; make an edit, wait >15 min, edit again — expect a second version.
  - **AI-memory guard**: for `document_type='ai_memory'`, editing an already-`approved` document silently resets it back to `status='draft'` and clears `reviewed_by`/`reviewed_at` — i.e. any content edit invalidates prior approval and requires re-approval. For ai_memory docs, `status` can ONLY change via the dedicated approve/reject endpoints, not via this generic update (a `status` field in the body is ignored for ai_memory).
  - For non-ai_memory documents, `status` can be set directly via this endpoint (no restriction on values, since ai_memory is the only type with an approval workflow gate).
  - Re-enqueues embedding (reason `"updated"`) only if content actually changed.
  - Enforces mutate-access rule (owner/manager, or the document's own creator).
- Move document to another folder (`PATCH /documents/:documentId/move`) — body `folderId` required, target folder must exist/not be deleted; no cycle check needed (documents aren't parents of anything).
- Duplicate document (`POST /documents/:documentId/duplicate`) — copies title (` (copy)` suffix), content, folder, and document type into a new document at `status='draft'`; always allowed to whoever can read the document (no extra mutate-access check beyond project membership); re-enqueues embedding as a new "created" document.
- Delete document (`DELETE /documents/:documentId`, soft delete) — sets `is_deleted=true`; frontend confirms via `window.confirm`.
- Restore document (`PATCH /documents/:documentId/restore`) — owner/manager only; same "no UI entry point" gap as folder restore (function exists in `lib/api.ts`, never called from any component).
- Document types drive labeling and templates but are otherwise just metadata, except `ai_memory` which gates the approval workflow (see below).
- Full-text search vector (`search_vector`, tsvector) is auto-maintained by a Postgres trigger combining `title` (weight A) + `content_text` (weight B) on every insert/update — used by both keyword search and RAG's FTS leg.
- Jira ticket mirroring: a background sync job upserts Jira issues into the KB as `general` documents (not `ai_memory`) tagged with `source_provider='jira'`/`source_external_id`, filed into the project's "Requirements" folder if one exists (falls back to the root folder if not — relevant given new projects don't get default subfolders, see Folders section).
- Restore-version and AI-memory approval are covered in their own sections below.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 818–891 (list/create/versions/restore-version/approve/reject/get/move/restore/duplicate/update/delete)
- Backend service: `listKnowledgeDocuments` (3212), `createKnowledgeDocument` (3227), `kbDocument` helper (3257), `getKnowledgeDocument` (3266), `updateKnowledgeDocument` (3273, versioning + ai_memory guard logic at 3285–3322), `moveKnowledgeDocument` (3336), `duplicateKnowledgeDocument` (3355), `deleteKnowledgeDocument` (3379), `restoreKnowledgeDocument` (3393)
- Schema: `V45_knowledge_base_v2.sql` (`knowledge_documents` table + `document_type` check constraint, search_vector trigger), `V56_knowledge_embedding_status.sql` (embedding_status/embedding_content_hash columns)
- Frontend page: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/knowledge-base/documents/[documentId]/page.tsx` (editor, autosave, title, duplicate/delete/history/approve-reject menu)
- Frontend list/create UI: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/knowledge-base/page.tsx` (`CreateDocumentModal`, `DOCUMENT_TEMPLATES`, `docNodeToHtml`/`docNodeToText`)
- Rich text editor: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/knowledge-base/RichTextEditor.tsx` (TipTap-based)
- Frontend API client: `lib/api.ts` lines 2478–2546

---

### Document Versioning

**What it is:** An automatic, throttled snapshot history of a document's title/content, browsable and
individually restorable from the document page's "View history" panel.

**Use cases:**
- Recovering from an accidental bad edit or an unwanted AI-driven rewrite.
- Reviewing how a requirements document evolved over time.
- Comparing whether a specific historical wording is what's currently live (no diff view, but titles/timestamps are visible).

**Problem it solves:** Protects against content loss from careless edits or from generic-document
editing (autosave means there's no separate "draft vs published" safety net otherwise).

**Features & actions:**
- List versions (`GET /documents/:documentId/versions`) — returns `id, versionNumber, title, createdBy, createdAt` for all snapshots of a document, newest first (by `version_number DESC`). No content is exposed in the list (would need a per-version detail endpoint to view historical content, which doesn't exist — the frontend only ever *restores* a version, it never previews one before restoring).
- Snapshot creation is implicit, not a user action: triggered inside `updateKnowledgeDocument` whenever content actually changed AND the latest snapshot (if any) is older than 15 minutes (`KB_VERSION_SNAPSHOT_MINUTES`). The snapshot captures the document's state **before** the incoming update is applied.
- Restore version (`POST /documents/:documentId/restore-version`, body `{ versionId }`)
  - Looks up the version row by `id` scoped to `document_id` — restoring a `versionId` that belongs to a *different* document returns 404 "Version not found" (tests: cross-document versionId, non-existent versionId).
  - **Restoring is itself reversible**: before overwriting the live document, the *current* (pre-restore) state is snapshotted as a new version (next `version_number`), so restoring an old version doesn't lose the version you restored *from*.
  - Overwrites `title`, `content_json`, `content_html`, `content_text` on the live document; does NOT touch `document_type` or `status`/approval fields.
  - Logs a `restored_version` activity entry including the restored version number.
  - Enforces the same mutate-access rule as document update (owner/manager, or the document's own creator) — a `qa_engineer` who didn't create the document cannot restore a version even if they can view history.
  - Note: restoring a version does NOT re-enqueue an embedding job explicitly in this handler — worth testing whether RAG search/Zyra context reflects a restored version's content promptly, since `updateKnowledgeDocument` (which does re-embed) is a separate code path from `restoreKnowledgeDocumentVersion`.
- Edge case: restoring a version whose content referenced something now deleted (e.g. an inline image link, or if the document was itself soft-deleted between opening history and clicking restore) — `kbDocument` requires the doc be non-deleted, so restoring a version of an already-deleted document returns 404 "Document not found" via the initial `kbDocument` lookup in `restoreKnowledgeDocumentVersion`.
- Frontend: "View history" opens a modal listing versions with title + "Version N — timestamp"; each row has a "Restore" button; no diff/preview, no delete-a-version, no rename-a-version.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 828–841
- Backend service: `listKnowledgeDocumentVersions` (3753), `restoreKnowledgeDocumentVersion` (3763), snapshot-on-edit logic inside `updateKnowledgeDocument` (3288–3308)
- Schema: `knowledge_document_versions` table in `V45_knowledge_base_v2.sql`
- Frontend: history modal in `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/knowledge-base/documents/[documentId]/page.tsx` (`historyOpen`, `openHistory`, `handleRestoreVersion`, lines ~180-199 and 337-355)

---

### AI Memory Approval

**What it is:** A human-in-the-loop review gate for a special `ai_memory` document type: AI-authored
"project understanding" notes must be explicitly approved by an owner/manager before they're trusted as
context fed back into AI features (Zyra chat/task generation), distinguishing curated memory from
Zyra's own always-trusted rolling scratchpad.

**Use cases:**
- A team lead reviewing an AI-drafted "what this project is about" memory doc before it influences future AI-generated test plans/tasks.
- Rejecting an inaccurate AI memory note so it's excluded from future AI context without deleting it outright.
- Editing an approved memory doc's content and having it automatically fall back to needing re-review (prevents stale approval from covering unreviewed edits).

**Problem it solves:** Prevents unreviewed/possibly-hallucinated AI-authored content from silently
becoming trusted input to further AI generation (a feedback-loop/trust risk), by gating it behind an
explicit human approval step, while still letting Zyra maintain its own private scratchpad memory
unrestricted (since Zyra is both its author and its only reader there).

**Features & actions:**
- Approve (`PATCH /documents/:documentId/approve-ai-memory`)
  - Owner/manager only (403 otherwise, regardless of who authored the document).
  - 400 "Only AI memory documents can be approved" if `document_type !== 'ai_memory'` — i.e. calling this on a general/requirement/etc. document is rejected.
  - Sets `status='approved'`, `reviewed_by=<caller>`, `reviewed_at=now()`.
- Reject (`PATCH /documents/:documentId/reject-ai-memory`) — mirror of approve; sets `status='rejected'`; same owner/manager + type-check gating.
- Editing an approved ai_memory doc via the normal update endpoint silently demotes it back to `draft` (see Documents section) — approval is content-bound, not a one-time flag.
- Only `status='approved'` ai_memory documents are trusted as AI context:
  - `knowledgeSnapshot()` (used by Zyra's explicit document-picker / task-generation context builder) filters with `document_type != 'ai_memory' OR status = 'approved'`.
  - RAG semantic retrieval (`rag-retrieval.service.ts`) applies the identical filter in both its ANN (vector) and FTS legs — an unapproved/rejected/draft ai_memory document is invisible to Zyra's free-text chat retrieval too.
  - Every other document type is trusted unconditionally regardless of `status`.
- Distinct from "Zyra AI Memory" scratchpad: Zyra also maintains its own rolling memory document (title literally `"Zyra AI Memory"`, filed under the project's "AI Memory" folder if it exists, else the root folder) which is stored as a plain `document_type='general'` (NOT `ai_memory`) document with `is_ai_generated=true` — this scratchpad is always trusted without approval, is appended-to automatically after Zyra interactions, and is capped at 20,000 characters (oldest content truncated off the end). It's a different mechanism from the human-reviewed `ai_memory` type despite the similar name — worth distinguishing clearly in test cases (searching/filtering by `documentType=ai_memory` will NOT return the "Zyra AI Memory" scratchpad document).
- Frontend: document page shows an amber/AI-styled banner "This is AI-generated memory. Review before it's trusted as context." with Approve/Reject buttons, visible only when `documentType === 'ai_memory'`, the caller has owner/manager role, AND status is neither already `approved` nor `rejected` (i.e. banner disappears after a decision — there's no "un-approve"/"re-open for review" UI action beyond editing the content, which auto-resets it to draft).
- Status is also surfaced as a colored chip in both the folder listing table (per-row) and the document detail header: draft = neutral, approved = success/green, rejected = error/red.
- Edge case worth testing: a `qa_engineer` (non-owner/manager) who authored an ai_memory document can edit it (if mutate-access allows "items you created") but cannot approve/reject their own submission — approval is strictly role-gated, not creator-gated.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 843–851
- Backend service: `approveAiMemory` (3800), `rejectAiMemory` (3818), `kbRequireOwnerOrManager` (2849), ai_memory-specific branch in `updateKnowledgeDocument` (3313–3319), `knowledgeSnapshot` (6550) and its `ai_memory`/`status='approved'` filter (6555), Zyra scratchpad memory: `rememberZyraMemory` (6522), `kbAiMemoryFolderId` (6510)
- RAG filter: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-retrieval.service.ts` lines 84 (ANN join) and 96 (FTS) — both apply `document_type != 'ai_memory' OR status = 'approved'`
- Schema: `document_type` check constraint + `status`/`reviewed_by`/`reviewed_at` columns in `V45_knowledge_base_v2.sql`
- Frontend: approve/reject banner + StatusChip in `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/knowledge-base/documents/[documentId]/page.tsx` (lines 201-217, 234, 287-291, 325-333) and status chip in the folder listing table in `knowledge-base/page.tsx` (`aiMemoryTone`, lines 220-224, 1104-1124)

---

### Knowledge Base Files

**What it is:** Uploaded binary/text attachments (images, PDFs, Office docs, spreadsheets, code, audio,
video, zips) stored per-folder, with best-effort automatic text extraction so their contents can be
searched and used as AI context.

**Use cases:**
- Attaching a requirements PDF, a Postman export, a CSV of test data, or a screenshot as evidence.
- Uploading a meeting recording (audio/video) and having it auto-transcribed for later reference/search.
- Downloading or previewing an uploaded file directly in-browser without leaving Tesbo.

**Problem it solves:** Lets teams keep binary artifacts alongside their structured documents in one
place, and (via extraction/transcription) makes even non-text file types partially searchable and
usable as AI context, not just documents.

**Features & actions:**
- Upload (`POST /files/upload`, multipart, field name `files`, up to **10 files** per request, `folderId` in form body)
  - Per-file size cap: `MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE` env var, default **50 MB** (`KB_MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE`).
  - `folderId` required and must reference an existing, non-deleted folder; at least one file required (400 otherwise).
  - **Allowed extensions (allowlist, case-insensitive, checked against the whole batch atomically)**: `png jpg jpeg webp svg`, `pdf doc docx txt md`, `xls xlsx csv`, `ppt pptx`, `js ts java py json xml yaml yml sql html css`, `mp3 wav m4a`, `mp4 mov webm`, `zip`. If ANY file in the batch has a disallowed extension, the **whole batch is rejected** (400 naming the offending file) — nothing is written to storage; test uploading a mixed batch of 1 valid + 1 invalid file and confirm the valid one is NOT silently accepted.
  - Extension is derived from the filename (`path.extname`), not the declared MIME type — test uploading a file with a spoofed/mismatched extension vs actual content (e.g. a `.txt`-named PDF) to see how extraction behaves (it will be treated as plaintext, likely garbling binary bytes into `content_text`).
  - **Duplicate filenames within a folder** are auto-disambiguated: `kbUniqueFileName` appends ` (1)`, ` (2)`, etc. to the base name if the exact `original_file_name` already exists (non-deleted) in that folder — no overwrite, no error.
  - Storage key format: `knowledge-base/<organizationId>/<projectId>/<uuid>.<ext>` (never exposes the real filename or a guessable path).
  - **Synchronous text extraction** (blocks the upload response) for supported types:
    - Plaintext passthrough (`txt md csv json xml yaml yml sql html css js ts java py`) — read as UTF-8, capped at 20,000 chars (`KB_EXTRACTED_TEXT_LIMIT`).
    - Spreadsheets (`xls xlsx`) — every sheet converted to CSV text via `XLSX`, concatenated, capped at 20,000 chars.
    - PDF (`pdf`) — text extracted via `pdf-parse`, capped at 20,000 chars.
    - Word (`docx` only — **legacy binary `.doc` is accepted for upload but NOT text-extracted**, `mammoth` only parses Open XML `.docx`) — extracted via `mammoth`, capped at 20,000 chars.
    - Images (`png jpg jpeg` only — **`webp`/`svg` are accepted for upload but never OCR'd**, since the OCR engine's decoder only reliably supports png/jpg/bmp) — OCR'd via Tesseract, requires baked-in `eng.traineddata.gz` at `TESSDATA_PATH` (default `/app/tessdata`); silently returns no text if that data file is missing (e.g. running outside the built container image) — logged as a warning, not an error.
    - Any extraction failure (corrupt file, parser exception) is caught and logged; the file is still created, just with `extracted_text = null`.
  - **Asynchronous transcription** (fire-and-forget, doesn't block upload response) for audio (`mp3 wav m4a`) and video (`mp4 webm` — **`.mov` is accepted for upload but never transcribed**, since the transcription API doesn't accept that container):
    - Only runs if the project has an allocated AI key from provider `openai` specifically (any other/no provider → `extraction_status='unsupported'`, no transcription attempted).
    - Uses OpenAI's `whisper-1` model; sets `extraction_status` to `pending` → `ready`/`failed`/`unsupported` as it progresses.
    - On success, re-enqueues an embedding job (reason `"transcribed"`) since there was no content to embed at upload time.
  - Non-transcribable files enqueue an embedding job immediately (reason `"created"`) if extraction produced any text (implicitly — enqueue is unconditional in code, but the embedding worker itself will mark it `unsupported` if content is empty).
  - Activity log entry `"uploaded"` per file.
- Get file metadata (`GET /files/:fileId`) — returns file row + breadcrumb.
- Rename (`PATCH /files/:fileId`, body `originalFileName`) — only the display name changes; `file_name`/`storage_key` (the actual storage path) are untouched. Enforces mutate-access (owner/manager, or the uploader).
- Move (`PATCH /files/:fileId/move`, body `folderId`) — target folder must exist/not be deleted.
- Delete (`DELETE /files/:fileId`, soft delete) — sets `is_deleted=true` AND **immediately deletes the storage object** (best-effort; a storage failure is logged but doesn't fail the request) — meaning, like folder-cascade delete, restoring a deleted file afterward restores the DB row but not its bytes. Test: delete a file, restore it, then try to download/preview — expect a "File content is not available" 404.
- Restore (`PATCH /files/:fileId/restore`) — owner/manager only; same "no UI entry point" gap as folder/document restore.
- Download (`GET /files/:fileId/download`) — sets `Content-Disposition: attachment`; either redirects (302) to a short-lived S3 presigned URL, or streams the local file, depending on storage backend. 404 "File content is not available" if the storage key is missing or the object doesn't exist on disk (S3 existence isn't actually checked ahead of time — `exists()` always returns `true` for S3, deferring to the signed-URL request itself).
- Preview (`GET /files/:fileId/preview`) — identical to download but `Content-Disposition: inline` so the browser renders it instead of saving it.
- Frontend preview modal only renders certain kinds inline (`getFileViewerKind`): `image` (`png jpg jpeg webp svg`), `pdf`, `video` (`mp4 mov webm`), `audio` (`mp3 wav m4a`), `text` (`txt md csv js ts java py json xml yaml yml sql html css` — note: this list does NOT include `docx/xls/xlsx/ppt/pptx/zip`, which fall to `"unsupported"` → shows a "Preview isn't available" placeholder with a Download button only). Note the frontend text-preview list is a strict subset of the backend's plaintext-extraction list (matches, minus md/csv already there) — consistent.
- Text-kind preview in the modal is fetched via `fetch()` + `res.text()` against the preview URL (not just an `<iframe>`/`<img>` src) — so it goes through the same access-check/streaming path as download.
- Activity log entries for upload/rename/move/delete/restore all recorded via `logProjectActivity`.
- Same owner/manager-vs-creator mutate-access + owner/manager-only-restore permission model as folders/documents.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 893–965 (upload/download/preview/get/move/restore/update/delete)
- Backend service: constants `KB_MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE`, `KB_ALLOWED_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_PLAINTEXT_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_SPREADSHEET_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_PDF_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_DOCX_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_IMAGE_OCR_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_AUDIO_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_TRANSCRIBABLE_VIDEO_EXTENSIONS`, `KB_EXTRACTED_TEXT_LIMIT`, `KB_TESSDATA_PATH` (3410–3437); `extractKnowledgeFileText` (3443), `ocrImageText` (3475), `transcribeKnowledgeFile` (3498), `kbFile`/`kbUniqueFileName` (3533/3542), `uploadKnowledgeFiles` (3556), `getKnowledgeFile` (3606), `updateKnowledgeFile` (3613), `moveKnowledgeFile` (3629), `deleteKnowledgeFile` (3647), `restoreKnowledgeFile` (3663), `getKnowledgeFileAccess` (3680)
- Storage backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/storage/storage.service.ts` (`put`, `exists`, `getBuffer`, `getAccessUrl`, `delete`) — local disk vs S3-compatible, switched via `STORAGE_DRIVER` env var
- Schema: `knowledge_files` table in `V45_knowledge_base_v2.sql`; `V50_knowledge_files_extracted_text.sql`, `V51_knowledge_files_extraction_status.sql`, `V57_knowledge_files_search_vector.sql`
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/knowledge-base/FileViewerModal.tsx` (preview modal), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/fileViewer.ts` (`getFileViewerKind`), `UploadModal` in `knowledge-base/page.tsx` (drag-and-drop + click-to-browse, multi-file staging list before upload)
- Frontend API client: `lib/api.ts` lines 2550–2602

---

### Knowledge Base Search

**What it is:** A project-scoped keyword search across folders, documents, and files, separate from
(and simpler than) the semantic RAG retrieval used internally by Zyra's AI chat.

**Use cases:**
- Quickly finding a document/file/folder by name or content keyword without navigating the folder tree.
- Filtering search results by item type (folder/document/file) or by recency (today/week/month).

**Problem it solves:** Makes the knowledge base navigable by keyword instead of requiring the user to
know exactly which folder something lives in.

**Features & actions:**
- `GET /knowledge-base/search?q=...&type=all|folder|document|file&date=today|week|month`
  - Empty/whitespace-only `q` returns `{ list: [], total: 0 }` immediately (no error, no wildcard-match-everything behavior).
  - **Folders**: matched via `name ILIKE '%q%'` — simple substring, case-insensitive; no ranking.
  - **Documents**: matched via Postgres full-text (`search_vector @@ plainto_tsquery('english', q)`) OR `title ILIKE '%q%'` (so a title substring match works even if FTS wouldn't match, e.g. partial words); ranked by `ts_rank`. Note: `plainto_tsquery` strips stopwords/punctuation and stems words — searching for something the FTS treats as empty (e.g. only stopwords, or certain special characters) still falls back to the ILIKE title check. Test with special characters (`%`, `_`, quotes, non-Latin scripts) to confirm no SQL errors and sane (possibly empty) results — `%`/`_` are ILIKE wildcards themselves but the query is parameterized so they're literal characters, not injected wildcards, which is worth explicitly verifying behaves as "search for a literal percent sign" rather than matching everything.
  - **Files**: matched via `original_file_name ILIKE '%q%' OR file_extension ILIKE '%q%'` only — **does NOT search `extracted_text`** despite `knowledge_files.search_vector`/`extracted_text` existing in the schema (V57) and being used by RAG's FTS leg. This means a keyword search here will NOT surface a file whose filename doesn't match but whose extracted/OCR'd/transcribed content does — that's only reachable via Zyra's semantic chat. Worth an explicit test case: upload a PDF named `report.pdf` containing the word "invoice", search "invoice" here (expect 0 results) vs ask Zyra about "invoice" (expect it to surface via RAG).
  - Each result type capped at 50 rows independently (folders, documents, files each `LIMIT 50` — so `total` can be up to 150 even though no combined limit/pagination exists beyond that).
  - Soft-deleted items are always excluded.
  - Date filter (`today`/`week`/`month`) applies to `updated_at`, appended identically to all three sub-queries; any other/no value = no date filtering.
  - Results are annotated with a breadcrumb (ancestor folder chain) per item before returning.
  - No pagination on the search endpoint itself (unlike the folder-items list, which the frontend paginates client-side after merging with type/sort filters).
- Frontend: single search box in the KB page's filter bar (debounced only via manual Enter/submit — search fires on form submit, not as-you-type/on every keystroke, despite triggering a fresh network fetch whenever `searchQuery` state changes); a "Clear" link resets it; type filter (`all/folder/document/file`) and sort (`updated/name/size`) are applied **client-side** on top of whatever the server already returned (i.e. changing type/sort while a search is active does not re-query the server, it just re-filters/re-sorts the existing `searchResults` array in memory) — worth testing that switching type-filter during an active search doesn't silently drop items that would match a different combination server-side (it can't, by construction, since results are capped at 50/type from the one query).
  - When a search is active, the results table adds a "Folder path" column (breadcrumb) not shown in normal folder-browsing mode.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` line 813–816
- Backend service: `searchKnowledgeBase` (3693)
- Frontend: search box + client-side filter/sort logic in `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/knowledge-base/page.tsx` (lines 510-513, 603-613, 790-799, 1013-1039)
- Frontend API client: `lib/api.ts` `searchKnowledgeBase` (2606–2615)

---

### Knowledge Base RAG / Semantic Retrieval (supporting pipeline)

**What it is:** A background embedding pipeline that chunks and vector-embeds document/file content so
Zyra's free-text AI chat can retrieve relevant knowledge-base context semantically, fused with keyword
full-text search — distinct from (and additive to) the manual keyword `search` endpoint above.

**Use cases:**
- Zyra answering a free-text question by pulling in relevant KB documents/files as context, even when the user's wording doesn't literally match the document text.
- Keeping AI context fresh automatically as documents/files are created/edited/transcribed, without any manual "reindex" action from the user.

**Problem it solves:** Plain keyword/ILIKE search misses semantically-related content that doesn't share exact wording; embeddings let Zyra find conceptually relevant KB content.

**Features & actions:**
- Every document create/update(-with-content-change)/duplicate, and every file create/transcription-completion, calls `enqueueEmbedding` (fire-and-forget, failures swallowed) which:
  - Immediately flips the source's `embedding_status` to `'queued'`.
  - Enqueues a BullMQ job keyed by a deterministic `jobId` (`document-<id>` / `file-<id>`) so concurrent enqueues for the same source dedupe (no duplicate embedding work queued).
- The embedding worker (`RagEmbeddingProcessor`):
  - Re-reads the source's current content (`content_text` for documents, `extracted_text` for files); if the row is gone/soft-deleted by the time the job runs, marks status `'unsupported'` and exits cleanly (no error).
  - Skips (marks `'unsupported'`) if content is empty, or if the project has no usable embedding-capable AI key allocation (e.g. an Anthropic-only project — Anthropic doesn't offer embeddings, so this is expected, not a bug; Zyra silently falls back to keyword search for such projects).
  - **Idempotent via content hash**: computes a SHA-256 of the content; if it matches `embedding_content_hash` already stored, skips re-embedding entirely (no-op) — re-saving a document with unchanged content_text doesn't burn embedding-API calls.
  - Chunks content (`RagChunkingService`): splits on markdown headings first (tracking a "Heading > Subheading" breadcrumb per chunk), then recursively on blank-line/newline/sentence boundaries down to a target size, merging small pieces back up with a small overlap between consecutive chunks; hard-cuts anything still oversized. Capped at a max chunk count per source (excess content is silently dropped, not erroring).
  - Replaces all prior chunks for that source in one transaction (delete + reinsert) — old chunk rows never leak/duplicate across re-embeds.
  - Chunks land in a hash-partitioned (64 buckets by `project_id`) `knowledge_document_chunks` table with an HNSW cosine-similarity index.
- Retrieval (`RagRetrievalService.retrieveKnowledgeContext`) — never throws (any failure anywhere resolves to `[]`, so callers' existing fallback logic stays clean):
  - Runs ANN (vector cosine similarity against the query's own embedding) and FTS (Postgres `plainto_tsquery` against documents and files separately) in parallel.
  - Both legs apply the **same ai_memory-approval filter** as `knowledgeSnapshot` (`document_type != 'ai_memory' OR status = 'approved'`) — unapproved AI memory is invisible here too.
  - Fuses ANN + FTS rankings via Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF) in application code (not SQL, since ANN is chunk-level and FTS is document-level).
  - Returns up to `RAG_MAX_SOURCES` items, trimmed to fit a total character budget (`RAG_CONTEXT_CHAR_BUDGET`), each with a citation (`sourceType`, `sourceId`, `headingPath`).
- Self-healing: `resumeInterruptedEmbeddings` re-enqueues anything stuck in `pending/queued/processing` (e.g. after a crash/restart) — safe to call repeatedly due to the deterministic jobId.
- This pipeline is internal/AI-facing only — there is no direct user-facing endpoint or UI surface for "semantic search"; it's consumed by Zyra's chat feature (outside this module's scope) rather than the Knowledge Base search box.

**Key files:**
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-ingestion.service.ts` (`enqueueEmbedding`, `resumeInterruptedEmbeddings`)
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-embedding.processor.ts` (worker: content-hash idempotency, chunk+embed+store)
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-chunking.service.ts` (heading-aware recursive chunking)
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-retrieval.service.ts` (ANN+FTS fusion, ai_memory approval filter, char-budget trimming)
- `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag.constants.ts`, `rag.types.ts`
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V55_knowledge_document_chunks.sql` (64-way hash-partitioned table + HNSW index), `V56_knowledge_embedding_status.sql`
- Enqueue call sites in `legacy.service.ts`: `enqueueEmbedding` wrapper (328), and call sites at 3253, 3332, 3375, 3526, 3600, 4444, 4816, 6539, 6547

---

### Knowledge Base v1 (legacy flat items — superseded)

**What it is:** The original flat (non-hierarchical) knowledge base model (`knowledge_base_items`: notes
and files with no folders), left routable for backward compatibility but not used by the current
frontend, which is built entirely against the v2 (folders/documents/files) API.

**Use cases:** None in current UI — these routes are dead code from the frontend's perspective, kept only for API/rollback safety after the V45 migration moved data into the new schema.

**Problem it solves:** N/A currently — historical only.

**Features & actions:**
- `GET /knowledge-base` (`listKnowledge`) — list notes/files for a project, optional `type`/`search` (ILIKE on title/content) filters; **no auth/project-membership check** on this handler (`@Param`/`@Query` only, no `@Req`) — unlike every v2 endpoint, this route doesn't call `requireProjectAccess`, meaning (if still reachable) any authenticated-or-not caller who knows a `projectId` could list its legacy notes. Worth a security-focused test: confirm whether this route is actually reachable in production or effectively dead/blocked upstream.
- `POST /knowledge-base` (`createKnowledge`) — creates an `item_type='note'` row; defaults title to "Untitled note".
- `GET /knowledge-base/:itemId` (`getKnowledge`) — **no project-scoping at all**: looks up purely by `itemId` with no `projectId`/`is_deleted` check in the WHERE clause and no auth check — an item from Project A is fetchable via Project B's URL, or without matching project at all. Flag as a potential IDOR-style test case even though the feature is legacy/likely unused by the UI.
- `PATCH /knowledge-base/:itemId` (`updateKnowledge`) — same lack of scoping; updates title/content only.
- `DELETE /knowledge-base/:itemId` (`deleteKnowledge`) — hard delete (no soft-delete column on this table at all), same lack of scoping.
- `POST /knowledge-base/upload` — stubbed, always returns `{ error: "File uploads are not enabled in this endpoint yet" }` regardless of input.
- `GET /knowledge-base/:itemId/file` — stubbed, always returns `{}`.
- Route-ordering note (called out in the controller's own comment): the v2 literal routes (`folders`, `search`, `documents`, `files`) must be declared before these v1 `:itemId` catch-all routes, otherwise Express/Nest would match e.g. `GET /knowledge-base/search` against `GET /knowledge-base/:itemId` (with `itemId="search"`) instead of the intended search handler. Worth a regression test that hitting `/knowledge-base/search`, `/knowledge-base/folders`, `/knowledge-base/documents`, `/knowledge-base/files` never accidentally falls through to the v1 `:itemId` handlers.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 969–1002
- Backend service: `listKnowledge` (2793), `createKnowledge` (2808), `getKnowledge` (2817), `updateKnowledge` (2823), `deleteKnowledge` (2830)
- Schema: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V14_knowledge_base_items.sql`
- No frontend usage found (superseded by v2 pages/components documented above).

---

## Section H — Third-Party Integrations (Jira, Linear, OAuth, Personal Access Tokens)

Scope note on naming: the codebase has two unrelated features that both involve the phrase
"Personal Access Token." (1) `connectIntegrationWithToken` / `auth_method = 'personal_token'` on
`integration_connections` — this is what the frontend actually labels "Personal Access Token" and
is the PAT alternative to the Jira/Linear OAuth redirect flow; it is documented in its own section
below. (2) `src/auth/api-token.service.ts` — a same-week, differently-scoped feature ("Tesbo MCP
API tokens") that issues Tesbo's *own* bearer tokens so external/machine clients (e.g. an MCP
server) can call *Tesbo's* REST API without a browser session. It has no relationship to Jira or
Linear and does not back any of the `/connect-token` routes. Both are documented below so nothing
is missed, but they should not be conflated when writing test cases.

### Workspace Integration Connections (OAuth Framework)

**What it is:** A generic, provider-parameterized framework (`:provider` = `jira` or `linear`) for
connecting a third-party issue tracker to a Tesbo workspace via the standard OAuth 2.0
authorization-code flow. The connection is organization/workspace-scoped (one connection per
provider per workspace), not per-project — a workspace owner connects Jira/Linear once, and
individual projects later opt in by mapping to a remote project/team (see the Jira/Linear
Integration sections).

**Use cases:**
- A workspace owner sets up Jira or Linear once for the whole company/workspace instead of every
  project owner having to authenticate separately.
- An admin brings their own OAuth app (self-hosted Jira/Linear OAuth client) so the integration
  runs under their own Atlassian/Linear developer account rather than a shared Tesbo-wide app.
- A platform operator pre-configures default OAuth client credentials via environment variables so
  customers can connect without creating their own OAuth app first.

**Problem it solves:** Avoids re-authenticating per project and avoids storing raw OAuth
credentials in plaintext; centralizes "is this workspace connected to Jira/Linear, and which
projects use it" into one place.

**Features & actions:**
- **Configure OAuth client (workspace owner only)** — `PATCH /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/config`
  - Requires `clientId`, `redirectUri`, and (on first save) `clientSecret`; on later saves, submitting a
    blank `clientSecret` keeps the previously-saved encrypted secret rather than clearing it.
  - `redirectUri` must start with `http://` or `https://` (validated server-side) — anything else is
    rejected with a 400.
  - Blocked for non-owners (manager, qa_engineer, or any unrecognized role) with a 403
    "Only the workspace owner can manage integrations."
  - Client secret is encrypted at rest (AES-256-GCM, `src/common/crypto.util.ts`) before storage in
    `integration_oauth_configs`; only `hasClientSecret: true/false` is ever returned to the client,
    never the secret itself.
  - Falls back to environment variables (`JIRA_CLIENT_ID`/`JIRA_CLIENT_SECRET`/`JIRA_REDIRECT_URI`,
    and the `LINEAR_*` equivalents) when no workspace-level row is saved — this lets an operator
    ship a platform-default OAuth app. A workspace-saved config always takes precedence over env
    vars when both exist. A *partially*-saved workspace row (e.g. secret is null) is treated as
    "unconfigured" and env vars are used instead, rather than failing.
- **View config status** — `GET /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/config` — returns
  `configured`, `source` (`workspace` | `environment` | `none`), `clientId`, `redirectUri`,
  `hasClientSecret`, `updatedAt`. Not owner-gated — any workspace member can view it (masked).
- **Get the OAuth authorize URL** — `GET /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/auth-url` — builds
  the provider-specific authorization URL (Atlassian: `auth.atlassian.com/authorize` with
  `audience=api.atlassian.com` and scope `read:jira-work read:jira-user write:jira-work
  offline_access`; Linear: `linear.app/oauth/authorize` with scope `read,write,issues:create,comments:create`).
  Both set `state=<provider>` so the callback page knows which provider redirected back.
  - **Not owner-gated** in the backend (unlike config/callback/connect-token/disconnect) — any
    authenticated workspace member can request an auth URL even though the frontend only shows the
    "Connect" button to owners. A non-owner who reaches this endpoint directly and completes the
    provider's consent screen will still be rejected at the callback step (owner-only) — worth
    testing end-to-end as a privilege-boundary case.
  - Throws a 400 with an actionable message ("… OAuth is not configured. Add Client ID, Client
    Secret, and Redirect URI in Workspace Settings → Integrations.") when neither workspace config
    nor env vars are present.
  - Unsupported `:provider` values (anything other than `jira`/`linear`) are rejected with 400
    *before* any DB query.
- **OAuth callback / token exchange** — `POST /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/callback` —
  exchanges the `code` for tokens and upserts `integration_connections` (`ON CONFLICT
  (organization_id, provider) DO UPDATE`, so reconnecting the same provider updates the same row
  rather than creating a duplicate — existing project mappings/synced tickets tied to that
  connection id remain intact).
  - Owner-only (403 for any other role).
  - Requires `code` in the body (400 if missing).
  - Jira: posts to `auth.atlassian.com/oauth/token`; requires both `access_token` and
    `refresh_token` in the response (400 "Jira did not return OAuth tokens." if either is missing);
    then calls `accessible-resources` to discover the Jira Cloud site — 400 "No accessible Jira
    site was found." if the resource list is empty (e.g. user granted OAuth consent but the app
    isn't installed on any site).
  - Linear: posts to `api.linear.app/oauth/token` (form-encoded); requires `access_token` (400 if
    absent); then queries `organization { id urlKey }` over GraphQL — 400 "Could not read the
    connected Linear workspace." if `urlKey` is missing.
  - Access/refresh tokens are encrypted (AES-256-GCM) before insert; `token_expires_at` is computed
    from the provider's `expires_in` (default 3600s for Jira, ~10 years for Linear since Linear's
    OAuth tokens are treated as effectively non-expiring by this integration).
  - Any upstream non-2xx response from Jira/Linear surfaces as a 400 with the truncated response
    body as `detail`.
- **Disconnect** — `DELETE /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/disconnect` — owner-only; deletes
  the `integration_connections` row for that provider/workspace.
  - **Cascades**: `jira_project_mappings`/`linear_project_mappings` and `jira_tickets`/
    `linear_tickets` all have `ON DELETE CASCADE` FKs to `integration_connections.id`, so
    disconnecting silently deletes *every* project's mapping and *all* synced ticket cache rows for
    that provider workspace-wide, even if 10 different projects had it mapped.
  - Does **not** cascade to: test cases' `jira_issue_key`/`jira_url`/`linear_issue_key`/`linear_url`
    fields (plain text columns, no FK — they remain pointing at a key that may no longer resolve to
    a live synced ticket), bugs' `integration_provider`/`integration_issue_key` fields, or
    Knowledge Base documents previously mirrored from synced tickets (`knowledge_documents` with
    `source_provider = 'jira'/'linear'`, also no FK to the connection). Reconnecting starts sync
    from a clean slate and project-to-remote mappings must be re-selected from scratch.
- **Connection status** — `GET /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/status` — returns
  `connected`, connection `id`, `siteUrl`, `authMethod` (`oauth`|`personal_token`),
  `personalTokenIdentifier` (Jira PAT email, only when `authMethod === personal_token`),
  `tokenExpiresAt` (`null` for personal-token connections), `connectedBy`, `createdAt`, and
  `connectedProjects` (every Tesbo project currently mapped to this connection, with name/key).
  Not owner-gated.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` lines 1008–1041
  (`auth-url`, `config` GET/PATCH, `callback`, `disconnect`, `status`)
- Backend service: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `integrationConfigStatus`
  (~3994), `updateIntegrationConfig` (~4023), `integrationAuthUrl` (~4055), `integrationCallback`
  (~4082), `integrationDisconnect` (~4231), `integrationStatus` (~4239), private helpers
  `envIntegrationConfig` (~3955), `integrationOAuthConfig` (~3969), `getIntegrationConnection`
  (~4553), constants `JIRA_OAUTH_SCOPE`/`LINEAR_OAUTH_SCOPE` (~223), `assertIntegrationProvider` (~203)
- Crypto: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/common/crypto.util.ts` (AES-256-GCM `encryptSecret`/`decryptSecret`)
- Migrations: `V38_jira_oauth_config.sql`, `V47_integration_connections.sql` (workspace-scoped
  tables + migration of legacy per-project connections), `V68_integration_personal_access_tokens.sql`
- Tests: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/linear-integration.spec.ts` (auth-url/callback config
  precedence, owner gating, malformed-response handling)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/settings/IntegrationsTab.tsx` (workspace Integrations tab —
  connect/manage/disconnect cards, connected-project count), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/integrations/WorkspaceIntegrationConfig.tsx`
  (OAuth config form + Connect button + PAT tab), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/settings/integrations/{page,jira/page,linear/page}.tsx`,
  `Tesbo-Frontend/app/integrations/callback/page.tsx` (OAuth redirect landing page), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts`
  (`getIntegrationConfig`, `updateIntegrationConfig`, `getIntegrationAuthUrl`, `integrationCallback`,
  `getIntegrationStatus`, `disconnectIntegration`)

---

### Personal Access Token Authentication for Jira/Linear Connections

**What it is:** An alternative to the OAuth redirect flow for connecting Jira or Linear to a
workspace: instead of an OAuth app + browser consent screen, the workspace owner pastes a
provider-issued personal token directly (a Jira API token + Atlassian account email, or a Linear
personal API key) and Tesbo verifies it live against the provider before saving it. Implemented
entirely in `connectIntegrationWithToken` — it reuses the same `integration_connections` table as
OAuth, distinguished by `auth_method = 'personal_token'` (added in migration V68, originally
numbered V51).

**Use cases:**
- A workspace owner who doesn't want to (or isn't allowed to) register an OAuth application in
  their Atlassian/Linear admin console can still connect using a token they can generate themselves
  in under a minute.
- Faster setup for trials/demos/small teams — no OAuth app, client ID/secret, or redirect URI
  configuration required.
- Connecting a Jira Server/Data Center instance or any Jira site where the org hasn't approved a
  Marketplace/OAuth app yet, since PAT auth talks directly to the customer's own site URL rather
  than through Atlassian's `api.atlassian.com/ex/jira` OAuth gateway.

**Problem it solves:** Removes the OAuth app-registration step as a hard prerequisite for
connecting an issue tracker, at the cost of a credential that (by design) never expires and isn't
scoped as tightly as OAuth.

**Features & actions:**
- **Connect via token** — `POST /api/workspace/integrations/:provider/connect-token` (owner-only,
  403 otherwise).
  - `INTEGRATION_PAT_SUPPORTED` gates this per provider (`{ jira: true, linear: true }`) — a future
    provider that only supports OAuth would 400 with "`{provider}` does not support Personal Access
    Token authentication." The frontend's `PROVIDER_PAT_FIELDS` map mirrors this so the "Personal
    Access Token" tab simply doesn't render for such a provider.
  - **Jira**: requires `siteUrl`, `email`, `apiToken`.
    - `siteUrl` is normalized/validated by `normalizeJiraSiteUrl` — must match
      `https://<host>` exactly (no path, no query string); trailing slashes are stripped; anything
      not starting with `https://` (e.g. `http://`) or containing a path is rejected with 400
      "Jira site URL must look like https://yourcompany.atlassian.net".
    - `email` and `apiToken` are both required (400 "Email and API token are required." if either
      is blank).
    - Before saving, Tesbo calls `GET {siteUrl}/rest/api/3/myself` with HTTP Basic auth
      (`email:apiToken` base64-encoded) to confirm the credential actually authenticates — an
      invalid token, wrong email, or wrong site URL surfaces as a 400 from the upstream call
      (`Jira request failed (401).` etc.), and nothing is persisted.
    - On success, upserts `integration_connections` with `auth_method='personal_token'`,
      `personal_token_identifier = email`, `external_id = NULL` (no Jira Cloud ID for a
      directly-addressed site), `refresh_token = ''`, and `token_expires_at = now() + 100 years`
      (i.e., "never expires" is modeled as a far-future timestamp rather than nullable).
  - **Linear**: requires `apiKey` only (400 "API key is required." if blank).
    - Before saving, verifies the key by querying `viewer { id } organization { id urlKey }` over
      GraphQL; a 400 "Could not verify the Linear API key." is returned if `viewer.id` comes back
      empty (invalid/revoked key).
    - Upserts with `auth_method='personal_token'`, `personal_token_identifier = NULL` (Linear
      personal keys are a single opaque value, no paired identity field), `site_url` derived from
      the organization's `urlKey` if present.
  - **Upsert semantics / switching auth methods**: connecting via token when an OAuth connection
    already exists for that provider **overwrites the same row** (`ON CONFLICT (organization_id,
    provider) DO UPDATE`) — the connection `id` is preserved, so existing project mappings
    (`jira_project_mappings`/`linear_project_mappings`) and any already-synced tickets keep working
    without re-selecting them. The reverse (PAT → OAuth via `/callback`) behaves the same way. This
    is a good positive-path regression test: switch auth methods without disconnecting first and
    confirm project mappings survive.
- **Request auth differences from OAuth** (relevant to every Jira/Linear API call the backend
  makes, not just connect): `jiraBaseUrlAndAuth` routes personal-token Jira connections directly to
  the customer's own `site_url` with an HTTP Basic header, vs. OAuth connections which go through
  `https://api.atlassian.com/ex/jira/{cloudId}` with a Bearer token. `linearAuthHeader` sends the
  raw personal key as-is for PAT connections vs. a `Bearer `-prefixed token for OAuth. A bug in
  either branch would only surface for one auth method, so both need independent test coverage for
  every Jira/Linear action (status, projects/teams, sync, tickets, comment, search-issues).
- **No refresh cycle**: `getIntegrationConnection` short-circuits token refresh entirely for
  `auth_method === 'personal_token'` ("Personal tokens don't expire; nothing to refresh") — there is
  no revalidation of a personal token's continued validity until the next live API call fails.
- **Status reporting**: `GET .../status` surfaces `authMethod: "personal_token"` and
  `personalTokenIdentifier` (Jira email) so the UI can show "Connected via Personal Access Token
  (you@company.com)" instead of "Connected via OAuth."
- Edge cases worth testing: connecting with a syntactically valid but wrong/expired Jira API token
  or Linear key (should 400 with the upstream error, no partial write); connecting with a Jira site
  URL missing `https://` or with a trailing path; connecting with a Linear key that belongs to a
  different Linear organization than expected; revoking the token on the provider's side *after*
  connecting (no proactive detection — the failure only surfaces the next time a Jira/Linear API
  call is made, e.g. Sync or Search); a non-owner attempting `connect-token` directly.

**Note — a separate, unrelated "API token" feature exists:** `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/api-token.service.ts`
(+ `api-token.service.spec.ts`) implements project-scoped Tesbo API tokens (`tsbo_` prefix, SHA-256
hashed, stored in the `api_tokens` table) that let *external/machine clients* — e.g. the Tesbo MCP
server — authenticate *into Tesbo's own REST API* via `Authorization: Bearer tsbo_...`, as an
alternative to the browser session cookie. This is consumed by `AuthMiddleware`
(`Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts`): it first tries the session cookie, and only
falls back to `ApiTokenService.authenticate()` if there's no session, resolving to an
`ApiTokenPrincipal` (`tokenId`, `userId`, `projectId`, `scopes: ["read"|"write"]`). Key behaviors:
`hashToken`/`generateRawToken` (24 random bytes, hex-encoded, `tsbo_` prefix), `issueToken` (returns
the raw token exactly once — never recoverable afterward, only a `tokenPrefix` hint like
`tsbo_…a1b2c3` is shown thereafter), `revokeToken` (delete, scoped to `projectId` so one project
can't revoke another's token), `authenticate` (returns `null` for blank/unknown tokens without
querying the DB for blank input; best-effort `last_used_at` stamping that never blocks auth if it
fails), and scope normalization that silently discards invalid scope strings and **defaults to
`["read","write"]`** if nothing valid was supplied — worth testing that issuing a token with a
garbage scope string (e.g. `"delete"`) doesn't silently grant more than intended.
**This mechanism has no code path that touches Jira, Linear, or `integration_connections` at all** —
it is not what backs `/connect-token`, and should not be tested as part of the Jira/Linear
connection flow. It is documented here because it was explicitly in scope for this investigation,
not because it is part of the Jira/Linear PAT feature.

**Key files:**
- Backend (Jira/Linear PAT): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` line 1028 (`connect-token`
  route); `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `connectIntegrationWithToken` (~4169–4229),
  `INTEGRATION_PAT_SUPPORTED` (~213), `normalizeJiraSiteUrl` (~215), `jiraBaseUrlAndAuth` (~4588),
  `linearAuthHeader` (~4603)
- Migration: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/migrations/V68_integration_personal_access_tokens.sql` (adds
  `auth_method`, `personal_token_identifier`, check constraints)
- Backend (unrelated Tesbo API tokens): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/api-token.service.ts`,
  `api-token.service.spec.ts`, `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts`
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/integrations/WorkspaceIntegrationConfig.tsx`
  (`PROVIDER_PAT_FIELDS`, OAuth/"Personal Access Token" tab toggle, `handleConnectToken`), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts`
  (`connectIntegrationToken`)

---

### Jira Integration

**What it is:** Project-scoped mapping, ticket sync, ticket browsing, and commenting on top of a
workspace's shared Jira connection. Connecting Jira (above) is workspace-wide; each Tesbo project
separately picks which Jira project(s) feed it.

**Use cases:**
- A QA lead maps their Tesbo project to the matching Jira project(s) so tickets show up as
  Requirements/Knowledge Base context.
- Pulling the latest Jira tickets into Tesbo to see test coverage (which tickets have a linked test
  case, which don't) without leaving Tesbo.
- Posting a comment back to a Jira issue directly from Tesbo (e.g. noting which test cases cover
  it) without switching tools.
- Searching for a specific Jira issue live (not from the sync cache) when linking a bug or test
  case to a ticket that was just filed and hasn't synced yet.

**Problem it solves:** Gives testers/PMs a coverage view (Jira tickets vs. test cases) and a way to
close the loop (commenting) without needing a Jira license/tab open, while keeping ticket data fresh
via on-demand sync rather than continuous webhooks.

**Features & actions:**
- **Connection status** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/jira/status` — `connected`, connection
  `id`, `cloudId`, `siteUrl`, `tokenExpiresAt`, `connectedBy`, `createdAt`, and
  `connectedProjects` = the Jira project(s) currently mapped to *this* Tesbo project (from
  `jira_project_mappings`, `enabled = true`).
- **List remote Jira projects** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/jira/projects` — live call to
  `{baseUrl}/rest/api/3/project/search?maxResults=100`; 404 "Jira is not connected." if the
  workspace has no Jira connection; each item flagged `connected: true/false` based on whether it's
  already mapped to this Tesbo project. Filters out any Jira project missing an `id` or `key`.
  - Capped at 100 results — a Jira instance with >100 projects will have some projects unreachable
    from this picker (no pagination implemented); worth testing against a large Jira site.
- **Save Jira project mapping** — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/jira/projects` with
  `{ projects: [{id,key,name}, ...] }`.
  - **Full replace, not merge**: deletes all existing mappings for
    `(projectId, connectionId)` then re-inserts the submitted set — unchecking a previously-mapped
    project and saving unlinks it.
  - Entries missing `id` or `key` are silently dropped (not an error).
  - Submitting an empty `projects` array clears all mappings for the project (unlinks everything) —
    the *backend* allows this, but the *frontend* Save button is disabled when zero items are
    selected (`selected.size === 0`), so unlinking every Jira project can only be done today by
    checking a different item then unchecking it, or by calling the API directly. Worth testing
    both the UI restriction and the raw API behavior.
  - 404 "Jira is not connected." if there's no workspace Jira connection yet.
- **Sync tickets** — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/jira/sync` (`{ synced: <count> }`).
  - No-op (`{ synced: 0 }`, no error) if no Jira project is mapped to this Tesbo project yet.
  - For every mapped Jira project key, runs `project = "KEY" ORDER BY updated DESC` (JQL) with
    `maxResults: 100` per project and **no pagination beyond the first 100 issues per project** —
    a mapped Jira project with >100 issues will not have all of them synced in one call; there's no
    incremental/paged sync today. Good boundary test: map a project with >100 issues and confirm
    only the newest 100 (by `updated`) land.
  - Upserts each issue into `jira_tickets` keyed on `(jira_connection_id, jira_issue_id, project_id)`
    — re-running sync updates existing rows in place (status/summary/etc. refresh) rather than
    duplicating.
  - **Also mirrors every synced ticket into the Knowledge Base's "Requirements" folder** as a
    `knowledge_documents` row (`document_type='requirement_note'`, `source_provider='jira'`,
    `source_external_id=<jira issue id>`) and enqueues it for embedding/RAG — so Jira tickets become
    searchable Zyra context, not just a coverage list. If the project's Requirements folder was
    deleted/renamed, sync falls back to the project's root Knowledge Base folder; if there's no root
    folder at all, the mirror step is silently skipped for that sync run (tickets still land in
    `jira_tickets`, just not mirrored to Knowledge Base) — worth testing a project with a
    missing/renamed Requirements folder.
  - Jira's rich-text (Atlassian Document Format) `description` field is flattened to plain text via
    `jiraDescriptionToText` — nested formatting/tables/media are lost in the mirrored copy; a ticket
    with complex ADF content (tables, embedded images, mentions) is a good edge case to visually
    diff against the original Jira ticket.
  - Any single malformed/unreachable Jira API response aborts the whole sync (no partial-success
    reporting beyond "synced so far" — since it's a straight `await` loop, an error on project 2 of
    3 leaves project 1's tickets synced but throws before project 3 runs).
- **Browse synced tickets** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/jira/tickets` — paginated (`limit`
  capped at 100, default 25; `offset`), filterable by free-text `search` (matches issue key or
  summary, case-insensitive), `issueType`, `status`, and `coverage` (`covered`/`uncovered`, based on
  whether any non-deleted test case in the project has a matching `jira_issue_key`). This reads the
  local sync cache (`jira_tickets`), not live Jira — data can be stale until the next Sync.
- **Add a comment to a Jira issue** — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/jira/comment` with
  `{ issueKey, comment }` (aliases `jiraIssueKey`/`body` also accepted). Both required (400
  otherwise). Posted as a single-paragraph Atlassian Document Format comment via
  `POST {baseUrl}/rest/api/3/issue/{issueKey}/comment`. 404 if Jira isn't connected for the project's
  workspace. Edge cases: commenting on an issue key that doesn't exist / was deleted upstream
  (upstream 404 surfaces as a Tesbo 400), commenting with a token/user that lacks comment
  permission on that specific issue (permission scheme edge case even though the workspace-level
  connection is valid).
- **Live issue search** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/jira/search-issues?search=...` —
  deliberately bypasses the `jira_tickets` sync cache (comment in code: "used by the bug-linking
  picker, where a ticket filed moments ago may not have synced yet"); builds a JQL restricted to the
  project's mapped Jira project keys, matching `summary ~ "term*"` or an exact `key = "TERM"` (case
  is upper-cased for the key match); returns up to 20 results with `{provider, key, summary, status,
  url}`. `{ list: [] }` (not an error) if no Jira project is mapped yet.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 1045–1078
- Backend service: `legacy.service.ts` — `jiraStatus` (~4268), `jiraProjects` (~4290),
  `connectJiraProjects` (~4309), `syncJira` (~4334), `jiraTickets` (~4451), `jiraComment` (~4485),
  `jiraSearchIssues` (~4511), `getJiraConnection` (~4546), `jiraBaseUrlAndAuth` (~4588), `jiraFetch`
  (~4608), `jiraDescriptionToText` (~190s)
- Migrations: `V12_jira_integration.sql`, `V47_integration_connections.sql` (mapping/ticket tables
  now FK to the shared connection)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/integrations/jira/page.tsx`,
  `Tesbo-Frontend/components/integrations/ProjectIntegrationMapping.tsx` (shared mapping/sync UI for
  both providers), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/IssuePickerModal.tsx` (search-issues consumer),
  `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` (`getJiraStatus`, `listJiraProjects`, `connectJiraProjects`,
  `syncJiraTickets`, `listJiraTickets`, `addJiraComment`, `searchJiraIssuesLive`),
  `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/requirements/page.tsx` (ticket list + coverage stat strip
  consumer, cross-source with Linear)

---

### Linear Integration

**What it is:** The Linear mirror of the Jira integration above — project-scoped mapping, sync,
ticket browsing, and commenting — structurally identical but built on Linear's GraphQL API and
"team" (not "project") as the unit of work.

**Use cases:** Same as Jira — mapping a Tesbo project to Linear team(s), pulling issues in for
coverage tracking, commenting back to Linear from Tesbo, live-searching Linear issues when linking
a bug/test case.

**Problem it solves:** Same as Jira, for teams whose issue tracker is Linear instead of/alongside Jira.

**Features & actions:**
- **Connection status** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/linear/status` — `connected`, `id`,
  `siteUrl`, `tokenExpiresAt`, `connectedBy`, `createdAt`, `connectedProjects` = mapped Linear teams
  for this Tesbo project (from `linear_project_mappings`).
- **List remote Linear teams** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/linear/teams` — GraphQL
  `query { teams { nodes { id key name } } }` (no pagination arguments passed — relies on Linear's
  default page size, so a Linear workspace with a very large number of teams may not return all of
  them; worth a boundary test). 404 "Linear is not connected." if not connected. Each team flagged
  `connected: true/false`.
- **Save Linear team mapping** — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/linear/teams` with
  `{ projects: [{id,key,name}, ...] }` (same field name `projects` reused for teams, mirroring the
  Jira endpoint's shape). Same **full-replace** semantics as Jira (delete-then-insert), same
  silent-drop of entries missing `id`/`key`, same "empty array clears mapping" backend behavior with
  the same frontend Save-button restriction (disabled at 0 selected). Verified by
  `linear-integration.spec.ts`: malformed entries (empty id, empty key) are dropped and only
  well-formed teams are linked; submitting zero valid teams still clears old mappings via the
  DELETE but issues no INSERT.
- **Sync tickets** — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/linear/sync` (`{ synced: <count> }`).
  - No-op if no team is mapped.
  - Per mapped team, fetches up to 100 issues (`first: 100, orderBy: updatedAt`) — same "no
    pagination past the first 100" caveat as Jira; a team with >100 issues won't fully sync in one
    call.
  - Upserts into `linear_tickets` keyed on `(integration_connection_id, linear_issue_id)`; sets a
    fixed `issue_type = "Issue"` for every row (Linear has no separate "issue type" taxonomy the way
    Jira does — every synced item is typed "Issue"), pulls `state.name` as `status`,
    `priorityLabel` as `priority`.
  - Also mirrors each synced issue into the Knowledge Base's "Requirements" folder
    (`source_provider='linear'`) and enqueues embedding, with the same Requirements-folder-missing
    fallback-to-root behavior as Jira.
- **Browse synced tickets** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/linear/tickets` — same
  pagination/search/filter shape as Jira's tickets endpoint (`limit`/`offset`/`search`/`issueType`/
  `status`/`coverage`), reading the `linear_tickets` cache.
- **Add a comment to a Linear issue** — `POST /api/projects/:projectId/linear/comment` with
  `{ issueKey, comment }` (alias `linearIssueKey`). Both required. First resolves the issue by
  `issueKey` via `query Issue($id: String!) { issue(id: $id) { id } }` (falls back to using the raw
  `issueKey` as the id if the lookup returns nothing) then runs `commentCreate` mutation. 404 if
  Linear isn't connected. Edge case: commenting with an issue identifier Linear can't resolve (e.g.
  a stale/typo'd key) — the fallback silently tries to comment using that string as an ID, which
  will likely fail upstream with a GraphQL error surfaced as a 400.
- **Live issue search** — `GET /api/projects/:projectId/linear/search-issues?search=...` — for each
  mapped team, runs a GraphQL query with `filter: { title: { containsIgnoreCase: search } }` (or no
  filter if search is blank), first 20 per team, returns `{provider: "LINEAR", key, summary,
  status, url}`. `{ list: [] }` if no team mapped.

**Key files:**
- Backend controller: `legacy.controller.ts` lines 1082–1115
- Backend service: `legacy.service.ts` — `linearStatus` (~4636), `linearTeams` (~4658),
  `connectLinearTeams` (~4677), `syncLinear` (~4703), `linearTickets` (~4823), `linearComment`
  (~4946), `linearSearchIssues` (~4965), `linearGraphQL` (~4617), `linearAuthHeader` (~4603)
- Migration: `V47_integration_connections.sql` (defines `linear_project_mappings`, `linear_tickets`)
- Tests: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/linear-integration.spec.ts` (`connectLinearTeams`
  malformed-entry and empty-selection behavior; `linkedLinearKeys` aggregate)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/settings/integrations/linear/page.tsx`,
  `Tesbo-Frontend/components/integrations/ProjectIntegrationMapping.tsx` (shared with Jira),
  `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` (`getLinearStatus`, `listLinearTeams`, `connectLinearTeams`,
  `syncLinearTickets`, `listLinearTickets`, `addLinearComment`, `searchLinearIssuesLive`)

---

### Ticket Linking (Test Cases & Bugs)

**What it is:** The mechanisms by which a Tesbo test case or bug record points at a specific Jira or
Linear ticket. There is no dedicated "ticket link" table for test cases — a test case simply carries
plain `jira_issue_key`/`jira_url`/`linear_issue_key`/`linear_url` columns (one Jira key + one Linear
key max per test case). Bugs similarly carry `integration_provider`/`integration_issue_key`
columns, plus a separate `bug_links` table that links a bug to a Tesbo *test case/cycle/execution*
(not to an external ticket) — the two link concepts are easy to confuse and worth testing
independently.

**Use cases:**
- Tagging a test case with the Jira/Linear requirement it was written to cover, so Requirements-page
  coverage stats and the "linked-jira-keys"/"linked-linear-keys" aggregates work.
- When a scripted test execution fails, filing a bug and recording where that defect is *actually*
  tracked — either by picking an already-filed Jira/Linear ticket via live search, or by pasting a
  URL to wherever the tester will log it themselves.
- Linking a failed execution to a Tesbo bug that already exists (not a new bug), to avoid duplicate
  bug reports for the same underlying defect across multiple runs.

**Problem it solves:** Connects the "what was tested" (test case/execution) side of Tesbo to the
"what's the actual requirement/defect" side (Jira/Linear), enabling coverage reporting and reducing
duplicate bug filing.

**Features & actions:**
- **Test case ↔ ticket link** — set directly on `POST /api/projects/:projectId/testcases` and
  `PATCH /api/testcases/:id` via `jiraIssueKey`/`jiraUrl`/`linearIssueKey`/`linearUrl` body fields
  (no dedicated endpoint or validation that the key actually exists in `jira_tickets`/
  `linear_tickets`, or that the URL matches the key — these are free-text fields set by whatever UI
  calls update, so a test case can reference a ticket key that was mistyped, belongs to an
  unmapped/different Jira project, or no longer exists upstream, without any error).
  - `GET /api/projects/:projectId/testcases` supports filtering by `jiraIssueKey`/`linearIssueKey`
    query params (exact match).
  - `GET /api/projects/:projectId/testcases/linked-jira-keys` and `.../linked-linear-keys` —
    aggregate every distinct linked key across a project's non-deleted test cases with a per-key
    count (`{ keys: [...], counts: { KEY: n } }}`) — used to show "this ticket already has N test
    cases" in ticket-linking UIs. A deleted test case (`deleted_at` set) is excluded, so
    soft-deleting the last test case linked to a key drops that key out of the aggregate.
  - Test case table UI shows the linked Jira key as a clickable link (icon + key, opens `jiraUrl` in
    a new tab) when both key and URL are present, or as plain unlinked text if only the key is set
    (no URL) — worth testing a test case with a key but no URL, and vice versa (URL but no key,
    which the UI doesn't render at all since it branches on `jiraIssueKey` first).
- **"Link a ticket" search picker** (`IssuePickerModal`) — used when filing a bug from a failed test
  execution. Defaults to whichever provider (Jira or Linear) is connected for the project;
  if both are connected, the user can flip between "Jira"/"Linear" tabs. Debounced (300ms) live
  search via `jiraSearchIssuesLive`/`searchLinearIssuesLive`. Shows "No issue tracker is connected
  for this project" if neither is connected. Selecting a result shows `{key} — {summary}` with an
  ✕ to clear and re-search.
- **File a bug from a failed execution, linking to an existing external ticket** (cycle/run detail
  page): "Is this defect already logged?" → "Yes, link existing" → choose Jira ticket / Linear
  ticket / an existing Tesbo bug.
  - Choosing "Existing Tesbo bug" opens a different picker (`ExistingBugPickerModal`) and calls
    `POST /api/bugs/:bugId/links` (`addBugLink`) with `{testcaseId, cycleId, executionId}` — this
    attaches the *current failing execution* to an already-existing bug record (`bug_links` table,
    `ON CONFLICT (bug_id, testcase_id, cycle_id) DO NOTHING`) rather than creating a new bug. This is
    the correct path for "same defect, another failed run."
  - Choosing "Jira ticket"/"Linear ticket" opens `IssuePickerModal` scoped to that provider; picking
    a result stores it in local component state (`bugIssue`) and displays `{key} — {summary}` in the
    dialog. **However, as currently written, the "File Bug" submit handler
    (`handleBugSubmit` in `app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx`) hard-codes
    `integrationIssueKey: null` in the `createBug` payload regardless of what was picked** — the
    same is true of the create/edit bug forms on the standalone Bugs page
    (`app/(app)/projects/[id]/bugs/page.tsx`, both `integrationIssueKey: null`). The picked ticket
    key is shown on screen but does not appear to be persisted to the bug record in either flow.
    **This is a high-value, concrete thing to verify end-to-end**: file a bug, mark it "already
    logged" in Jira/Linear, pick a specific ticket via search, save, then re-open the bug and
    confirm whether the Jira/Linear ticket key is actually stored and displayed (`viewBug.integrationIssueKey`
    on the bug detail view falls back to `viewBug.externalUrl` when the key is empty, which would
    mask the gap unless specifically checked).
- **File a bug, self-logging it in an external tracker (no ticket search)** — "Where should this be
  tracked?" → "I'll log it in my task management system myself" → pick Jira/Linear/Other +
  paste a URL (`SelfLoggedTrackerField` — deliberately has no search, per an explicit code comment:
  "the ticket already lives in the user's own tracker, we're just recording where to find it").
  Sets `externalUrl` + `integrationProvider` (`JIRA`/`LINEAR`/`OTHER`) on the bug; `integrationIssueKey`
