  stays null by design here (only a URL is captured, not a parsed key) — do not conflate this
  intentional gap with the search-picker gap above; they are two different code paths with
  different (and differently justified) behavior.
  - No URL format validation observed beyond the `type="url"` HTML input — pasting a non-URL string
    is a plausible edge case (stored as-is in `external_url`).
  - Bug detail view labels the external link "{Provider} Ticket" when `integrationProvider` is set,
    or generic "Bug Link" otherwise, and displays `integrationIssueKey || externalUrl` as the link
    text — since `integrationIssueKey` is always null from every current UI path, this always
    falls through to showing the raw URL.
- **Requirements page coverage view** (cross-source): `GET /api/projects/:projectId/tickets/summary`
  and `GET /api/projects/:projectId/tickets` aggregate Jira + Linear synced tickets into one
  paginated, filterable (search/issueType/status/coverage) list with total/covered/uncovered counts
  and a coverage percentage bar, per source and combined. "Covered" is computed live via an `EXISTS`
  check against `testcases.jira_issue_key`/`linear_issue_key` — so linking/unlinking a test case's
  ticket key immediately moves it between covered/uncovered on next load, with no caching lag. (The
  "Generate testcase coverage" AI action available from this page belongs to the AI test-generation
  feature, out of scope here — only the ticket list/coverage/filtering itself is part of this
  integrations surface.)

**Key files:**
- Backend: `legacy.controller.ts` — `linkedJiraKeys`/`linkedLinearKeys` routes (lines 263–270),
  bug links routes (`POST /api/bugs/:bugId/links`, `DELETE /api/bugs/:bugId/links/:linkId`, lines
  481–488); `legacy.service.ts` — `createTestCase` (~1348), `updateTestCase` (~1394),
  `listTestCases` filter columns (~1262), `linkedJiraKeys` (~1487), `linkedLinearKeys` (~1496),
  `createBug` (~1903), `getBug` (~1936), `updateBug` (~1943), `addBugLink` (~1966), `removeBugLink`
  (~1976), `requirementsSummary` (~4910), `allTickets` (~4860)
- Migrations: `V13_testcase_jira_link.sql`, `V66_testcase_linear_link.sql` (adds the plain
  `jira_issue_key`/`linear_issue_key`/`*_url` columns to `testcases`, with a partial index on
  non-null keys)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/components/IssuePickerModal.tsx` (Jira/Linear live search picker),
  `Tesbo-Frontend/components/SelfLoggedTrackerField.tsx` (manual URL/system entry, no search),
  `Tesbo-Frontend/components/TrackingDestinationField.tsx` ("Log into Tesbo" vs "I'll log it myself"
  toggle), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/cycles/[cycleId]/page.tsx` (file-bug-from-execution
  dialog — contains the `integrationIssueKey: null` gap noted above), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/bugs/page.tsx`
  (standalone Bugs list/create/edit — same gap), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/testcases/RepositoryTestCaseTable.tsx`
  (Jira-key column rendering), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/(app)/projects/[id]/requirements/page.tsx`
  (cross-source coverage view), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` (`linkedJiraKeys`/`linkedLinearKeys`,
  `addBugLink`, `createBug`, `updateBug`)

---

## Section I — Platform Admin, Branding, Tesbo Reports, MCP Server, RAG Pipeline

### Super Admin Console

**What it is:** A platform-wide admin console, separate from any single customer's workspace, restricted to users listed in the `platform_admins` table. It gives Tesbo's own operators (not customers) visibility into system health and control over who else holds this cross-tenant privilege.

**Use cases:**
- Tesbo's ops/founder team checking that the API, database, and email provider are healthy right after a deploy.
- Onboarding a new internal teammate as a platform admin so they can access `/admin`.
- Auditing who currently holds platform-admin rights and who granted it to them.
- (Latent) Pulling a cross-tenant view of every customer organization's size/activity for account management — endpoint exists but has no UI yet (see gap below).

**Problem it solves:** Tesbo is multi-tenant (organizations/workspaces are customers). Regular workspace owners can only manage their own organization; the Super Admin console is the only place with visibility/control that spans every organization in the database, and it needs to be locked down independently of any one workspace's role model.

**Features & actions:**
- **Access gating**
  - Entire `/admin` area is client-gated: `AdminLayout` calls `authMe()` and redirects to `/projects` unless `isPlatformAdmin` is true on the session (`GET /api/auth/me`).
  - Every backend admin route independently re-checks membership in `platform_admins` (`requirePlatformAdmin` in `legacy.service.ts`, and `SuperAdminService.isPlatformAdmin` for the health controller) — the frontend gate is not the only line of defense.
  - Two internal roles exist on `platform_admins.role`: `owner` and `admin`. Only `owner` can add/remove other admins; a plain `admin` can view but not manage (`AdminsTab.tsx` gates the add-form and remove-button on `role === "owner"`, but this is a UI-only check — worth testing that the backend also rejects a non-owner `admin` calling POST/DELETE `/api/admin/admins`, since `addAdmin`/`deleteAdmin` in `legacy.service.ts` only call `requirePlatformAdmin`, not an owner-specific check).
  - `deleteAdmin` guards `role <> 'owner'` in its SQL `WHERE` clause, so an owner row can never be deleted through this endpoint (test: attempt to delete the seed owner and confirm no-op / still present).
- **System Health page** (`/admin`, default landing page)
  - Fetches `GET /api/admin/system/health`: reports database status + latency + latest applied migration filename, and email provider (Postmark) "configured" vs "not_configured" state. Overall `status` is `"degraded"` if any service reports an error.
  - Manual "Refresh" button and an "Auto-refresh (30s)" checkbox that polls on an interval.
  - Renders one status card per service with a colored status dot (green pulsing = up, amber = misconfigured/warning, red = down/error), latency, provider, migration id, and any error text.
  - Edge cases to test: DB unreachable (should surface `services.database.status = "error"` with the caught error message, overall `status: "degraded"`, not a 500); Postmark token unset (should read "not_configured" rather than erroring).
- **Deployment branding editor** (embedded in the same System Health page — see Platform Branding section below for the underlying feature; the admin page is one of its two write surfaces along with... actually its only write surface).
- **Manage Admins page** (`/admin/admins` in the sidebar, but that route itself immediately client-redirects to `/settings?tab=admins` — the actual UI lives in the workspace Settings modal/tab, rendered by `AdminsTab.tsx`)
  - List all platform admins: name/avatar initials, email, role badge (`owner` vs `admin`), who granted them access and when (`GET /api/admin/admins`).
  - Add a platform admin by email (owner-only in the UI): the target user must already have a Tesbo account — `addAdmin` calls `upsertUser(email)` and then inserts/upgrades a `platform_admins` row (`ON CONFLICT (user_id) DO UPDATE SET role = 'admin'`), so re-adding an existing admin is idempotent and does not create a duplicate row. Test: adding an email with no existing user account — does `upsertUser` create a stub user, and can that user actually authenticate afterward?
  - Remove a platform admin (owner-only in the UI, and owner rows are protected server-side as noted above).
  - Empty state ("No platform admins configured") when the list is empty.
- **Customers overview (backend-only, currently unreachable from the UI)**
  - `GET /api/admin/customers` returns, per organization across the whole platform: id, name, slug, created_at, member count, project count, test case count, automated-test count and coverage %, and last-activity timestamp — plus a `summary` block (totals). This is a genuine cross-tenant query (`FROM organizations o LEFT JOIN organization_members ... LEFT JOIN projects ... LEFT JOIN testcases`).
  - **Gap worth flagging to QA:** there is no `/admin/customers` (or similarly named) page in the frontend, no nav item in `AdminSidebar.tsx`, and no `lib/api.ts` client function calling this route at all. The endpoint is fully implemented and platform-admin-gated but currently dead from a user-journey standpoint — it can only be exercised via a direct authenticated HTTP call. Also note the `summary` block in the service code looks partially unfinished: `totalMembers` and `totalAutomated` are hardcoded to `0` and `overallAutomationCoverage` to `0` regardless of actual data, which would fail any assertion expecting real aggregate numbers there.
- **Sidebar/session**
  - `AdminSidebar.tsx` shows a "Platform Admin" badge, links to System Health and Manage Admins, a collapse/expand toggle, "Back to Workspace" (→ `/projects`), and Log out.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/admin/admin-health.controller.ts` (`GET /api/admin/system/health`), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/admin/super-admin.service.ts` (`isPlatformAdmin`), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/admin/admin.module.ts`
- Backend (legacy): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` lines 1147–1180 (`/api/admin/customers`, `/api/admin/admins` GET/POST, `/api/admin/admins/:adminId` DELETE); `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `adminCustomers()` (~line 3836), `adminList()` (~line 3870), `addAdmin()` (~line 3928), `deleteAdmin()` (~line 3940), `requirePlatformAdmin()` (~line 363)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/admin/layout.tsx`, `Tesbo-Frontend/app/admin/page.tsx` (System Health + branding editor), `Tesbo-Frontend/app/admin/admins/page.tsx` (redirect shim), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/AdminSidebar.tsx`, `Tesbo-Frontend/components/settings/AdminsTab.tsx`
- Frontend API client: `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` — `getSystemHealth`, `getAdminList`, `addPlatformAdmin`, `removePlatformAdmin` (no client function exists for `/api/admin/customers`)

---

### Platform Branding

**What it is:** A single, platform-wide (not per-customer) product name + logo override, stored in a `platform_settings` key/value row, shown across every unauthenticated and authenticated surface of the app (login/signup, invite pages, shared-report pages, the main app sidebar).

**Use cases:**
- Tesbo (as the platform operator) white-labels the product name/logo for a self-hosted or reseller deployment without a code change or redeploy.
- Reverting a mis-applied logo back to the shipped Tesbo default in one click.

**Problem it solves:** Lets deployment-level branding (product name + logo) be changed at runtime by a platform admin, without needing engineering involvement, and centralizes it so every page that shows a logo/name stays in sync.

**Features & actions:**
- **Public branding read** — `GET /api/branding` (no auth required): returns `{ productName, logoUrl }`, falling back to `"Tesbo Test Manager"` / `/tesbo-test-manager-logo.png` if no `platform_settings` row exists yet or the query itself fails (query wrapped in `.catch()`), so branding never blocks page render.
  - Consumed by the `BrandLogo` component used on: login/auth split-screen (`AuthSplitShell.tsx`), workspace setup page, invite + invite-register pages, public shared test-run page (`/share/[token]`), and the main app `Sidebar.tsx`.
- **Admin branding read** — `GET /api/admin/branding`: platform-admin-gated version of the same payload (functionally identical to the public one today; exists as a separate authenticated surface for the admin editor).
- **Update branding** — `PATCH /api/admin/branding` (platform-admin only):
  - `productName`: trimmed; empty string silently falls back to `"Tesbo Test Manager"` rather than erroring.
  - `logoUrl`: must be either a same-origin public asset path (starts with `/`) or a base64 data URL with an allowed image mime type (`png`, `jpe?g`, `webp`, `svg+xml`) — anything else (e.g. an external `https://` image URL) is rejected with `400 Logo must be an uploaded image data URL or a public app asset path.` Test: pasting a remote image URL should fail, not silently pass through.
  - Size guard: rejects any logo payload over 2,500,000 characters (~2 MB) with `400 Logo is too large. Upload an image below 2 MB.` — note the UI's own client-side file-size check (`file.size > 2MB`) is on the *raw file*, while the backend check is on the *base64-encoded string length*, which is ~33% larger than the raw bytes; a file just under 2 MB raw could still be rejected server-side after base64 encoding — worth testing at the boundary.
  - Persisted via `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT (key) DO UPDATE` on `platform_settings`, recording `updated_by`.
- **Admin UI** (embedded at the top of the System Health page, `/admin`):
  - Live logo preview, product-name text field, "Upload logo" file picker (accepts png/jpeg/svg/webp; client-side rejects non-image files and files >2MB before even reading them), a rendered preview once a file is chosen, "Save branding" and "Reset default" buttons, and inline success/error messaging.
  - "Reset default" restores the shipped name + logo path and immediately persists it (not just a local UI reset).

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` lines 1157–1170 (`GET /api/branding`, `GET /api/admin/branding`, `PATCH /api/admin/branding`); `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `publicBranding()` (~3891), `adminBranding()` (~3900), `updateAdminBranding()` (~3905)
- Frontend: `Tesbo-Frontend/app/admin/page.tsx` (branding section of System Health page), `Tesbo-Frontend/components/BrandLogo.tsx` (consumer used across auth/invite/share/sidebar), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` (`getBranding`, `getAdminBranding`, `updateAdminBranding`, `BrandingSettings` type)

---

### Tesbo Reports (Automated Test Run Ingestion)

**What it is:** A designed-but-not-yet-implemented module intended to let external CI pipelines (Playwright first, per the client code) push automated test-run results into a project for reporting/analytics/alerting, kept separate from Tesbo's manual test-case/cycle-execution workflow. **As it exists in this codebase today, this is a stub**: the backend only implements six read-only GET endpoints that return hardcoded empty/placeholder data with no database backing, and the corresponding frontend has a fully-typed API client for a much larger surface (ingestion, alert CRUD, run sharing, settings, key rotation) but **no page or component anywhere calls any of it** — it is unreachable from the actual app UI.

**Use cases (intended, per the frontend contract — not currently functional):**
- A CI pipeline runs Playwright and uploads the JSON results (or raw result file) to Tesbo after each build, so a QA/dev lead can see pass/fail trends without leaving Tesbo.
- Comparing automated run history per spec file and per individual test to spot flaky tests.
- Getting alerted (immediate or daily digest) when a failure ratio crosses a threshold, or when a new build's status changes.
- Sharing a single automated run externally via a public, time-limited link (e.g. to a stakeholder without a Tesbo login).

**Problem it solves (intended):** Gives CI-driven automated test output a home in Tesbo distinct from manually-tracked test cases/cycles/executions, so "was last night's Playwright run green" is answerable without a separate CI dashboard.

**Features & actions:**
- **Implemented today (backend stubs, all under `/api/projects/:projectId/tesbo-reports/...`, no auth/param validation, no DB queries):**
  - `GET /runs` → always returns `[]`
  - `GET /specs` → always returns `[]`
  - `GET /tests` → always returns `[]`
  - `GET /analytics` → always returns `{ totalRuns: 0, totalTests: 0, passRate: 0, byStatus: {}, runsByDay: [] }`
  - `GET /alerts` → always returns `[]`
  - `GET /settings` → always returns `{ keepTrace: true, traceRetentionDays: 14, ingestionApiKey: "", alertsEnabled: false, shareByDefault: false }`
  - None of these six take `projectId` into account in the handler at all (the route param is declared but unused) — every project sees the identical empty payload.
- **Designed but NOT implemented anywhere in the backend (the frontend `lib/api.ts` calls these; they will 404 or fail if invoked):**
  - `GET /runs/:runId` — single run detail (spec count + per-case results with duration, trace/screenshot/video URLs, browser/OS metadata, step-level detail)
  - `GET /specs/:specName` — per-spec breakdown of its tests with pass/fail/skip counts
  - `GET /specs/:specName/tests/:testName` — history of one test across runs
  - `POST /alerts`, `PUT /alerts/:alertId`, `DELETE /alerts/:alertId`, `POST /alerts/:alertId/toggle`, `POST /alerts/:alertId/send-test` — full alert-rule CRUD; a rule has `conditionType` (`FAILURE_RATIO` | `PASS_RATIO` | `BUILD_UPDATE`), `comparator` (`GREATER_THAN` | `GREATER_OR_EQUAL`), numeric `threshold`, `recipients` (emails), `frequency` (`IMMEDIATE` | `DAILY`), `enabled`
  - `GET/POST/DELETE /runs/:runId/share` — enable/disable a public share token for one run, with an expiry (`expiresInHours`, default 168h/7 days)
  - `GET /public/tesbo-reports/:token` — the actual public (unauthenticated) view of a shared run
  - `PUT /settings` and `POST /settings/rotate-key` — update retention/alerting/sharing defaults and rotate the project's ingestion API key
  - `POST /ingest/playwright` — JSON-body ingestion of a Playwright result payload, returns `{ runId }`
  - `POST /ingest/playwright/upload` — multipart file upload variant of the same, bearer-token authenticated via `localStorage` token
  - `POST /runs/:runId/cases/:caseId/artifacts/:kind/upload` — attach a trace/screenshot/video artifact file to a specific case result
- **Nothing in `Tesbo-Frontend/app` or `Tesbo-Frontend/components` references any `tesbo-reports` path or type** (`TesboRunSummary`, `listTesboRuns`, etc.) — confirmed via full-tree search. There is no visible nav entry, project page, or route for this feature today.

**What QA should actually test/track here:** Given the above, the realistic test plan for this "feature" right now is a **negative/regression check** — confirm the six stub GET endpoints keep returning their fixed empty payloads (as a contract other future work might rely on) and confirm none of the unimplemented write/ingest/share endpoints have silently appeared as functional without corresponding release notes. This should be flagged to the product owner as an incomplete/parked feature rather than something to write full functional test cases against yet — since there is no ingestion mechanism, "runs" can never exist, so downstream analytics/alerts/sharing cannot be exercised end-to-end regardless of what the client code implies.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` lines 1182–1210 (the six stub routes; handlers return literals directly in the controller, not via `LegacyService`)
- Backend: no `legacy.service.ts` methods exist for this feature at all (grep for `tesbo-reports`/`TesboReport` in the service file returns nothing)
- Frontend client (fully speculative surface, ~lines 2666–2965 of `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts`): types `TesboRunSummary`, `TesboRunCase`, `TesboRunDetail`, `TesboPublicRunDetail`, `TesboSpecSummary`, `TesboSpecDetail`, `TesboProjectTest`, `TesboAnalytics`, `TesboAlertRule`, `TesboShareState`, `TesboSettings`; functions `listTesboRuns`, `getTesboRun`, `listTesboSpecs`, `getTesboSpec`, `getTesboTestHistory`, `listTesboTests`, `getTesboAnalytics`, `listTesboAlertRules`, `createTesboAlertRule`, `updateTesboAlertRule`, `deleteTesboAlertRule`, `toggleTesboAlertRule`, `sendTesboAlertTest`, `getTesboRunShare`, `createTesboRunShare`, `disableTesboRunShare`, `getPublicTesboRun`, `getTesboSettings`, `updateTesboSettings`, `rotateTesboIngestionKey`, `ingestTesboPlaywright`, `ingestTesboPlaywrightUpload`, `uploadTesboCaseArtifact`
- No frontend page/component consumes any of the above (verified: no matches for `tesbo-reports`, `TesboRun*`, etc. anywhere under `Tesbo-Frontend/app` or `Tesbo-Frontend/components`)

---

### MCP Server Integration

**What it is:** An in-process, dependency-free MCP (Model Context Protocol) server exposed over a single JSON-RPC 2.0 HTTP endpoint per project, letting external AI tools/agents (e.g. Claude Desktop, or any MCP-compatible client) read and write a Tesbo project's test data using a project-scoped API bearer token instead of a browser session.

**Use cases:**
- A developer wires Claude (or another MCP client) to their Tesbo project so an AI agent can pull the current test-case list, generate new test cases from a spec, or check the requirement/traceability matrix without leaving their coding assistant.
- A CI or automation script uses a `write`-scoped token to record execution results (pass/fail) or file a bug automatically after a check.
- An AI coding agent creates a test plan/cycle for a feature it just implemented and marks off its own manual verification.

**Problem it solves:** Gives AI agents and other machine clients a safe, auditable, protocol-standard way to interact with a specific Tesbo project's data — writes are clearly attributed to a dedicated "tesbo-mcp" actor (distinct from human and other-agent activity in audit history), and a token can never act outside its own project no matter what the client requests.

**Features & actions:**
- **Transport & auth**
  - Single endpoint: `POST /api/projects/:projectId/mcp`, body is JSON-RPC 2.0 (`{jsonrpc:"2.0", id, method, params}`).
  - Requires `Authorization: Bearer <token>` resolved to an API token principal by `AuthMiddleware`; a browser session (cookie-based) is explicitly rejected with `401 MCP requires a valid API token` — MCP is a machine-only surface, never usable from a logged-in browser tab directly.
  - **Project-scope enforcement:** the token's own `projectId` (baked in at token creation) must equal the `:projectId` in the URL, or the call fails with JSON-RPC error code `-32001` (`ProjectScopeDenied`) — even if a caller correctly guesses/knows another project's id, a token literally cannot act outside the project it was minted for. Tested explicitly: token with no project scope at all is also rejected.
  - **Tool-scope enforcement:** each tool declares `requiredScope: "read"` or `"write"`; the token must carry that scope (tokens can hold `read`, `write`, or both) or the call fails with code `-32002` (`ScopeDenied`), naming the missing scope in the error message.
- **Protocol methods** (`tools/list`, `tools/call`, `initialize`, `ping`)
  - `initialize` → returns protocol version `2024-11-05`, server name `tesbo-mcp`, version `0.1.0`, and capabilities (`tools.listChanged: false`, i.e. the tool list is static and won't push change notifications).
  - `ping` → empty result, for client keep-alive/liveness checks.
  - `tools/list` → returns every registered tool's `name`, `description`, and JSON-Schema `inputSchema` (8 tools today — full list below).
  - `tools/call` → dispatches to the named tool with `arguments`; unknown tool name → `MethodNotFound` (-32601); on success wraps the JSON-stringified result as an MCP `content: [{type:"text", text}]` part with `isError:false`; on a handler exception, maps the underlying error (e.g. a `BadRequestException`'s message) onto a `ToolExecutionError` (-32003) rather than leaking a raw 500.
  - Malformed request (missing/wrong `jsonrpc` version, non-string `method`) → `InvalidRequest` (-32600); the request `id` is always echoed back on error responses (including `null` if none was sent), per JSON-RPC spec.
- **The 8 exposed tools** (each is a thin wrapper over an existing `LegacyService` method, so MCP reuses the exact same code paths/validation as the REST API):
  1. `list_projects` (read) — returns the single project the token is scoped to (never a cross-project list, since tokens are project-bound).
  2. `list_testcases` (read) — filters: `suiteId`, `status`, `priority`, `type`, `automationStatus`, `jiraIssueKey`, `search`, `limit` (up to 500), `offset`.
  3. `create_testcase` (write) — required `title`; optional `suiteId`, `description`, `preconditions`, `steps[]`, `testData`, `priority`, `severity`, `type`, `automationStatus`, `component`, `status`. Missing/blank title → tool execution error before hitting the service. Attributed to the `tesbo-mcp` agent actor.
  4. `create_suite` (write) — required `name`; optional `parentId` (nest under another suite), `position`.
  5. `create_cycle_from_plan` (write) — required `name`; optional `planId` (seed from an existing plan), `description`, `environment`, `buildVersion`, `releaseName`.
  6. `record_execution_result` (write) — required `executionId`, `status`; optional `actualResult`, `defectKey`, `defectUrl`. **Extra project-scope check inside the handler itself**: looks up the execution's owning project via `executions → cycle_items → cycles` and rejects with `ProjectScopeDenied` if it belongs to a different project than the token, or `ToolExecutionError` ("Execution not found") if the execution id doesn't exist at all — this closes the gap where an execution *id* alone wouldn't otherwise prove project ownership. Attributed to the `tesbo-mcp` agent actor.
  7. `create_bug` (write) — required `title`; optional `description`, `status`, `externalUrl`, `links[]` (`{testcaseId, cycleId, executionId}`). Attributed to the token's **human owner** (`reported_by` column references `users(id)`, not the agent actor) — i.e. bugs filed via MCP show up as reported by the person who created the token, not by "tesbo-mcp".
  8. `get_requirement_matrix` (read) — full traceability matrix for the project: every test case with its runs, latest execution status, and any linked bugs.
- **Actor attribution model:** only write tools resolve/attach an actor id (reads never touch actor columns); the "tesbo-mcp" agent actor id is looked up once from `actors ⋈ agents` (seeded migration V65) and cached for the life of the process.
- **Edge cases validated by the existing test suite** (`mcp.service.spec.ts`) worth including in a manual QA pass too: non-2.0 payload rejected; unknown method/tool rejected; read tool works with read-only token but write tool is blocked for a read-only token; a client-supplied project id in tool arguments is ignored in favor of the token's own project; underlying service exceptions are mapped to a clean tool error rather than crashing the RPC call.

**Auth prerequisite — Personal Access Token / API token system (shared with direct REST API access, not just MCP):**
  - Tokens live in an `api_tokens` table, always project-scoped (not workspace-wide), created via `POST /api/projects/:id/apikeys` (name + optional `scopes` array, defaults to `["read","write"]` if none/invalid given), listed via `GET /api/projects/:id/apikeys` (returns only a masked `tsbo_…<last6ofhash>` prefix, never the secret again), revoked via `DELETE /api/projects/:id/apikeys/:keyId`.
  - Raw token format: `tsbo_` + 24 random bytes (hex); only a SHA-256 hash is ever stored; the raw value is returned exactly once at creation time and is unrecoverable afterward — losing it means issuing a new token.
  - `last_used_at` is stamped best-effort on every successful authentication (used for both REST bearer-auth and MCP).
  - **Notable gap:** there is no frontend UI anywhere in `Tesbo-Frontend` for creating, listing, or revoking these project API tokens (confirmed via full-tree search — no page/component references `apikeys`). The entire token lifecycle, and therefore the entire MCP onboarding flow, is currently API-only: a developer would need to call `POST /api/projects/:id/apikeys` directly (e.g. via curl/Postman while authenticated with a normal browser session) to obtain a token before an MCP client could ever connect. This should be flagged as a UX/testability gap — QA cannot exercise the "connect an MCP client" journey through the product UI today.

**Key files:**
- Backend (MCP protocol): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.controller.ts` (`POST /api/projects/:projectId/mcp`), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.service.ts` (JSON-RPC engine: `handleRequest`, `dispatch`, `callTool`), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.tools.ts` (the 8-tool registry), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.types.ts` (protocol types, error codes), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.module.ts`
- Backend tests: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/mcp/mcp.service.spec.ts`
- Backend (token issuance, shared with REST bearer auth): `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/api-token.service.ts` (`ApiTokenService` — `issueToken`, `listTokens`, `revokeToken`, `authenticate`), routes in `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.controller.ts` (~lines 216–229: `GET/POST /api/projects/:id/apikeys`, `DELETE /api/projects/:id/apikeys/:keyId`), handlers in `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` (`listApiKeys`, `createApiKey`, `revokeApiKey`, ~lines 308–326), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/auth/auth.middleware.ts` (bearer-token resolution)
- Frontend: none — no page/component manages API tokens or MCP connections today

---

### RAG Pipeline (Internal Infrastructure)

**What it is:** Internal plumbing — not a user-facing page in its own right — that turns a project's Knowledge Base documents/files into searchable vector embeddings, and serves hybrid semantic + keyword retrieval to power Zyra's (Tesbo's AI assistant) free-text chat context. It has no dedicated UI, but its behavior is indirectly observable (embedding status on KB documents) and its prerequisite (a workspace AI key) is configurable by workspace owners.

**What it enables:** When Zyra's chat is asked a free-text question, instead of relying only on a cheap recency-based snapshot of recently-touched KB documents, RAG retrieval finds the KB chunks that are actually semantically relevant to the question (via vector similarity) and blends them with full-text keyword matches, so Zyra's answers can cite the right section of the right document even in a large knowledge base. If nothing is embedded yet, or the project has no usable (OpenAI) AI key allocated, retrieval silently returns nothing and the caller falls back to the existing simpler snapshot — RAG is designed to never be a hard dependency or a new failure mode.

**Pipeline stages:**
1. **Ingestion (producer)** — `RagIngestionService.enqueueEmbedding()` is fired (fire-and-forget) from every KB write path in `legacy.service.ts` that creates/updates a `knowledge_documents` row or a `knowledge_files` row (including after audio/video transcription completes). It flips the source's `embedding_status` to `queued` and enqueues a BullMQ job (queue name `knowledge-embedding`) with a deterministic job id (`{sourceType}-{sourceId}`) so concurrent enqueues for the same document dedupe automatically. Jobs retry up to 3 times with exponential backoff (starting 5s).
   - Self-healing: on backend boot, `RagModule.onModuleInit` calls `resumeInterruptedEmbeddings()`, which re-enqueues anything left in `pending`/`queued`/`processing` (covers a backend crash mid-job, since Redis persistence alone doesn't recover an in-flight job the process died holding).
2. **Chunking** — `RagChunkingService.chunk()` (pure, synchronous, unit-testable, no I/O): splits text on markdown headings first (tracking a heading breadcrumb like "Setup > Prerequisites" per chunk for citation), then recursively splits each section on a separator cascade (blank line → newline → sentence → hard character cut) merging adjacent small pieces up to a ~1600-char target with a 240-char overlap between consecutive chunks (so context isn't lost at a boundary). Chunks under 20 chars are discarded; capped at 500 chunks per source document.
3. **Embedding (consumer/worker)** — `RagEmbeddingProcessor` (a BullMQ `WorkerHost`): loads the source's raw text, resolves the project's AI key allocation (`resolveEmbeddingAllocation`), and skips (marks `unsupported`) if there's no content, no allocation, or the allocated provider isn't OpenAI (Anthropic has no embeddings endpoint, so an Anthropic-only workspace key makes RAG a no-op for that project, not an error). Computes a SHA-256 content hash and skips re-embedding entirely if content is unchanged since the last successful embed. Calls `embedTexts()` (OpenAI `text-embedding-3-small`, 1536 dimensions) in batches of 96 chunks, then atomically replaces that source's rows in `knowledge_document_chunks` (delete-then-insert inside one DB transaction) with `pgvector` embedding columns. Any chunk whose returned vector doesn't match the expected 1536 dimensions is silently dropped rather than stored malformed.
   - Status lifecycle observable on the KB document/file row: `pending → queued → processing → ready`, or `unsupported` (no content / no valid key / provider mismatch) / `failed` (exhausted all 3 retries, tracked via the BullMQ `failed` worker event).
4. **Retrieval** — `RagRetrievalService.retrieveKnowledgeContext(projectId, query)`, called from Zyra's chat handler in parallel with the existing cheap "recency" knowledge snapshot (never adds latency to that path since both run concurrently); its result supersedes the fallback only if non-empty. Never throws — any failure (no allocation, embeddings API error, etc.) is caught and resolves to `[]`.
   - Runs an ANN (approximate nearest neighbor) cosine-similarity search over `knowledge_document_chunks` restricted to the project's partition (top 40 candidates) **and** a Postgres full-text search (`ts_rank`/`plainto_tsquery`) over both `knowledge_documents` and `knowledge_files` (top 20 each) in parallel.
   - Fuses the two rank lists via **Reciprocal Rank Fusion** (RRF, k=60) computed in application code (chunk-level ANN results and document-level FTS results don't reconcile cleanly in SQL).
   - Trims the fused, ranked sources down to at most 8 sources and a 6,000-character total context budget, truncating the last included source's content with a trailing `...` if it would overflow the budget.
   - AI-memory-type KB documents are excluded from both ANN and FTS retrieval unless their `status = 'approved'` — i.e. an unreviewed AI-generated memory note can't leak into Zyra's context via RAG before a human approves it.
5. **AI key allocation (`rag-ai-allocation.ts`)** — shared helper (also reused by `LegacyService.zyraAiAllocation` for Zyra generally): looks up `project_ai_key_allocations ⋈ workspace_ai_keys` for the project, and only returns a usable allocation if the key is `is_active` and its `provider` is (case-insensitively) `"openai"`. `embedTexts()` builds the request with the allocation's configurable auth header/scheme and base URL (defaults to `https://api.openai.com/v1/embeddings`, with normalization to append `/v1/embeddings` or `/embeddings` as needed for custom base URLs), and surfaces the provider's own error message on a non-2xx response.

**What's configurable / observable by a user (indirectly, through the adjacent "AI Providers" workspace settings feature, not through RAG itself):**
- Workspace owners manage one or more workspace-level AI keys (`Settings → AI Providers` tab) — name, provider (OpenAI/Anthropic/custom with configurable base URL + auth header/scheme), the secret key itself (shown masked after creation, e.g. `sk-...abcd`), and a default model — via `POST/GET/DELETE /api/workspace/ai-keys`.
- Owners allocate exactly one workspace AI key per project (a dropdown per project row); RAG (and Zyra generally) is "blocked"/no-op for a project with no allocation or a non-OpenAI allocation. This is the single lever that turns semantic KB retrieval on or off for a given project — worth a QA test matrix: no key allocated / OpenAI key allocated / Anthropic-only key allocated / custom-provider key allocated (should all degrade gracefully rather than error).
- Embedding status per KB document/file (`pending/queued/processing/ready/unsupported/failed`) is stored on the document/file row itself, so if the Knowledge Base UI (documented elsewhere) surfaces that status field, it's a directly observable signal of this pipeline's health for a given document — worth confirming whether that status is actually surfaced anywhere in the KB UI, since it wasn't in this investigation's scope to check the KB frontend.

**Key files:**
- Backend: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-ingestion.service.ts` (producer/enqueue + startup resume), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-chunking.service.ts` (pure text chunker), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-embedding.processor.ts` (BullMQ worker: embed + persist), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-retrieval.service.ts` (hybrid ANN+FTS retrieval with RRF fusion), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag-ai-allocation.ts` (`resolveEmbeddingAllocation`, `embedTexts`, `normalizeEmbeddingsUrl`), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag.constants.ts` (all tunables: chunk sizes, batch size, ANN/FTS candidate counts, RRF k, context budget), `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag.types.ts`, `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/rag/rag.module.ts`
- Integration point in host service: `Tesbo-Backend-Nest/src/legacy/legacy.service.ts` — `enqueueEmbedding()` wrapper (~line 328) called from every KB create/update path (~lines 3253, 3332, 3375, 3526, 3600, 4444, 4816, 6539, 6547); retrieval call inside Zyra chat handling (~line 5336: `this.ragRetrieval.retrieveKnowledgeContext(projectId, message)`, merged with `knowledgeSnapshot()` fallback)
- Adjacent, user-facing configuration surface (separate feature, documented for cross-reference only): `Tesbo-Frontend/components/settings/AiProvidersTab.tsx` (workspace AI key CRUD + per-project allocation UI), `Tesbo-Frontend/lib/api.ts` (`listWorkspaceAiKeys`, `createWorkspaceAiKey`, `deleteWorkspaceAiKey`, `allocateWorkspaceAiKeyToProject`, `WorkspaceAiKey`/`WorkspaceAiProjectAllocation` types), backend route family `/api/workspace/ai-keys` in `legacy.controller.ts`/`legacy.service.ts`

---

---

## Appendix: Known Gaps & Risk Areas (Testing Priorities)

This appendix consolidates the highest-value findings surfaced while researching every module
above, grouped by the kind of risk, so a testing roadmap can prioritize deliberately instead of
treating all ~200 API routes as equally worth covering.

### A. Platform-wide authorization / IDOR gap (highest priority)

The single biggest recurring theme across this entire investigation: the codebase has a correct,
reusable authorization helper — `requireProjectAccess(userId, projectId)` in `legacy.service.ts`
— but it is only wired up on a **minority** of routes (project CRUD, project API keys). It is
**not** called by the service methods backing:

- Test Suites (list/create/update/delete)
- Test Cases (list/get/create/update/delete, bulk update/delete)
- Project Members (list/add/remove) — including the ability to add yourself as `owner` of any
  project by ID, and the unused workspace-level `project-access` endpoints
- Test Plans (list/create/get/update/delete, plan items, plan runs/progress)
- Test Cycles/Runs (list/create/get/update/delete, add/remove test cases)
- Test Executions (update) and Public Share toggling
- Requirements/Traceability endpoints
- Bugs (get/update/delete, links, attachments)
- Knowledge Base v1 legacy endpoints (no project scoping *at all* — an item from Project A is
  fetchable via Project B's URL or with no project context whatsoever)

**Practical consequence:** with any two valid logged-in accounts on different projects/
organizations, one account can very likely `GET`/`PATCH`/`DELETE` almost any resource belonging to
the other, purely by supplying its UUID. This is the single highest-value security regression test
to add — one systematic cross-tenant/cross-project access test per resource type, rather than
trusting the client-side role gating (which is real and well-implemented, but is the *only* line
of defense today for most of these routes).

### B. Features that are non-functional stubs today (deprioritize functional testing, add regression coverage instead)

Writing deep functional test cases against these will waste QA cycles — they have no real
implementation yet. Recommended treatment: one lightweight regression test per item confirming it
*stays* a known no-op (so nobody mistakes a future silent partial-fix for a completed feature),
not a full test suite.

| Feature | Current reality |
|---|---|
| **Bulk Execution Actions** (`bulk-assign`, `bulk-status`) | Controller methods are literally empty (`{}`); no frontend caller, no bulk-select UI on the executions table at all. |
| **Recurring Run Scheduling** (`/cycles/schedules`) | Full DB schema + full frontend CRUD UI exist, but all four backend endpoints are disconnected stubs — a created schedule vanishes from the list instantly; no scheduler/worker exists to execute one even if it persisted. |
| **Notifications** (bell icon) | `GET /api/notifications` hardcodes `[]`; mark-as-read is a no-op; the bell icon has no handler, no badge, no dropdown. |
| **AI Script Review** (`/ai/review-script`) | Hardcoded `{status:"passed", summary:"", categories:[], validatedSteps:[]}` for any input; no frontend caller. |
| **Tesbo Reports** (automated CI test-run ingestion, `/tesbo-reports/*`) | Six GET stubs return empty/static payloads; the frontend has a fully-typed client for ~20 more endpoints (ingestion, alerts, sharing, settings) that **no page or component calls** — the feature is unreachable from the UI in either direction. |
| **`cycles/:cycleId/report/summary`** | Hardcoded all-zero response regardless of the real cycle; superseded by the Execution Report tab. |
| **Knowledge Base v1** (`/knowledge-base/:itemId` legacy flat endpoints) | Superseded by the v2 folders/documents/files model; kept only for rollback safety; no frontend usage. |
| **`POST /onboarding/org-and-project`** | Implemented backend + API client wrapper, but no UI calls it. |
| **`generateAiTestCases()` / AI Generation History browsing** | Backend routes work, but no current screen calls the standalone generator or a history browser — the only path users actually take is via Zyra Tasks. |
| **Project API Keys** (`/projects/:id/apikeys`) — the MCP-token feature | Fully implemented and correctly authorization-gated backend, but **zero frontend UI** exists to create/list/revoke these tokens — the entire "connect an MCP client" journey is API-only today (curl/Postman required). |
| **Workspace `project-access` endpoints** (`PUT`/`DELETE /api/workspace/project-access`) | Dead: no frontend caller, and (per finding A above) not even auth-scoped. |

### C. Concrete, reproducible bugs worth a dedicated test case each

These are not gaps in coverage — they are specific, already-identified defects, each traced to
exact code. Good first candidates for a bug-bash or a "does this still repro" regression pass:

1. **Ticket-link silently dropped when filing a bug.** Picking a Jira/Linear ticket via the search
   picker (both in the Failed-execution dialog and the standalone Bugs page) is displayed on
   screen but never sent in the `createBug`/`updateBug` payload (`integrationIssueKey` is
   hard-coded `null`). File a bug, pick a ticket, save, reopen — the ticket reference is missing.
2. **Fields can never be cleared once set** (bug description, external URL, integration
   provider/key, BetterBugs URL): `updateBug` uses `COALESCE(newValue, oldValue)` with
   `body.field || null`, so an empty string is indistinguishable from "not provided" and the old
   value always survives.
3. **Suite rename silently promotes a child suite to root.** `updateSuite`'s `parentId` is *not*
   `COALESCE`d — it's always overwritten to `body.parentId ?? null`. The rename UI only sends
   `{name}`, so renaming a nested (child) suite unexpectedly moves it to the top level.
4. **`estimatedDuration` is a dead field end-to-end** — present in the DB, the manual test-case
   form, and the import mapping UI, but dropped by both `createTestCase`/`updateTestCase` and the
   import payload. Anything typed there is silently discarded.
5. **Public share links leak more than they display.** The rendered `/share/:token` page only
   shows ID/title/priority/type/status, but the underlying JSON endpoint
   (`/api/public/shared-runs/:token/executions`) returns the full row — actual result text, defect
   key/URL, raw assignee user ID, full steps/preconditions/test data — to any anonymous caller who
   hits it directly.
6. **Removing a test case from a run permanently destroys its execution history** for that run
   (hard delete cascades from `cycle_items` → `executions`, bypassing the soft-delete columns added
   for exactly this purpose), unlike almost every other delete operation in the product.
7. **Bulk "Update status/priority" modal pre-fills Draft/P2 regardless of the actual selection** —
   confirming without changing the defaults silently resets every selected test case to Draft/P2.
8. **AI Insights "health score" and the Overview tab's "AI summary" are fully deterministic**
   (rule-based templates/weighted formulas), not LLM-generated, despite the "AI" badge — worth a
   byte-identical-output regression test to catch the day this assumption changes.
9. **`createOrgAndProject`, dangling AI-key allocations, and duplicate-name key upserts** — creating
   a workspace AI key with a name that already exists silently *replaces* the old key's
   provider/secret rather than erroring; no warning is shown in the UI before this happens.
10. **Onboarding's "invite team" step can self-escalate privilege.** `addWorkspaceMember` (used by
    the onboarding flow, not the real Invitations feature) has no role/permission check and no role
    validation — a request naming the caller's own email with `role: "owner"` updates their own
    membership row.

### D. Suggested prioritization for an initial test pass

1. **Security/IDOR regression suite** (finding A) — highest value, cross-cutting, currently
   entirely unguarded outside the client.
2. **Core workflow smoke tests**: Projects → Suites → Test Cases → Test Plans → Test Runs →
   Executions → Bugs, including the auto-bug-filing-on-Failed flow and the concrete bugs in
   section C above.
3. **Import/export round-trip** (CSV/XLSX) and **bulk operations**, given the concurrency/ID-
   generation and default-value gotchas documented in Module 2.
4. **Reports/Dashboard zero-data and boundary states** — most report tabs have explicit, testable
   empty/edge states (documented per-tab above) that are easy to regress silently.
5. **AI features gated by key allocation** — the "no key / inactive key / wrong provider" states
   recur across AI Test Generation, Zyra Chat, Zyra Tasks, and RAG; one shared test matrix covers
   all of them.
6. **Integrations** (Jira/Linear OAuth + PAT, sync, ticket linking) — focus on the PAT vs OAuth
   auth-path divergence (each has independent code) and the ticket-link-dropped bug above.
7. **Explicitly deprioritize** everything in section B until product decides whether to build,
   finish, or remove them — cover with a single "stays a stub" smoke test each instead.
